Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Invalidation of Mutayammim's Prayer Upon Seeing Water
Commentary on the invalidation of mutayammim's prayer upon seeing water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mutayammim sees water during prayer and identify the condition of ability as the decisive factor.

Core Idea
Mere sight does not break tayammum; only ability to use water invalidates the prayer.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that a mutayammim's prayer becomes invalid if he sees water. The commentator explains that this ruling hinges on the ability to use water, not just the sight. This distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rule in real-life scenarios where a person may see water but cannot reach it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage addresses a mutayammim (one who performed tayammum) in prayer who sees water. The initial ruling from the matn is that his prayer becomes invalid (batalat). The commentator clarifies that invalidation is conditional upon ability to use the water.
Mere sight without ability has no effect.
2
Locate the condition
The key word is 'ability' (qudra). The text states 'with the ability to use water' (بالقدرة على استعمال الماء) and that mere sight without ability is not considered, as evidenced in the chapter of tayammum.
This condition is derivative of the original condition for tayammum: absence of water.
3
Trace the proof (qiyas)
The commentator draws an analogy: absence of water is a condition at the start of tayammum, so it remains a condition during the prayer, like other conditions. If the condition is lost (ability arises), the prayer becomes invalid.
This qiyas connects initiation conditions to continuity conditions.
4
Apply to real scenarios
If a mutayammim sees water but cannot reach it (e.g., across a river), his prayer is valid. If he can reach it, his prayer becomes invalid at that moment.
The ruling applies at the instant of ability, not retroactively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبطلت أن رأى متيمم ماء) أي بطلت صلاته بالقدرة على استعمال الماء، ولا عبرة بالرؤية المجردة عن القدرة بدليل ما قدمه في بابه. وإنما بطلت لأن عدم الماء شرط في الابتداء فكان شرط البقاء كسائر الشروط وكالمكفر بالصوم إذا أيسر ليس له البناء لأنه برؤية الماء ظهر حكم الحدث السابق فكأنه شرع على غير وضوء بخلاف ما إذا سبقه الحدث لأنه شرع بوضوء تام أطلقه فشمل ما إذا رأى المتيمم قبل سبق الحدث أو بعده، وفي الثاني خلاف والصحيح هو البطلان كما في المحيط، وجزم به الشارح. واختار في النهاية أنه دون فساد. وفي فتح القدير : والذي يظهر أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء إذا أوجبت أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئه عنها وضوء واحد، فالأوجه ما في شرح الكنز وهو الموافق لما قدمناه من قول محمد فيمن حلف لا يتوضأ من الرعاف فبال ثم رعف ثم توضأ أنه يحنث . يوجب كما قدمنا النظر فيه في باب الغسل فالأوجه ما في النهاية وهو الحق في اعتقادي لكن كلام النهاية ليس عليه بل على ما نقل عن محمد في باب فلا تتفرع مسألة التيمم على الوجه الذي ذكره على ما هو ظاهر اختياره اهـ. والذي يظهر أن هذا ليس مبنياً على هذا الفرع فإنهم عللوا الاستقبال بأنه لما ظهر الحدث السابق تبين كونه شرع بغير طهارة فليس له البناء سواء قلنا إنها توجب أحداثاً أو حدثاً كما لا يخفى. وذكر الشارح وتقييده بالمتيمم لبطلان الصلاة عند رؤية الماء لا يفيد لأنه لو كان متوضىء يصلي خلف متيمم فرأى المؤتم الماء بطلت صلاته لعلمه أن إمامه قادر على الماء بإخباره، وصلاة الإمام تامة لعدم قدرته، ولو قال وبطلت أن رأى متيمم أو المقتدى به ماء لشمل الكل اهـ. وأقره عليه في فتح القدير وفيه نظر لأن المقتدي بالمتيمم إذا رأى ماء لم يعلم به الإمام فإن صلاة المقتدي لم تبطل أصلاً، وإنما بطل وصفها وهو الفرضية وكلامه في بطلان أصلها برؤية الماء، ولهذا صرح في المحيط بأن المتوضيء خلف المتيمم إذا رأى الماء أو كان على الإمام فائتة لا يذكرها والمؤتم يذكرها أو كان الإمام على غير القبلة وهو لا يعلمه والمؤتم يعلمه فقهقه المؤتم فعليه الوضوء عندهما خلافاً لمحمد وزفر بناء على أن الفرضية متى فسدت لا تنقطع التحريمة عندهما خلافاً لمحمد اهـ. وأيضاً نفي الفائدة مطلقاً ممنوع فإن المترضىء إذا رأى ماء لا يضره فقد أفاد قوله : (أو) تمت مدة مسحه أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان وأجداً للماء أو لم يكن واجداً وهو اختبار بعض المشايخ. وذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أنه لو تمت المدة وهو في الصلاة ولا ماء يمضي على الأصح في صلاته إذ لا فائدة في النزع لأنه للغسل ولا ماء لا يخفى أن المصنف استعمل البطلان بالمعنى الأعم أعني إعدام الفرض فبقي الأصل وإلا فالأولى ما قاله العيني أن مسألة المقتدي بمتيمم ليس فيها إلا خلاف زفر ولا خلاف فيها بين الإمام وصاحبيه يعني وهذه المسائل ليس فيها إلا قول الإمام وصاحبيه .اهـ. وقد يجاب عن الزيلعي بأنه بنى كلامه على مختاره من أنه إذ فسد الاقتداء لفقد شرط كطاهر بمعذور لم تنعقد أصلاً وإن كان لاختلاف الصلاتين تنعقد نفلاً غير مضمون فهنا لما فقد الشرط وهو الوضوء بطلت صلاة المقتدي من أصلها لكن يخالفه ما ذكره المؤلف عن المحيط. وقد يقال ما في المحيط مشكل لأن صلاة الإمام غير جائزة في اعتقاده المقتدي فكيف تنتقض طهارته بقهقهته إلا أن يقال : لا يلزم من فساد اقتدائه عدم بقاء تحريمته فإذا ظهر له عدم صحة صلاة إمامه فسد اقتداؤه فبقي شارعاً في صلاة نفسه بناء على خلاف مختار الزيلعي، لكن المتبادر من عبارة المحيط إن الذي فسد هو وصف الفرضية فقط بقاء الاقتداء متنفلاً فبقي كلامه مشكلاً فليتأمل . قوله : إذا رأى ماء لا يضره فقد أفاد) أنه يفيد الاحتراز عما لو كان متوضئاً ورأى الماء فإنها لا تبطل قوله : فشمل ما إذا كان واجداً للماء أو لم يكن) وشمل ما إذا كان قبل الحدث أو بعده ويجري فيه ما مر . قال في النهر : وصحح الشارح والحدادي أنه يستقبل يعني
His saying: (And it is invalidated if a mutayammim sees water) i.e. his prayer is invalidated by the ability to use water, and mere sight without ability is not considered, as evidenced by what preceded in its chapter. And it is invalidated only because the absence of water is a condition at the initiation, so it is a condition of continuity like other conditions, and like the one who expiates by fasting if he becomes wealthy: he does not have the right to build, because by seeing water the ruling of the previous hadath becomes apparent, as if he began without wudu, contrary to the case of being overtaken by hadath, because he began with complete wudu. He (the author) gave it absolute scope, so it includes when the mutayammim sees water before or after being overtaken by hadath. In the second case there is disagreement, and the correct view is invalidation, as in al-Muhit, and the commentator affirmed it. In al-Nihaya he chose that it is less than corruption (duna fasad). In Fath al-Qadir: It appears that consecutive causes like urine then nosebleed then vomiting, if they necessitate consecutive hadaths, one wudu suffices for them. So the soundest is what is in Sharh al-Kanz, which agrees with what we presented of Muhammad's statement: if someone swears not to perform wudu from a nosebleed, then he urinates, then has a nosebleed, then performs wudu, that he breaks his oath. It necessitates, as we considered earlier in the chapter of ghusl, so the soundest is what is in al-Nihaya, and it is the truth in my belief, but the statement of al-Nihaya is not based on that, but rather on what is transmitted from Muhammad in the chapter. So the issue of tayammum does not branch out on the basis he mentioned, as is apparent from his choice. And it appears that this is not built on this branch, for they reasoned the istiqbal (resuming) by saying: when the previous hadath manifests, it becomes clear that he began without purification, so he does not have the right to build, whether we say it necessitates multiple hadaths or one hadath, as is not hidden. And the commentator's mention and his restriction to the mutayammim for invalidation of prayer upon seeing water is not useful, because if there was a person with wudu praying behind a mutayammim and the follower saw water, his prayer would be invalidated because he knows that his imam is able to use water by his informing, while the imam's prayer is complete due to his inability. And if he said 'And it is invalidated if a mutayammim or the one being followed sees water', it would include everything. And he approved it in Fath al-Qadir, but there is consideration: the one following the mutayammim, if he sees water but the imam does not know, the follower's prayer is not invalidated at all; rather its description (the obligatory nature) is invalidated, and his statement deals with the invalidation of its essence by seeing water. Therefore it was stated clearly in al-Muhit that the one with wudu behind a mutayammim, if he sees water, or if the imam has a missed prayer and does not remember it while the follower remembers, or if the imam is facing a direction other than qibla and does not know while the follower knows, and the follower laughs, then he must perform wudu according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] contrary to Muhammad and Zafar, based on the view that when the obligatory nature is corrupted, the tahrima is not cut off according to them, contrary to Muhammad. End. Also, the absolute denial of benefit is objectionable, because the one with hadath, if he sees water, it does not harm him. So his saying 'or the duration of his wiping ends' benefits by excluding the case where he is able to use water. He gave it absolute scope, so it includes whether he is able to use water or not. And Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that if the duration ends while he is in prayer and there is no water, he continues on the soundest view, because there is no benefit in removing (the khuffs) since it is for ghusl and there is no water. It is not hidden that the author used 'invalid' in the broader sense, i.e. the negation of the obligatory nature, so the essence remains. Otherwise, what al-Ayni said is better: the issue of the follower of a mutayammim has no disagreement except from Zafar, and there is no disagreement between the Imam and his two companions. That is, these issues have only the statement of the Imam and his two companions. End. And one may respond to al-Zayla'i that he built his statement on his chosen view that when the following becomes corrupt due to the loss of a condition, like a pure person following one with an excuse, it does not become valid at all; although if it is due to difference of prayers, it becomes valid as a non-binding supererogatory prayer. Here, since the condition (wudu) is lost, the follower's prayer is invalidated from its origin. But what the author mentioned from al-Muhit contradicts this. And it may be said that what is in al-Muhit is problematic: the imam's prayer is not valid in the follower's belief, so how is his purity vitiated by his laughter? Unless it is said: corruption of his following does not necessitate the non-existence of his tahrima; thus when it becomes apparent that his imam's prayer is not valid, his following becomes corrupt, and he remains engaged in his own prayer based on the view contrary to the chosen view of al-Zayla'i. But what is apparent from the wording of al-Muhit is that only the description of obligatory nature is corrupted, while the following remains as a supererogatory prayer. So his statement remains problematic. Let it be pondered. His saying: 'if he sees water it does not harm him' benefits by excluding the case where he has wudu and sees water, for then it is not invalidated. His saying: 'so it includes whether he is able to use water or not' includes whether it is before hadath or after, and what preceded applies to it. Al-Nahr said: The commentator and al-Haddadi clarified that he must resume (prayer from the beginning); meaning.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'And it is invalidated if a mutayammim sees water.' The commentator explains that invalidation occurs by the ability to use water, not by mere sight. He draws an analogy: the absence of water is a condition for starting tayammum, so it remains a condition for continuity. If a mutayammim sees water during prayer, his prayer becomes invalid because the condition is lost. However, if he sees water but cannot reach it, the prayer remains valid. The text then explores different scenarios: comparing to the case of a person who loses the ability to fast and then becomes able again, and the issue of consecutive hadaths. There is a discussion on whether the prayer of a follower behind a mutayammim is invalidated if the follower sees water. The commentator quotes various scholars like al-Zayla'i, al-Kashgari, and Qadikhan, and notes differences between Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, Muhammad, and Zafar. The final part addresses the problem of a follower laughing when he knows the imam's prayer is invalid, and whether his wudu breaks. The passage ends with an opinion that the correct view is that the follower must resume prayer from the beginning.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who performs tayammum (dry ablution) due to lack of water or inability to use it.
قدرة (qudra (ability)): The capacity to use water, either by finding it or being able to reach it.
بناء (bina' (building upon)): Continuing a prayer from where it was interrupted, rather than starting anew.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly describes the ruling on a mutayammim who sees water during prayer?
A) His prayer becomes invalid immediately upon sight.
B) His prayer becomes invalid only if he can use the water.
C) His prayer remains valid even if he can use the water.
D) He must stop and perform wudu immediately without invalidating the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The key takeaway is that the mutayammim's prayer is valid only as long as he cannot use water; ability to use water at any point invalidates the prayer.

Unlettered Person Learning a Surah Behind an Imam
Explains the ruling when an unlettered person learns a surah during prayer, focusing on the difference of opinion behind a reciter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the corrected Hanafi view holds that an unlettered person's prayer remains valid despite learning a surah behind an imam, and evaluate the opposing argument.

Core Idea
The imam's recitation counts as the follower's, so the prayer remains complete even if the follower learns the surah during prayer.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: an unlettered person (ummi) who cannot read or write is praying behind a reciter (imam). During prayer, he involuntarily hears and memorizes a surah, effectively learning it. Does this invalidate his prayer? The classical Hanafi masters disagreed, and later authorities settled on a ruling that preserves the prayer's validity. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the ummi learning behind a reciter
Identify the ruling adopted by the text: the prayer does not invalidate. Note the authority: al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya and Abu al-Layth.
The phrase 'wa bihi na'khudh' indicates the adopted view.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Most mashayikh argued that the prayer invalidates. Their reasoning: actual recitation (performing the recitation oneself) is superior to legal recitation (being credited with the imam's recitation). The follower's learning is based on imitation, which cannot replace actual recitation.
This is a strong objection based on the concept of ḥaqīqah versus ḥukman.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
The text's response: the imam's recitation is legally considered the follower's recitation. Thus, the follower's prayer has a complete beginning and end. Building on a complete act is permissible.
The key is the principle of legal attribution (al-qirā'atu qirā'atun lahū).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the follower learns a surah, his prayer is valid according to the adopted view. He does not need to repeat the prayer. According to the opposing view, the prayer would be invalid and must be repeated.
This affects the obligation to repeat the prayer (iʿāda).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو) تعلم أمي سورة) وهو منسوب إلى أمة العرب وهي الأمة الخالية عن العلم والكتابة والقراءة فاستعير لمن لا يعرف الكتابة والقراءة. والمراد بالتعلم تذكره إياها بعد النسيان لأن التعلم لا بد له من التعليم وذلك فعل ينافي الصلاة فتتم صلاته اتفاقاً . وقيل . سمعه بلا اختيار وحفظه بلا صنع بأن سمع سورة الاخلاص مثلاً من قارىء فحفظها من غير احتياج إلى التلبس بما يفسد الصلاة من عمل كثير . كذا قالوا . وقوله اتفاقاً لأن عند أبي حنيفة الآية تكفي وهما وإن قالا بافتراض ثلاث آيات لم يشترطا «سورة» وقع ، السورة. وأطلق فشمل كل مصل وفيما إذا كان يصلي خلف قارئ اختلاف المشايخ، فعامتهم على أنها تفسد لأن الصلاة بالقراءة حقيقة فوق الصلاة بالقراءة حكماً فلا يمكنه البناء عليها . وقيل : لا تبطل وصححه في الفتاوى الظهيرية قال : الأمي إذا تعلم سورة خلف القارىء فإنه يمضي على صلاته وهو الصحيح .اهـ. ووجهه أن قراءة الإمام قراءة له فقد تكامل أول الصلاة وآخرها وبناء الكامل جائز. قال أبو الليث : لا تبطل صلاته اتفاقاً وبه : نأخذ .
His statement: 'Or an unlettered person learns a surah.' It is attributed to Umm al-Arab, meaning the nation devoid of knowledge, writing, and reading. It is metaphorically used for one who does not know writing and reading. By 'learning' is meant his recalling it after forgetting, because learning requires teaching, and that is an act contrary to prayer, so his prayer is complete by agreement. And it is said: He heard it involuntarily and memorized it without effort, such as hearing Surah al-Ikhlas from a reciter and memorizing it without needing to engage in much action that would invalidate prayer. So they said. And his statement 'by agreement' because according to Abu Hanifa one verse is sufficient, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) – although they say three verses are obligatory – did not stipulate a surah. He made it absolute, including every worshipper. And regarding when he is praying behind a reciter, there is difference among the mashayikh: most say it invalidates because the prayer with actual recitation is superior to the prayer with legal recitation, so he cannot build upon it. And it is said: it does not invalidate, and it is corrected in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: 'The unlettered person, if he learns a surah behind a reciter, he continues on his prayer, and that is correct.' The reason is that the recitation of the imam is recitation for him, so the beginning and end of the prayer are complete, and building on the complete is permissible. Abu al-Layth said: 'His prayer does not invalidate by agreement, and we adopt this.'
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when an unlettered person (who cannot read or write) learns a surah during prayer. The term 'ummi' is metaphorical for someone lacking knowledge of writing. The text clarifies that 'learning' here means recalling a previously forgotten surah, as active learning would involve teaching and break the prayer. If he simply hears and memorizes without effort, the prayer is complete by agreement. The agreement is based on Abu Hanifa's view that one verse suffices, while the Sahibayn require three verses but do not demand a full surah. The main dispute is when the ummi is praying behind a reciter and learns a surah from him. Most scholars say the prayer is invalidated because the follower's recitation is mere imitation, not actual, so the prayer's completion is compromised. However, al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya and Abu al-Layth hold it does not invalidate, and the text adopts this view: the imam's recitation counts as the follower's recitation, so the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
أمي (ummi): One who cannot read or write; metaphorically from 'umm' (mother) indicating natural state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected view in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, what is the ruling if an unlettered person learns a surah behind a reciter during prayer?
A) The prayer is invalidated.
B) The prayer continues and is valid.
C) The prayer becomes nafl.
D) The person must break the prayer and start over.

Key Takeaway
The corrected Hanafi view: an unlettered person's prayer remains valid if he learns a surah behind an imam, because the imam's recitation legally fulfills his obligation.

Conditions for a Garment Found by a Naked Person in Prayer
Ruling on garment conditions for a naked person in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a garment found by a naked person during prayer to be permissible for covering, and apply them to a scenario.

Core Idea
A garment found in prayer is valid if it is pure, or if impurity can be removed, or if at least a quarter is pure and covers the private parts.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh: what should a person do if they are praying naked (due to lack of clothing) and then find a garment? The text clarifies that not every garment is acceptable; certain conditions regarding purity and coverage must be met. By understanding these conditions, you will know the obligation to cover and continue the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person is praying naked (covering private parts is fard). They find a garment. Determine the ruling on covering with that garment.
2
Check the garment's purity
If the garment has no impurity (najasa) preventing prayer, it is valid. If it has impurity, check if you have means to remove it (e.g., water). If yes, wash and cover.
Impurity here means ritual impurity that prevents validity of prayer.
3
Assess pure area and coverage
If impurity cannot be removed, at least a quarter of the garment must be pure, and the garment must cover the private parts. If both hold, covering is wajib.
The quarter requirement is specific to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو وجد عار ثوبا أي ثوباً تجوز فيه الصلاة بأن لم تكن فيه نجاسة مانعة من الصلاة، أو كانت فيه وعنده ما يزيل به النجاسة، أو لم يكن عنده ما يزيل به النجاسة ولكن ربعه أو أكثر منه طاهر وهو ساتر للعورة
His statement: 'Or a naked person finds a garment' – meaning a garment in which prayer is permissible: that it does not have a impurity preventing prayer, or if it has impurity but he has something to remove it with, or he does not have something to remove it with but a quarter or more of the garment is pure and it covers the private parts.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the condition for a naked person who finds a garment during prayer. The garment must meet three conditions: (1) no ritual impurity impeding prayer, (2) if it has impurity, the person must have a means to remove it, or (3) if he cannot remove the impurity, at least a quarter or more of the garment must be pure and sufficient to cover the private parts. The implication is that he should cover himself and continue the prayer. The text does not discuss what happens if the garment does not meet these conditions.

Key Terms
عار (aar): A naked person, one without clothing covering the private parts.
ثوب (thawb): A garment acceptable for prayer; must be free of najasa or have removable najasa or have sufficient pure area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for a garment found by a naked person during prayer to be valid for covering?
A) The entire garment must be pure.
B) At least half of the garment must be pure.
C) At least a quarter of the garment must be pure and it must cover the private parts.
D) The garment must be new and free of all impurities.

Key Takeaway
A garment found during naked prayer is permissible if it is pure, or if impurity can be removed, or if at least a quarter is pure and covers the private parts; covering becomes wajib.

Recalling a Missed Prayer During Prayer
Explains ruling when one recalls a missed prayer during current prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on recalling a missed prayer during prayer and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Recalling a missed prayer turns the current prayer into nafl; the foundation remains intact.

When a person remembers a missed obligatory prayer while performing another, what happens to the current prayer? Does it become invalid, or does it continue? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, focusing on the key distinction between the prayer's foundation (asl) and its description of obligation (wasf al-fardiyya). Understanding this ruling is essential for maintaining correct prayer order (tartib).

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position
The current prayer is not invalidated when a missed prayer is recalled. The obligation (fardiyya) is lost, but the foundation remains.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says the prayer remains suspended until the person prays five prayers to resolve its status. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it becomes nafl immediately. One narration from Muhammad says it invalidates.
The text says 'khilafan li Muhammad' — meaning contrary to Muhammad's view that it invalidates.
3
Analyze the key distinction: wasf vs asl
The passage states that 'invalidation of the description does not necessitate invalidation of the foundation' (būțlān al-wașf lā yūjibu būțlān al-așl). This is the core argument.
This principle is also used in other fiqh areas.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn: the prayer becomes nafl. Practically, the person completes the current prayer as a nafl and later makes up the missed prayer in order.
5
Note the analogy to tayammum
The text al-Siraj al-Wahhaj likens this case to the tayammum performer who sees water after his hadath occurred; both involve a similar principle of foundation vs. description.
This analogy reinforces the Hanafi reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو) تذكر فائتة) أي عليه أو على إمامه ولم يسقط الترتيب بعد، وقد قدمنا أن المأموم إذا تذكر فائتة على إمامه ولم يتذكرها الإمام فسد وصف الفرضية لا أصلها، وكذا إذا تذكر فائتة عليه فإن أصل الصلاة لم يبطل وإنما انقلبت نفلاً لما عرف أن بطلان الوصف لا يوجب بطلان الأصل عندهما خلافاً لمحمد. في السراج الوهاج : ثم هذه الصلاة لا تبطل قطعاً عند أبي حنيفة بل تبقى موقوفة إن صلى بعدها خمس وهن موافق لما سبق عن المحيط في المتيمم إذا رأى الماء بعد ما سبقه الحدث.
His statement: 'Or he recalls a missed prayer' – meaning on himself or on his imam, and order has not been waived. And we have preceded that the follower, if he recalls a missed prayer on his imam and the imam does not recall it, then the description of obligatory nature (fardiyya) is invalidated, not its foundation. Similarly, if he recalls a missed prayer on himself, then the foundation of the prayer is not invalidated; rather it is turned into nafl, because it is known that invalidation of the description does not necessitate invalidation of the foundation according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani). In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Then this prayer definitely does not invalidate according to Abu Hanifa; rather it remains suspended. If he prays five after it, they are consistent with what preceded from al-Muhit regarding the tayammum performer when he sees water after the hadath preceded him.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute about recalling a missed prayer during the current prayer. The text states that if a follower recalls a missed prayer that his imam owes, and the imam does not remember it, the obligatory nature (fardiyya) of the current prayer is invalidated, but the prayer itself (foundation) remains valid. Similarly, if the person recalls his own missed prayer, the current prayer is not invalidated but becomes nafl. This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), but according to Imam Muhammad (in one narration), the prayer becomes invalid. The text cites al-Siraj al-Wahhaj stating that according to Abu Hanifa, the prayer definitely does not invalidate but remains suspended; if he later prays five (substitute prayers), they are compatible with the ruling on tayammum.

Key Terms
فائتة (fai'ta): A missed obligatory prayer that must be made up.
وصف الفرضية (wasf al-fardiyya): The legal description of obligatory nature of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, what happens to a person's current prayer if he recalls a missed prayer (fai'ta) during it?
A) The prayer is invalidated completely.
B) The prayer becomes a nafl prayer.
C) The prayer remains fard but must be repeated later.
D) The prayer is suspended until the missed prayer is made up.

Key Takeaway
Recalling a missed prayer during the current prayer invalidates only the description of fardiyya, not the prayer itself; the prayer becomes nafl.

Removing Khuffs with Light Action: Ruling and Proof
States ruling on removing khuffs with light action during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on removing khuffs during prayer with slight action and identify the consensus (ijma) as its proof.

Core Idea
Removing loose khuffs with slight action does not break prayer; heavy action invalidates by consensus.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a key detail in the rules of prayer: the removal of khuffs (leather socks) while praying. The commentary clarifies that 'slight action' (amal yasir) is permissible and does not invalidate the prayer, whereas heavy action would. The proof is the consensus of scholars that heavy action exits one from prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is removing khuffs during prayer. The condition is that removal must be with slight action (amal yasir), meaning the khuffs are loose and require no effort.
2
Apply the ruling
If the removal meets the condition, the prayer remains valid. If heavy action is required, the prayer is invalid.
Heavy action means any movement that takes the person out of the state of prayer.
3
Locate the dalil
The word 'ittifāqan' (by consensus) indicates that scholars agree heavy action invalidates prayer; by implication, light action does not.
Ijma is a primary source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies equally to one or two khuffs; the dual form is coincidental.
The same ruling holds for a single khuff as established in the chapter on khuffs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو نزع خفيه بعمل يسير بأن كانا واسعين لا يحتاج فيهما إلى المعالجة في النزع. قيد به لأن العمل الكثير يخرج به عن الصلاة فتتم صلاته حينئذ اتفاقاً، والظاهر أن ذكر الخف بلفظ المثنى اتفاقي لأن الحكم كذلك في الخف الواحد لما قدمه في بابه من أن نزع الخف ناقض للمسح ولذا أفرده في المجمع .
His saying: (or removed his two khuffs with slight action) meaning they were loose such that no effort is needed in removing them. He restricted it because heavy action exits one from prayer, so his prayer is complete then by consensus. It is apparent that mentioning khuff in the dual is coincidental because the ruling is the same for a single khuff, as he previously mentioned in its chapter that removing the khuff nullifies the wipe, therefore he mentioned it singly in al-Majma.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This is an expansion of the matn ruling on removing khuffs during prayer. The author, al-Marghinani, explains that the condition 'with slight action' is crucial. If the khuffs are loose and can be removed without significant movement, the prayer remains valid. If heavy action is required, the prayer is invalidated by consensus. The dual form 'khuffayn' is not restrictive; the same applies to a single khuff, as previously established in the chapter on khuffs.

Key Terms
عمل يسير (amal yasir): Slight action that does not involve significant movement; here, removing loose khuffs without effort.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for removing khuffs without invalidating prayer?
A) The khuffs must be new
B) The removal must be with slight action
C) The prayer must be a sunnah prayer
D) The imam must consent

Key Takeaway
Removing khuffs with slight action does not invalidate prayer; the proof is scholarly consensus.

Ruling on a Naked Person Finding Clothing During Prayer
States ruling on a naked person finding clothing during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a naked person's prayer remains valid upon finding clothing.

Core Idea
Finding clothing during prayer does not invalidate it if the garment is pure or can be purified and covers the 'awrah.

In the Hanafi school, a person who has no clothing may pray naked. But what happens if they find clothing while praying? Does the prayer become invalid? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the prayer continues valid subject to specific conditions regarding the purity and coverage of the found garment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person begins prayer naked due to lack of clothing, then finds a garment during the prayer.
2
Recognize the default ruling
The prayer remains valid if the found garment meets certain conditions; it does not automatically become invalid.
3
List the conditions for the garment
The garment must be such that prayer is permissible in it: either (a) no ritual impurity that prevents prayer, or (b) impurity present but the person has means to remove it (e.g., water), or (c) impurity present, no means, but at least a quarter of the garment is pure and it covers the 'awrah.
4
Apply the conditions
Analyse each scenario: if (a) or (b) or (c) holds, the prayer continues valid; otherwise, the garment should not be used and the prayer remains as before (naked).
5
Conclude the ruling
Under the specified conditions, the prayer is valid and the person can wear the found garment and continue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو وجد عار ثوبا أي ثوباً تجوز فيه الصلاة بأن لم تكن فيه نجاسة مانعة من الصلاة، أو كانت فيه وعنده ما يزيل به النجاسة، أو لم يكن عنده ما يزيل به النجاسة ولكن ربعه أو أكثر منه طاهر وهو ساتر للعورة
His saying: (or a naked person found clothing) meaning clothing in which prayer is permissible, either because there is no ritual impurity preventing prayer, or there is impurity but he has what can remove it, or he does not have what can remove it but a quarter or more of it is pure and it covers the 'awrah.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement regarding a person who begins prayer naked due to lack of clothing and then finds clothing during the prayer. The prayer remains valid if the found clothing meets conditions: it is pure (or can be made pure) and covers the 'awrah. The author specifies that if the clothing has impurity but the person has means to remove it (e.g., water), or if a quarter or more is pure and covers the 'awrah, the prayer continues.

Key Terms
عار (ari): A person who is naked and does not have clothing to cover during prayer.
نجاسة (najasa): Ritual impurity that prevents the validity of prayer if present on the body or clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a naked person finds clothing with impurity but has water to remove it?
A) Prayer is invalid because the clothing is impure
B) Prayer remains valid because he can purify it
C) He must start prayer over after purifying
D) He must finish prayer naked

Key Takeaway
A naked person's prayer remains valid when finding clothing if the garment is pure, or can be purified, or if a quarter and more is pure and covers the 'awrah.

When Inability Becomes Ability Mid-Prayer: Ruling on Ruku' and Sujud
Ruling statement with ta'lil on regaining ability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person who cannot perform ruku' and sujud during prayer later becomes able, and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind the invalidation.

Core Idea
A prayer begun without essential pillars cannot be salvaged if ability returns; the strong cannot rest on the weak.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a person begins prayer unable to bow or prostrate (e.g., due to illness or restriction), then regains the ability during the prayer. How does the Hanafi school rule? The answer lies in the principle that later acts must be built on sound foundations. Let's analyze the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Who is involved and what changes mid-prayer? The text refers to someone who 'becomes able' (قدر) to perform ruku' and sujud after being unable.
2
State the ruling
The prayer is invalid (batil). This is the explicit hukm in the text.
The ruling is unconditional: the entire prayer must be restarted.
3
Extract the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text says: 'because the latter part of his prayer is stronger, so it is not permissible to build the strong upon the weak.' Understand this logical link.
The 'weak' refers to the initial portion that lacked pillars; the 'strong' is the latter part with full ability.
4
Apply the underlying principle
The principle is general: any act that begins with a deficiency in an essential pillar cannot be rectified later by fulfilling that pillar. The entire act must be sound from start.
This applies to any situation where a fundamental condition or pillar is initially missing.
5
Distinguish from other scenarios
Compare with cases where a substitute is valid (e.g., tayammum) or where the missing element is not a pillar (e.g., a sunnah). The ruling changes accordingly.
The key is whether the deficiency affects a pillar (rukn) or merely an obligatory (wajib) or recommended act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو قدر (موم أي على الركوع والسجود لأن آخر صلاته أقوى فلا يجوز بناؤه على الضعيف
His saying: (or became able to [بمعنى: قدر على]) i.e., able to bow and prostrate because the latter part of his prayer is stronger, so it is not permissible to build the strong upon the weak.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement about a person who begins prayer unable to perform ruku' and sujud (e.g., due to illness or restriction) and then during prayer becomes able. The prayer is invalidated because the latter part of the prayer (when ability returns) is stronger than the earlier part performed without the pillars, and you cannot base a stronger act on a weaker foundation. Hence, the prayer must be restarted.

Key Terms
موم (mum): Unclear; likely a scribal error for 'على' meaning ability to perform ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ta'lil (reason) given in the text for the invalidity of prayer when a person becomes able to bow and prostrate mid-prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid because intention was not renewed.
B) The later part is stronger and cannot be built on the weaker initial part.
C) The prayer is valid if the missed actions are repeated.
D) The prayer becomes void because of change in intention.

Key Takeaway
If ability to perform the essential pillars of ruku' and sujud returns during prayer, the entire prayer is invalid and must be restarted, as the strong cannot stand on a weak foundation.

Appointing an Ummi as Imam: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute over appointing an ummi as imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on appointing an ummi as imam and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the appointment.

Core Idea
Appointing an ummi invalidates prayer if done before tashahhud; after tashahhud it is valid.

When an imam loses wudu mid-prayer, he may appoint a substitute. But what if the substitute is an ummi (one who cannot recite properly)? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The imam experiences hadath during prayer and appoints an ummi to lead. What is the ruling on the congregation's prayer?
2
State the Hidayah view
Al-Hidayah holds that the prayer becomes corrupt (fāsid) because the ummi is unfit to lead reciters. The unfitness is a legal impediment.
3
State Fakhr al-Islam's refinement
Fakhr al-Islam argues that if the appointment occurs after tashahhud, it does not corrupt the prayer, citing consensus. The action of appointing an ummi before tashahhud is contrary (munāfī) to prayer, but after tashahhud it is not.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The later authorities (al-Kāfī, Ghāyat al-Bayān) follow Fakhr al-Islam: no corruption after tashahhud. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو استخلف أمياً) يعني عند سبق الحديث على ما اختاره في الهداية لأن فساد الصلاة بحكم شرعي وهو عدم صلاحيته للإمامة في حق القارىء لا بالاستخلاف لأنه غير مفسد حتى جاز استخلافه القارىء واختار فخر الإسلام أنه لا فساد بالاستخلاف بعد التشهد بالإجماع، وصححه في الكافي وغاية البيان، لأن استخلاف الأمي فعل مناف للصلاة فيكون مخرجاً منها، وكونه ليس بمناف لها إنما هو في مطلق الاستخلاف، وأما الاستخلاف المقيد وهو استخلاف الأمي فهو مناف لها
His saying: (or appointed an ummi as substitute) meaning when hadath preceded, according to what was chosen in al-Hidayah, because the corruption of the prayer is by a legal ruling—his unfitness for imamate regarding the reciter—not by the act of appointment itself, for it is not corruptive as even a reciter may appoint him. Fakhr al-Islam chose that there is no corruption by appointment after tashahhud by consensus, and he corrected it in al-Kafi and Ghayat al-Bayan, because appointing an ummi is an action contrary to prayer, thus it exits one from prayer. That it is not contrary is only in absolute appointment; as for restricted appointment—i.e., appointing an ummi—it is contrary.
Source pages p. 656

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when an imam experiences hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer and appoints an ummi as his substitute. There is a dispute: according to al-Hidayah, the prayer becomes invalid due to the ummi's unfitness for imamate over reciters. However, Fakhr al-Islam holds that if the appointment occurs after tashahhud, it does not invalidate by consensus. The reasoning is that appointing an ummi is an act contrary to prayer (munāfī), thus it exits one from prayer, whereas appointing a qualified person is not contrary. The preferred view according to al-Kafi and Ghayat al-Bayan is that there is no corruption after tashahhud.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlāf): Appointing a substitute imam during prayer when the original imam becomes unable to continue.
أمي (ummī): One who cannot recite al-Fātiha correctly or recite from the Quran.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting after the second rak‘ah and at the end of the prayer.
مناف للصلاة (munāfī li aṣ-ṣalāh): An action that contradicts the nature of prayer and thus invalidates it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Kafi, when does appointing an ummi as imam not corrupt the prayer?
A) If the ummi is a relative
B) If the appointment occurs after tashahhud
C) If the congregation is all ummi
D) If the prayer is nafl

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, appointing an ummi as imam after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer, but doing so before tashahhud does.

Sunrise During Fajr and 'Asr Time During Jumu'ah: Invalidation and Disputes
Discusses invalidation of prayer by sunrise and 'Asr entry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that both sunrise and entry of 'Asr time invalidate prayer without action, and explain the proofs and the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the definition of 'Asr entry.

Core Idea
The ruling is based on the hadith of prohibited times; the dispute over 'Asr entry stems from differing criteria for the beginning of 'Asr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two scenarios where prayer becomes invalid without any action from the worshiper: sunrise during Fajr and the entry of 'Asr time during Jumu'ah. It first presents the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i school on sunrise, then discusses an internal Hanafi difference regarding when 'Asr time actually begins, which affects the invalidation of Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios and the Common Ruling
The passage states that sunrise during Fajr and the entry of 'Asr time during Jumu'ah both invalidate (tufsid) the prayer, and this invalidation occurs without the worshiper's action (min ghayri san'ihi). Recognize that this is a ruling of batil (invalid).
The ruling applies specifically when the event occurs during the prayer, not before.
2
Analyze the Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Sunrise
The Shafi'i school argues that the prayer is valid until sunrise, citing the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught it.' The Hanafi school responds with the hadith prohibiting prayer at sunrise, which implies invalidation. The Hanafis reconcile by saying the Shafi'i hadith applies before the prohibition was revealed.
The Hanafi proof uses istidlal (inference) from the prohibition.
3
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Asr Entry
The passage notes a difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on when 'Asr time begins. Abu Hanifa holds that 'Asr enters when the shadow of an object becomes twice its length, while the Sahibayn say when it becomes equal to the object's height. This difference affects when Jumu'ah becomes invalid.
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's view of an interval between Zuhr and 'Asr is also mentioned.
4
Consider the Solution from Later Hanafi Scholars
The passage refers to al-Mi'raj and al-Mustasfa, suggesting that the dispute is resolved by distinguishing the two positions: according to the Sahibayn, invalidation occurs when the shadow is equal; according to Abu Hanifa, when it is twice.
This shows how later scholars harmonized the differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو طلعت الشمي في الفجر أو دخل وقت العصر في (الجمعة) لأنها مفسدة للصلاة من غير صنعه، ومذهب الشافعي وغيره فسادها بطلوعها تمسكاً بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من أدرك ركعة من الصبح قبل أن تطلع الشمس فقد أدركها» (۱) ولنا حديث عقبة بن عامر الجهني المتقدم من النهي عنها في الأوقات الثلاثة فإنه يفيد بطريق الاستدلال الفساد بطلوع الشمس، وإذا تعارضا قدم النهي فيجب حمل ما رووا على ما قبل النهي عن الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة. فإن قيل : كيف يتحقق الخلاف في البطلان بدخول وقت العصر في الجمعة فإن الدخول عنده إذا صار ضل كل شيء مثليه، وعندهما إذا صار مثله؟ قلنا : هذا على قول الحسن بن زياد فإن عنده وقتاً مهملاً بين خروج الظهر ودخول العصر، فإذا صار الظل مثله يتحقق الخروج عندهما والصلاة تامة وعنده باطلة. كذا في الكافي وفيه نظر، لأنهم قالوا : أو دخل وقت العصر ولم يقولوا أو خرج وقت الظهر. وقيل: يمكن أن يقعد في الصلاة بعدما قعد قدر التشهد مقدار ما صار الظل مثليه فحينئذ يتحقق الخلاف . كذا في المعراج والظاهر في الجواب ما نقله في المعراج عن المستصفى بعد هذا الكلام من أن هذا على اختلاف القولين فعندهما إذا صار الظل مثله ، وعنده إذا صار مثليه .
His saying: (or the sun rose during Fajr or the time of 'Asr entered during Jumu'ah) because it corrupts the prayer without any action of his. The school of al-Shafi'i and others hold that it becomes corrupt by sunrise, adhering to his saying ﷺ: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught it.' Our proof is the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir al-Juhani that prohibits prayer in the three times, which by way of inference indicates corruption by sunrise. When they conflict, the prohibition is given precedence, so we must interpret their narration as applying before the prohibition of prayer in the disliked times. If it is said: How is the dispute realized regarding invalidation by entering 'Asr time in Jumu'ah? For entering according to him (Abu Hanifa) is when the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is when it becomes equal? We say: This is according to the saying of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, who holds that there is an interval between the exit of Zuhr and entry of 'Asr. So when the shadow is equal, exit occurs according to them and the prayer is complete, but according to him it is invalid. Thus in al-Kafi, and it has some consideration, because they said 'or entered 'Asr time' and did not say 'or exited Zuhr time.' It was said: It is possible that he sat in prayer after sitting for tashahhud long enough for the shadow to become twice its length; then the dispute is realized. Thus in al-Mi'raj. The apparent answer is what al-Mi'raj narrated from al-Mustasfa after this discussion: that this is according to the two sayings; according to them when the shadow is equal, and according to him when it is twice.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage deals with two cases: sunrise during Fajr prayer and entering of 'Asr time during Jumu'ah prayer. Both invalidate the prayer without any action from the worshiper. The author presents the Hanafi position against al-Shafi'i. The Shafi'i school cites the hadith of catching a rak'ah before sunrise as evidence that the prayer is valid until sunrise. The Hanafi response uses the hadith prohibiting prayer at sunrise, which implies invalidation. They reconcile by saying the Shafi'i hadith applies before the prohibition. The second part discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on when exactly 'Asr time begins, which affects the invalidation of Jumu'ah. Abu Hanifa uses the 'shadow twice' criterion, while the Sahibayn use 'shadow equal', leading to different conclusions on when the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس (ṭulūʿ al-shams): Sunrise; a time when prayer is prohibited and thus invalidates ongoing prayer.
مفسدة (mufsidah): That which corrupts or invalidates; here, the sunrise or 'Asr entry acts as an invalidator (mufsid) without the worshiper's action.
الوقت المكروه (al-waqt al-makrūh): The disliked time for prayer; includes sunrise, when prayer is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) and thus invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the proof that sunrise invalidates the Fajr prayer?
A) The hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught it.'
B) The hadith prohibiting prayer at sunrise.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Qiyas on the invalidating effect of menstruation.

Key Takeaway
Sunrise during Fajr and entry of 'Asr time during Jumu'ah invalidate the prayer without any action from the worshiper, based on the hadith of prohibited times.

Plaster Falling Off After Healing and Cessation of Excuse
Defines ruling on plaster falling off after healing and end of excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a plaster falling off invalidates previous prayer and apply the same temporal condition to the cessation of an excuse.

Core Idea
A plaster falling off due to healing invalidates prayer; otherwise it is valid. The same logic applies to end of excuses: only continuous cessation for a full time confirms invalidation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defines the ruling when a plaster used for concessions falls off, or when an excused person's condition ends. The key is distinguishing complete healing from mere falling off or temporary cessation. The text also clarifies that for excuses, the cessation must be permanent for a full prayer time to trigger qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text covers two cases: a plaster falling off a broken limb and the end of an excuse (e.g., chronic bleeding). Both involve the end of a necessity that allowed concessions in prayer.
2
Determine the condition for invalidation
For the plaster, the condition is that it falls off due to healing ('an bar'). If it falls off without healing, prayer remains valid by consensus.
The consensus is mentioned as proof.
3
Apply the temporal rule for excuses
For an excuse, mere cessation is not enough. The cessation must continue for a complete prayer time to indicate permanence. If it returns later, the original prayer with concessions was valid.
This is an expansion from the plaster analogy.
4
State the ruling outcome
If the condition (healing or permanent cessation) is met, the previous prayers performed with the concession become invalid (batil) and must be made up (qada). Otherwise, they are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو سقطت جبيرته عن برء أو زال عذر المعذور) قيد بالبرء لأن سقوطها لا عن برء لا يبطل الصلاة اتفاقاً لما بيناه في بابه. والمراد بزوال العذر استمرار انقطاعه وقتاً كاملاً، فإذا انقطع عذره بعد القعود فالأمر موقوف، فإن دام وقتاً كاملاً بعد الوقت الذي صلى فيه ووقع الانقطاع فيه فحينئذ يظهر أنه انقطاع هو برء فيظهر الفساد عند أبي حنيفة فيقضيها وإلا فمجرد الانقطاع لا يدل عليه لأنه لو عاد في الوقت الثاني فالصلاة الأولى صحيحة كما قدمناه
His saying: (or his plaster fell off due to healing or the excuse of the excused person ceased) He restricted it to healing because its falling off without healing does not invalidate the prayer by consensus, as we explained in its chapter. By cessation of the excuse is meant its continuous cessation for a complete time. So if his excuse ceases after sitting, the matter is suspended. If it continues for a complete time after the time in which he prayed and in which the cessation occurred, then it becomes apparent that the cessation is a recovery, and thus corruption becomes apparent according to Abu Hanifa, and he must make it up. Otherwise, mere cessation does not indicate that, because if it returns in the second time, the first prayer is valid as we previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This ruling covers two situations: a plaster (jabirah) falling off a broken limb, and the cessation of an excuse (like chronic bleeding) that allowed concessions. The key condition is that the falling off must be due to complete healing; if it falls off without full recovery, the prayer remains valid by consensus. For the excuse, the cessation must last for a complete prayer time to indicate permanence; otherwise, if it returns, the original prayer with concession was valid.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): Plaster or splint used to support a broken bone; its removal after healing may invalidate prayer if it was relied upon for purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Appointing an Unlettered Imam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Validity of Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of appointing an unlettered imam during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions regarding the invalidation of prayer when an unlettered person is appointed as imam during prayer, and state the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Appointing an unlettered imam invalidates prayer per al-Hidayah; valid after tashahhud per Fakhr al-Islam—the debate turns on 'contrary to prayer'.

This lesson examines an internal Hanafi difference concerning the ruling when a reciting worshipper (qari) appoints an unlettered person (ummi) to lead the remainder of the prayer. The key issue is whether the act of appointment itself is considered 'contrary to prayer' (munaf) and thus a nullifier, or whether it depends on the timing and the specific person appointed. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens our ability to apply the principles of istikhlaaf and to recognise when an action removes one from the state of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is the appointment (istikhlaaf) of an unlettered person as imam during prayer by a reciter who becomes unable to continue due to a slip in recitation. Determine what triggers this appointment and who the parties are.
The appointer is the original imam who is a qari; the appointed is ummi.
2
State the Hidayah position and its reasoning
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah holds that the prayer becomes invalid. His reasoning: the restricted appointment (muqayyad) of an ummi is an action contrary to prayer (munaf li al-salat) because the ummi is legally unfit to lead a qari. The corruption arises from the legal ruling of unfitness, not from the mere act of appointment.
The contrast: absolute appointment (mutilaq) is not munaf, but restricted appointment is.
3
State Fakhr al-Islam's position and its reasoning
Fakhr al-Islam (al-Zila'i) argues that if the appointment occurs after the tashahhud (final sitting), it does not invalidate, and he claims consensus on this. He authenticates this view in al-Kafi and Ghayat al-Bayan. His reasoning: absolute appointment is not contrary to prayer, and the restriction (appointing an ummi) does not change that after tashahhud because the prayer is essentially complete.
The dispute hinges on the distinction between 'absolute' and 'restricted' appointment, and the relevance of timing.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the appointment occurs before tashahhud, both views likely agree the prayer is invalid (though Fakhr al-Islam might still hold it valid before tashahhud? The text only mentions after tashahhud. But the thamarah: after tashahhud, Hidayah says invalid, Fakhr says valid. Thus, a worshipper following the Hidayah view would repeat the prayer, while one following Fakhr would not.
The mufta bihi according to the text is the Hidayah view, but later works like al-Kafi authenticate the other view, so a mufti may choose either depending on need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو استخلف أمياً) يعني عند سبق الحديث على ما اختاره في الهداية لأن فساد الصلاة بحكم شرعي وهو عدم صلاحيته للإمامة في حق القارىء لا بالاستخلاف لأنه غير مفسد حتى جاز استخلافه القارىء واختار فخر الإسلام أنه لا فساد بالاستخلاف بعد التشهد بالإجماع، وصححه في الكافي وغاية البيان، لأن استخلاف الأمي فعل مناف للصلاة فيكون مخرجاً منها، وكونه ليس بمناف لها إنما هو في مطلق الاستخلاف، وأما الاستخلاف المقيد وهو استخلاف الأمي فهو مناف لها
His statement: (or he appointed an unlettered person as imam) meaning when previous hadith occurs, according to what he chose in al-Hidayah, because the corruption of the prayer is by a legal ruling, which is his lack of qualification for imamah with respect to the reciter, not by the act of appointment, because it is not nullifying, so much so that the reciter's appointment is permissible. And Fakhr al-Islam chose that there is no corruption by appointment after tashahhud by consensus, and he authenticated it in al-Kafi and Ghayat al-Bayan, because appointing an unlettered person is an action contrary to prayer, thus it is a cause of exit from it. And its not being contrary to prayer is only in absolute appointment, but the restricted appointment, i.e., appointing an unlettered person, is contrary to it.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. It explains the ruling when a praying person who is reciting (qari) appoints an unlettered person (ummi) as imam due to a preceding hadith (i.e., his tongue slips). The author of al-Hidayah ruled that the prayer becomes invalid. The reasoning is that the unlettered person is legally unfit to lead the reciter, so the act of appointing him is a nullifier. However, Fakhr al-Islam (Imam al-Zila'i) held that if the appointment occurs after the tashahhud (final sitting), it does not invalidate, and he claimed consensus on this. He supported this view in al-Kafi and Ghayat al-Bayan. The key distinction is that absolute appointment (without specifying an unlettered person) is not contrary to prayer, but restricted appointment (choosing an unlettered person) is contrary. Thus, the Hanafi school has an internal difference: the preferred view in al-Hidayah is that it invalidates, while others, including Fakhr al-Islam, hold it valid if after tashahhud.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaaf): The act of appointing a substitute imam during prayer when the original imam is unable to continue.
أمي (ummi): An unlettered person who cannot recite Quran properly or at all.
مناف للصلاة (munaf li al-salat): An action contrary to the nature of prayer; such an action invalidates the prayer if done deliberately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Hidayah, if a reciter (qari) appoints an unlettered person as imam during prayer, what happens to the prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) The prayer remains valid.
C) The prayer turns into nafl.
D) The imam must repeat the rakah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal ikhtilaf on whether appointing an unlettered imam invalidates prayer; the difference depends on whether the appointment is considered 'contrary to prayer' and the timing (after tashahhud matters).

When Falling of a Cast or Cessation of Excuse Invalidates Prayer
Explanation of when falling of a medical cast or ending of an excuse invalidates prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which the falling of a medical cast (jabirah) invalidates the prayer, and explain the ruling regarding the cessation of an excuse according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
A cast falling only invalidates prayer if due to healing; for an excuse, cessation must last a full prayer time to invalidate.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a nuance in prayers performed under an excuse. The key is distinguishing between a cast falling due to healing versus accidentally, and for the excused person, the cessation must be continuous for an entire prayer period. Understanding this avoids unnecessary repetition of prayers and ensures proper application of the rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text discusses (a) the falling of a cast (jabirah) and (b) the cessation of an excuse ('udhr). Both affect the validity of a prayer performed under those conditions.
2
Note the common condition: healing (bar')
In both cases, invalidation depends on whether complete healing has occurred. Falling of the cast or cessation of the excuse must be a result of healing, not a temporary or incidental event.
3
Analyze the ruling for the cast
If the cast falls due to healing, the prayer becomes invalid. If it falls without healing (e.g., accidentally), the prayer remains valid by agreement among the Hanafi imams.
The text says 'اتفاقاً' (by agreement), indicating no ikhtilaf on this point.
4
Analyze the ruling for the excused person
For someone with a valid excuse (e.g., inability to use water), mere interruption of the excuse is not enough. According to Abu Hanifa, the interruption must continue for a complete prayer time after the prayer to be considered healing. If the excuse returns in the next time, the original prayer is valid.
The text uses 'وقف' (suspended) to describe the status until the full time passes.
5
Understand the practical consequence
If after praying with tayammum, water becomes available but only briefly, the prayer remains valid. If water remains available for the entire next prayer time, the original prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
This is based on Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو سقطت جبيرته عن برء أو زال عذر المعذور) قيد بالبرء لأن سقوطها لا عن لا يبطل الصلاة اتفاقاً لما بيناه في بابه. والمراد بزوال العذر استمرار انقطاعه وقتاً كاملاً، فإذا انقطع عذره بعد القعود فالأمر موقوف، فإن دام وقتاً كاملاً بعد الوقت الذي صلى فيه ووقع الانقطاع فيه فحينئذ يظهر أنه انقطاع هو برء فيظهر الفساد عند أبي حنيفة فيقضيها وإلا فمجرد الانقطاع لا يدل عليه لأنه لو عاد في الوقت الثاني فالصلاة الأولى صحيحة كما قدمناه
His statement: (or his cast fell due to healing, or the excuse of the excused person ceased) He restricted it to healing because its falling not due to [healing] does not invalidate the prayer by agreement, as we explained in its chapter. And the meaning of cessation of excuse is the continuation of its interruption for a complete time period. So if his excuse is interrupted after the final sitting, the matter is suspended. If it continues for a complete time period after the time in which he prayed and the interruption occurred in it, then it becomes clear that the interruption is healing, so invalidity becomes apparent according to Abu Hanifa, and he must make it up. Otherwise, mere interruption does not indicate [healing] because if it returns in the second time, the first prayer is valid as we have already mentioned.
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage discusses two cases: (1) falling off of a cast (jabirah) from a wound, and (2) cessation of the excuse of one who has a valid excuse (like illness) that permits tayammum or concessions. The cast falling off only invalidates the prayer if it falls due to complete healing. If it falls without healing (e.g., accidentally), the prayer remains valid by agreement. For the excused person, the cessation must be complete and continuous for an entire time period to be considered healing. If the interruption of the excuse is temporary and returns in the next prayer time, the original prayer is valid. According to Abu Hanifa, if the cessation is continuous for a full time period after the prayer, then the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated. This is because the excuse was not genuine; the person should have performed wudu or full prayer. The ruling is based on the condition of 'healing' being necessary before invalidation.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabirah): A cast or splint used for a broken bone or wound, upon which masah is allowed.
عذر ('udhr): A legal excuse that permits concessions in prayer, such as illness that allows tayammum.
برء (bar'): Complete healing, which is the condition for invalidation when cast falls or excuse ceases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever it falls, regardless of reason.
B) Only if it falls due to complete healing.
C) Only if it falls after the final sitting.
D) It never invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The prayer performed under a cast or excuse is only invalidated if the cast falls due to complete healing or if the excuse ceases completely for a full prayer time.

The Twelve Cases and Dispute After Final Sitting
Intra-Hanafi dispute on events after final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute about whether invalidating events after the final sitting invalidate the prayer, and state the position of Abu Hanifa versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The final sitting does not fully complete the prayer; events after it still invalidate according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

The Hanafi school is known for a set of twelve specific cases (Ithna Ashariyyah) where the prayer is invalidated or turns into nafl. Scholars later added more cases derived from these. A key dispute arises when such events occur after the final sitting (qa'dah): Abu Hanifa holds they still invalidate, while the Sahibayn consider the prayer already complete. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and the later scholarly analysis of Abu Hanifa's position.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Ithna Ashariyyah and its extensions
Recognize that the twelve cases are famous but the term is linguistically odd. Additional cases have been derived, such as praying in a najis garment then finding water, or a slave-girl freed during prayer without covering. Understand that all these reduce to three principles: occurrence of previous hadath, strengthening of a weak state, and entry of an incomplete time into a complete one.
The text quotes al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that only three of these convert the prayer to nafl: remembering a missed prayer, sunrise, or exit of Zuhr time on Friday.
2
Identify the core dispute
All agree that these events invalidate if they occur before the final sitting. The disagreement is when they occur after the final sitting but before taslim. Abu Hanifa says invalid; the Sahibayn say valid.
The Sahibayn analogize to hadath and speech after completion of the prayer.
3
Analyze the reasoning via al-Bardu'i and al-Karkhi
Later scholars debated why Abu Hanifa held his position. al-Bardu'i argued that Abu Hanifa considered exiting the prayer by one's own action (al-khuruj bi-sun'ihi) to be a fard, so the prayer is not complete until that exit occurs. al-Karkhi rejected this, citing the hadith where the Prophet said after tashahhud one may leave or stay, and claimed al-Bardu'i's inference was erroneous.
The text notes no explicit statement from Abu Hanifa on this, only al-Bardu'i's deduction.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a person prays and after tashahhud the sun rises, according to Abu Hanifa the prayer must be repeated; according to the Sahibayn it is valid. Later fatwa often follows the Sahibayn.
This affects daily practice, e.g., delaying salam until after sunrise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذكر هنا اثني عشر مسألة ولقبها اثنا عشرية عند أصحابنا وهي مشهورة عندهم بهذه النسبة إلا أن هذا الإطلاق غير جائز من حيث العربية لأنه إنما ينسب إلى صدر العدد مثله المركب في بعد أن يكون علماً على ما عرف في فنه فيقال في النسبة إلى خمسة عشر علماً على رجل أو غيره خمسي، وأما إذا لم يكن مسمى به وأريد به العدد فلا ينسب إليه أصلاً لأن الجزأين حينئذ مقصود أن بالمعنى، فلو حذف أحدهما اختل المعنى، ولو لم يحذف استثقل . قالوا : وقد زيد عليها مسائل فمنها : إذا كان يصلي بالثوب النجس فوجد ماء يغسل به وهو مستفاد من مسألة ما إذا وجد العاري ثوباً ومنها ما إذا كان يصلي القضاء فدخل عليه الأوقات المكروهة وهو مستفاد مسألة من طلوع الشمس في الفجر. ومنها إذا خرج الوقت على المعذور وهي ترجع إلى ظهور الحدث السابق ومنها الأمة إذا كانت تصلي بغير قناع فأعتقت في هذه الحالة ولم تستتر من ساعتها، وهو مستفاد مما إذا وجد العاري ثوباً، ففي التحقيق لا زيادة على ما هو المشهور، وحاصلها يرجع إلى ظهور الحدث السابق وقوة حاله بعد ضعفها وطرو الوقت الناقص على الكامل. وفي السراج الوهاج : إن الصلاة في هذه المسائل إذا بطلت لا تنقلب نفلاً إلا في ثلاث مسائل وهو ما إذا تذكر فائتة أو طلعت الشمس أو خرج وقت الظهر في يوم الجمعة . أطلق المصنف في بطلانها بهذه العوارض فشمل ما قبل القعود وما بعده ولا خلاف في بطلانها في الأول، وأما في حدوثها بعده فقال أبو حنيفة بالبطلان وقالا بالصحة لأنه معنى مفسد لها فصار كالحدث والكلام وقد حدثت بعد التمام فلا فساد واختلف المشايخ على قول أبي حنيفة؛ فذهب البردعي إلى أنه إنما قال بالبطلان لأن الخروج من الصلاة بصنع المصلي فرض عنده لأنها لا تبطل إلا بترك فرض ولم يبق عليه سوى الخروج بصنعه، وتبعه على ذلك العامة كما في العناية . وذهب الكرخي إلى أنه لا خلاف بينهم أن الخروج بصنعه منها ليس بفرض لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لابن مسعود «إذا قلت هذا أو فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك، فإن شئت أن تقوم فقم، وإن شئت أن تقعد فاقعد وليس فيه نص عن أبي حنيفة وإنما استنبطه البردعي من هذه المسائل غلط منه لأنه لو كان فرضاً كما زعمه لاختص بما هو قربه وهو السلام، وإنما حكم هو وصاحبيه ما لو كان بعده لا مطلقاً قوله : (قالوا وقد زيد عليها مسائل القائل الإمام الزيلعي وتبعه ابن الهمام وصاحب الدرر لكنهم اقتصروا على ثلاثة منها وهي ما عدا الثالثة، وكذا ذكر الثلاثة ابن شعبان في شرح المجمع كما ذكره الشرنبلالي قال ونوع دخول الوقت المكروه على مصلي القضاء بالزوال وتغير الشمس وكذلك طلوعها. ونقل الشرنبلالي أيضاً عن الذخيرة: لو سلم الأمي ثم تذكر أن عليه سجود السهود فعاد إليه فلما سجد تعلم سورة فسدت عند الإمام لا عندهما فتصير من الاثني عشرية، ولو سلم ثم تعلم سورة ثم تذكر سجدة تلاوة لم يذكر هذا في الكتاب وينبغي يكون من الاثني عشرية. اهـ كلام الذخيرة قوله : ففي التحقيق لا زيادة نازعه الشيخ اسمعيل أن
And he mentioned here twelve cases and they are called the 'Twelve' (ithna 'ashariyyah) among our companions, and they are famous among them by this name. However, this expression is not permissible from the standpoint of Arabic language... (linguistic discussion). They said: Cases have been added to them, including: if he was praying in a najis garment and found water to wash it with, which is derived from the case of when a naked person finds a garment; and from them: if he was performing qada prayer and a disliked time entered upon him, which is derived from the case of sunrise during Fajr; and from them: if time exits for the excused person, which refers to the occurrence of previous hadath; and from them: a slave-girl who was praying without covering and was freed in that state and did not cover immediately, which is derived from the case of the naked person finding a garment. So in reality, there is no increase beyond what is well-known, and its essence refers to the occurrence of previous hadath and the strengthening of its state after its weakness, and the entry of an incomplete time over a complete one. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Indeed, the prayer in these cases, if it becomes invalid, does not turn into nafl except in three cases: when one remembers a missed prayer, or the sun rises, or the time of Zuhr exits on Friday. The author made absolute in its invalidation by these occurrences, so it includes what is before the final sitting and what is after. There is no dispute about its invalidation in the former. As for their occurrence after it, Abu Hanifa said: invalidation; and the two said: validity, because it is a meaning that corrupts it, so it becomes like hadath and speech, and they occurred after completion, so no corruption. And the mashayikh differed on the saying of Abu Hanifa: al-Bardu'i went that he only said invalidation because exiting the prayer by one's own action is a fard according to him, since it is only invalidated by leaving a fard, and nothing remains except exiting by his action, and the general body followed him as in al-‘Inayah. And al-Karkhi went that there is no dispute among them that exiting by one's own action from it is not a fard, due to his statement (peace be upon him) to Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete; if you wish to stand, stand; if you wish to sit, sit.' There is no text from Abu Hanifa on this; rather, al-Bardu'i inferred it from these cases erroneously... (cut off).
Source pages p. 658

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq (page 658) discusses a famous set of twelve cases (al-ithna 'ashariyyah) known in the Hanafi school that invalidate prayer or turn it into nafl. The author notes linguistic issues with the term 'اثنا عشرية' (twelve-ness) in Arabic. He then lists additional cases that have been added, such as praying in a najis garment finding water, praying qada when a disliked time enters, etc. He then quotes from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that out of all these cases, the prayer only turns into nafl in three: when one remembers a missed prayer, sunrise, or exit of Zuhr time on Friday. The core dispute is about whether these invalidating events cause invalidity if they occur after the final sitting (al-qa'dah). All agree they invalidate if before; but after, Abu Hanifa says they invalidate, while the Sahibayn say they do not, because the prayer is already complete. Later scholars (mashayikh) differed on the reason for Abu Hanifa's position. Al-Bardu'i claimed Abu Hanifa considered exiting the prayer voluntarily (al-khuruj bi-sun' al-musalli) to be a fard, so if one does not exit after sitting, the prayer remains incomplete. Al-Karkhi disagreed, citing the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that after tashahhud, one may leave or stay; exiting is not a fard. Al-Karkhi said al-Bardu'i's inference is a mistake. The passage ends with additional cases from later works.

Key Terms
اثنا عشرية (Ithna 'Ashariyyah): A set of twelve specific cases where prayer is invalidated or turns into nafl, as collected by Hanafi scholars.
قعود (qu'ud): The final sitting (tashahhud) in prayer, which is the last pillar before salam.
فرض (fard): In this context, it refers to the alleged obligation of exiting the prayer by one's own action (al-khuruj bi-sun'ihi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if an invalidating event occurs after the final sitting but before salam, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid.
C) The prayer becomes nafl.
D) The prayer is suspended.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi dispute on events after final sitting: Abu Hanifa invalidates, Sahibayn uphold validity; later fatwa follows Sahibayn.
