So his statement 'And the answer' means that the answer to the imam with what al-Karkhi said is not consistent, so pay attention. The Masbuq's Status in Makeup and the Exception on Leading
Definition and exception to the masbuq's solitary makeup

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the general principle that a masbuq is alone in his makeup prayer and identify the first exception regarding leading and being led by another masbuq.

Core Idea
A masbuq is alone in his makeup, but cannot lead or be led by another masbuq because their tahrimas are separate.

After laying out specific scenarios, the text defines the masbuq and states a general principle: the masbuq is considered alone (munfarid) in the part of the prayer he makes up. However, there are four exceptions. This lesson focuses on the first exception: a masbuq cannot be an imam for nor follow another masbuq in the makeup portion, with a discussion of an exception made by Mulla Khusraw.

Guided Path
1
Define the Masbuq
The text defines a masbuq as one who did not perceive the first rak'ah (or the beginning) of the imam's prayer. This includes missing the first takbir.
The definition is important for applying subsequent rulings.
2
State the General Principle
The masbuq is alone (munfarid) in his makeup prayer. This means he recites individually and does not follow anyone during his makeup.
This principle has exceptions, as listed.
3
Identify the First Exception
The first exception is that a masbuq cannot be led by another masbuq (in the makeup), nor can he lead another masbuq. This is because their tahrimas (opening takbirs) are separate – each entered the prayer at different times.
If two masbuqs follow each other, the follower's prayer becomes invalid.
4
Explore the Dispute with Mulla Khusraw
Mulla Khusraw in al-Durar wa al-Ghurur made an exception to this exception, stating that a masbuq can lead others in a specific case involving 'al-Shams'? but the text criticises this and clarifies the correct view.
This reveals the intra-madhhab debate on the limits of the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وصح استخلاف المسبوق) لوجود المشاركة في التحريمة، والأولى للإمام أن يقدم مدركاً لأنه أقدر على إتمام صلاته، وينبغي لهذا المسبوق أن لا يتقدم لعجزه عن السلام، فلو تقدم يبتدىء من حيث انتهى إليه الإمام لقيامه مقامه، وإذا انتهى إلى السلام يقدم مدركاً يسلم بهم فلو استخلف في الرباعية مسبوقاً بركعتين فصلى الخليفة ركعتين ولم يقعد فسدت صلاته، ولو أشار إليه الإمام أنه لم يقرأ في الأوليين لزمه أن يقرأ في الأخريين لقيامه مقام الإمام، وإذا قرأ التحقت بالأوليين فخلت الأخريان عن القراءة فصار كأن الخليفة لم يقرأ في الأخريين، فإذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبقه لزمه القراءة فيما سبق به من الركعتين فقد لزمه القراءة في جميع الفرض الرباعي. ولو لم يعلم المسبوق الخليفة كمية صلاة الإمام ولا القوم بأن كان الكل مسبوقين مثله، إن كان الإمام سبقه الحدث وهو قائم صلى الذي تقدم ركعة وقعد مقدار التشهد ثم قام وأتم صلاة نفسه والقوم لا يقتدون به ولكنهم يمكثون إلى إن يفرغ هذا صلاته، فإذا فرغ قام القوم فيقضون ما بقي من صلاتهم وجداناً لأن من الجائز أن الذي بقي على الإمام آخر الركعات فحين صلى الخليفة تلك الركعة تمت صلاة الإمام، فلو اقتدوا به فيما يقضي هو كانوا اقتدوا بمسبوق فيما يقضي فتفسد صلاتهم، ولا يشتغلون بالقضاء لجواز أن يكون بعض ما يقضي هذا الخليفة مما بقي على الإمام الأول فيكون القوم قد انفردوا قبل فراغ إمامهم من جيمع أركان الصلاة فتفسد صلاتهم، فالأحوط في ذلك ما قلنا. كذا في الظهيرية. وفي فتح القدير : ويقعد هذا الخليفة فيما بقي على الإمام الأول على كل ركعة . وهكذا في الخلاصة، ولم يبينوا ما إذا سبقه الحدث وهو قاعد واقتدوا به وهو قاعد فاستخلف واحداً منهم ولم يعلموا أنها الأولى أو الثانية والفرض رباعي كالظهر، وينبغي على قياس ما أن يصلي الخليفة ركعتين وحده وهم جلوس فإذا فرغ منهما قاموا وصلى كل واحد وحده، والخليفة ما بقي ولا يشتغلون بالقضاء قبل فراغه من الأوليين لما ذكرناه لاحتمال أن تكون القعدة التي للإمام هي الأخيرة، وحينئذ ليس لهم الأقتداء، ويحتمل أن تكون الأولى وحينئذ ليس لهم الانفراد وحقيقة المسبوق هو من لم يدرك أول صلاة الإمام والمراد بالأول وله أحكام كثيرة فمنها أنه منفرد فيما يقضي إلا في أربع مسائل : إحداهما أنه لا يجوز اقتداؤه ولا الاقتداء به لأنه بان تحريمة فلو اقتدى مسبوق بمسبوق فسدت صلاة المقتدي قرأ أو لم يقرأ دون الإمام واستثنى ملا خسرو في الدرر والغرر من قولهم لا منهم أنه أربعا [؟] الشمس إذ ليس فيه أداء مع الحدث. وقول المؤلف وهذا كله على تعليل البردعي الخ» غير ظاهر بل أول كلام الكمال إنما هو بناء على تعليل البردعي. وقوله والجواب بأن الفساد الخ» بناء على قول الكرخي لأن البردعي قائل بأن الفساد لعدم الفعل أي عدم الخروج بصنعه فصار حاصل كلام الكمال بحث في دليل الإمام على التخريجين أما على تخريج البردعي القائل بأن الفساد لعدم الفعل فيرد عليه أن اشتراط الفعل الاختياري إنما يلزم في المقاصد لا في الوسائل الخ . وأما على تعليل الكرخي القائل بأن الفساد لا لعدم الفعل بل للأداء الحدث فيرد عليه أنه غير مطرد. فقوله «والجواب» معناه أن الجواب عن الإمام بما قاله الكرخي غير مطرد فتنبه قوله : (ولا يشتغلون بالقضاء الخ) تصريح بما علم من قوله ولكنهم يمكثون إلى أن يفرغ وبيان لوجهه قوله : (ولم يبينوا ما إذا سبقه الحدث) أي سبق الإمام الأول وذلك حيث قيد أولاً بقوله إن كان الإمام سبقه الحدث وهو قائم» قوله : (إحداهما أنه لا يجوز اقتداره ولا الاقتداء به كذا في الفتح لكن الثانية ظاهرة، وأما الأولى فقال الشيخ إسمعيل : للنظر في إدخالها في المسائل المستثناة مجال لأن المنفرد أيضاً ليس له بعد التحريمة أن يقتدي بأحد، ولعله الداعي إلى ترك المصنف التعرض لها فليتدبر اهـ. قوله : (واستثنى ملا خسرو في الدرر والغرر الخ ) قال في النهر أقول : عبارته فيها المسبوق فيما يقضي له جهتان جهة الانفراد حقيقة حتى يثني ويتعوذ ويقرأ وجهة الاقتداء حتى لا يؤتم به وإن صلح للخلافة أي من حيث كونه مسبوقاً لا بخصوص كونه قاضياً، ومن العجب أن ما حكم عليه هنا بأنه سهو، جزم به في الأشباه والنظائر على أنه مستثنى من قولهم ولا يقتدي به وقد علمت ما الواقع اهـ . لكن لا يخفى عليك ظهور ما قاله المؤلف هنا وإن جاراه في الأشباه فإن قول الدرر فيما يقضي ينافي ما أدرجه في النهر بقوله أي من حيث كونه مسبوقاً، وكذا تتمة عبارة الدرر تنافي هو
His saying: (And it is valid to appoint a masbuq as substitute) because of the participation in the opening takbir. It is better for the imam to appoint someone who has caught up because he is more able to complete his prayer. And it is proper for this masbuq not to step forward due to his inability to make taslim. So if he steps forward, he begins from where the imam ended because he stands in his place. When he reaches the taslim, he presents someone who has caught up to make taslim with them. So if he appoints a masbuq in a four-rak'ah prayer who missed two rak'ahs, and the substitute prays two rak'ahs and does not sit, his prayer becomes invalid. And if the imam indicates to him that he did not recite in the first two, he must recite in the last two because he stands in the imam's place. When he recites, it becomes connected to the first two, so the last two are empty of recitation, as if the substitute did not recite in the last two. So when he stands for what he missed, he must recite in what he missed of the two rak'ahs, so he must recite in the entire four-rak'ah prayer. And if the masbuq substitute does not know the quantity of the imam's prayer nor the congregation's, such that all are masbuqs like him: if the imam was overtaken by hadath while standing, the one who stepped forward prays one rak'ah and sits for the amount of tashahhud, then stands and completes his own prayer, and the congregation does not follow him but wait until he finishes his prayer. When he finishes, the congregation stands to make up what remains of their prayer (just finding it) because it is possible that what remained of the imam was the last rak'ah. When the substitute prayed that rak'ah, the imam's prayer was completed. So if they followed him in what he is making up, they would be following a masbuq in his makeup, and their prayer would be invalid. And they do not occupy themselves with making up because it is possible that some of what this substitute makes up is part of what remained of the first imam, so the congregation would have separated before the completion of their imam's entire prayer, and their prayer would be invalid. So what we said is the most cautious. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'And this substitute sits for every rak'ah of what remained of the first imam.' And similarly in al-Khulasa. And they did not clarify what if the imam was overtaken by hadath while sitting, and the congregation followed him while sitting, then he appointed one of them as substitute, and they do not know whether it is the first (sitting) or the second, and the prayer is four-rak'ah like zuhr. And by analogy, the substitute should pray two rak'ahs alone while they sit, and when he finishes them, they stand and each prays alone, and the substitute remains. And they do not occupy themselves with making up before he finishes the first two because of what we mentioned due to the possibility that the sitting of the imam is the last, and then they cannot follow, and it is possible that it is the first, and then they cannot separate. And the reality of the masbuq is the one who did not perceive the beginning of the imam's prayer, and 'the beginning' refers to the first opening takbir. It has many rulings: among them is that he is alone in his makeup except in four issues: one of them is that it is not permissible for him to be led nor to lead, because of the separation in the opening takbir. So if a masbuq follows a masbuq, the prayer of the follower is invalid whether he recites or not, except for the imam. And Mulla Khusraw in al-Durar wa al-Ghurur made an exception from their statement that he should not be among them that it is four [؟] al-Shams because there is no performance with hadath. And the statement of the author: 'And all this is according to the reasoning of al-Barda'i...' is not apparent. Rather, the initial statement of al-Kamal is based on the reasoning of al-Barda'i. And his statement: 'And the answer is that the invalidity...' is based on the statement of al-Karkhi, because al-Barda'i says that the invalidity is due to the lack of the act, i.e., not exiting by his own action. So the gist of al-Kamal's speech is a discussion of the proof of the imam on the two derivations: based on al-Barda'i's derivation that invalidity is due to lack of act, the objection is that the condition of voluntary action only applies to objectives not to means; and based on al-Karkhi's derivation that invalidity is not due to lack of act but due to the hadath, the objection is that it is not consistent. So his statement 'And the answer' means that the answer to the imam with what al-Karkhi said is not consistent, so pay attention. His saying: (And they do not occupy themselves with making up...) is an explicit statement of what is known from his statement: 'but they wait until he finishes' and clarification of its reason. His saying: (And they did not clarify what if the imam was overtaken by hadath...) i.e., when the first imam was overtaken, and this is where he first restricted it to 'if the imam was overtaken by hadath while standing'. His saying: (one of them is that it is not permissible for him to be led nor to lead) as in al-Fath, but the second is apparent. As for the first, Sheikh Isma'il said: there is room for consideration in including it among the exceptional issues because the individual also, after the opening takbir, cannot follow anyone. Perhaps this is why the author (of Kanz al-Daqaiq) avoided mentioning it, so reflect. His saying: (And Mulla Khusraw made an exception in al-Durar wa al-Ghurur...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: his expression in it is: the masbuq regarding what he makes up has two aspects: the aspect of being alone in reality, so he says the thana', ta'awwudh, and recites, and the aspect of being a follower, so he cannot be followed, even though he is valid as a substitute, i.e., by virtue of being a masbuq, not specifically by virtue of being a maker-up. And it is strange that what he ruled here as a mistake, he affirmed in al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair that it is excepted from their statement that he should not be followed, and you have seen what is the reality. But it is not hidden from you the clarity of what the author said here, even if he followed him in al-Ashbah. Indeed, the statement of al-Durar regarding 'what he makes up' contradicts what he included in al-Nahr by saying 'i.e., by virtue of being a masbuq'. And likewise the rest of the expression of al-Durar contradicts it.
Source pages p. 660

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq that it is valid to appoint a masbuq (a latecomer who missed part of the prayer) as a substitute imam (khalifa). The reason given is that the masbuq shares the opening takbir (tahrima) with the imam, so he has a valid connection to the prayer. However, it is preferable for the imam to appoint someone who has caught up completely (mudrik) because he is more capable of completing the prayer. The masbuq should not step forward to lead because he cannot make the final taslim himself (since he still owes rak'ahs). If he does step forward, he starts from where the imam left off, and when it is time for taslim, he should hand over to a mudrik who can make taslim with the congregation. The passage then discusses various scenarios: if the masbuq substitute misses two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer and does not sit after two rak'ahs, his prayer is invalid. If the imam indicates that he did not recite in the first two rak'ahs, the substitute must recite in the last two, which effectively makes the recitation belong to the first two, so the last two become without recitation. Then when he stands for his makeup (the two he missed), he must recite in them, resulting in recitation in all four rak'ahs. The next scenario is when the masbuq substitute does not know the amount of prayer the imam had done, and all are masbuqs. If the imam was overtaken by hadath while standing, the substitute should pray one rak'ah, sit, then stand and complete his own prayer. The congregation must wait and not follow him or start their makeup until he finishes, to avoid the risk of their prayer becoming invalid due to several possibilities. The passage also gives analogous rulings for when the imam is overtaken by hadath while sitting, and the prayer is four rak'ahs like zuhr. Then it defines the masbuq as one who missed the first rak'ah (or the beginning) of the imam's prayer. It states that the masbuq is considered alone (munfarid) in his makeup prayer except in four exceptional issues. The first exception listed is that it is not permissible for a masbuq to be led by another masbuq, nor to lead another (in his makeup), because his tahrima is separate. If two masbuqs follow each other, the follower's prayer is invalid. However, Mulla Khusraw made an exception in al-Durar wa al-Ghurur regarding this ruling, but the commentator discusses the disagreement. The passage ends with a discussion of the reasoning of al-Barda'i and al-Karkhi as applied to these rulings, and a critique of the statement of the author of al-Durar. The overall lesson is that the ruling of the masbuq being alone in his makeup is not absolute, and certain exceptions exist.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that enters the person into the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if one masbuq leads another masbuq in his makeup prayer?
A) Both prayers are valid.
B) The follower's prayer is invalid; the leader's is valid.
C) Both prayers are invalid.
D) The prayer is valid only if they recite aloud.

Key Takeaway
While a masbuq is generally alone in his makeup, one of four exceptions prohibits him from leading or being led by another masbuq due to separate tahrimas.

Precautionary Ruling for the Successor Imam When Uncertainty Arises
Explains the ruling for the congregation when the imam has hadath and appoints a successor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the successor imam when the congregation is uncertain whether the imam's sitting was the first or last, and explain the precautionary measure.

Core Idea
When uncertainty exists about the imam's state, the successor prays two rak'ahs alone while the congregation waits.

Imagine you are in a congregational prayer. The imam suddenly experiences a hadath (ritual impurity) and appoints a successor from among the followers. However, the followers are unsure whether the imam's sitting was after the first two rak'ahs (taslim earlier) or after the last two (end of prayer). What should they do? The Hanafi jurists provide a precautionary ruling to avoid invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The imam has hadath while sitting, and the congregation followed him. They are uncertain if that sitting was the first (after two rak'ahs) or the last (after four) in a four-rak'ah prayer like Zuhr.
2
Identify the problem
If the sitting was the last, the prayer should have ended, and any additional rak'ahs led by the successor would be invalid. If it was the first, the congregation should not have separated from the imam by letting him go.
The uncertainty could lead to invalid prayer if not handled cautiously.
3
State the precautionary ruling
The successor should pray two rak'ahs alone quietly while the congregation remains seated. After he finishes, each follower stands and prays the remaining rak'ahs individually. The successor continues where he left off after his two rak'ahs.
This ruling is found in Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah, and is described as 'the most precautionary (ahwat)' in al-Zahiriyyah.
4
Explain the reasoning
If the imam's sitting was the first, the congregation should not have separated themselves; but by waiting, they avoid following a successor after the imam's prayer was incomplete. If it was the last, they should not have followed the successor beyond the prayer; by not standing, they avoid adding extra rak'ahs. This method covers both possibilities.
The key is avoiding the possibility of invalidating the prayer due to uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكروه يكون بعض ما يقضي هذا الخليفة مما بقي على الإمام الأول فيكون القوم قد انفردوا قبل فراغ إمامهم من جميع أركان الصلاة فتفسد صلاتهم، فالأحوط في ذلك ما قلنا. كذا في الظهيرية. وفي فتح القدير : ويقعد هذا الخليفة فيما بقي على الإمام الأول على كل ركعة . وهكذا في الخلاصة، ولم يبينوا ما إذا سبقه الحدث وهو قاعد واقتدوا به وهو قاعد فاستخلف واحداً منهم ولم يعلموا أنها الأولى أو الثانية والفرض رباعي كالظهر، وينبغي على قياس ما أن يصلي الخليفة ركعتين وحده وهم جلوس فإذا فرغ منهما قاموا وصلى كل واحد وحده، والخليفة ما بقي ولا يشتغلون بالقضاء قبل فراغة من الأوليين لما ذكرناه لاحتمال أن تكون القعدة التي للإمام هي الأخيرة، وحينئذ ليس لهم الأقتداء، ويحتمل أن تكون الأولى وحينئذ ليس لهم الانفراد
They mentioned that some of what this successor completes from what remains of the first imam, then the people would have separated before the completion of their imam's arkan, so their prayer becomes invalid. The most precautionary in that is what we said. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah. And in Fath al-Qadir: This successor sits for every rak'ah that remains from the first imam. Thus in al-Khulasah. And they did not explain if the hadath overtakes him while he is sitting and they followed him while he is sitting, so he appointed one of them as successor, and they do not know if it is the first or second (rak'ah), and the fard is four like Zuhr. It would be appropriate by analogy that the successor prays two rak'ahs alone while they are sitting. When he finishes them, they stand and each prays alone, and the successor continues what remains. And they should not occupy themselves with completion (qada) before he finishes the first two, due to what we mentioned, because it is possible that the sitting of the imam was the last, in which case they should not follow. And it is possible that it was the first, in which case they should not separate themselves.
Source pages p. 661

Commentary
This passage discusses a situation where the imam experiences a hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer and appoints a successor. The congregation had already followed him while he was sitting, and they are uncertain whether that sitting was the first (after two rak'ahs) or the last (after four). To be cautious, the successor should pray two rak'ahs alone while the congregation remains seated. After he finishes, they each pray the remaining rak'ahs individually. The reasoning: if the sitting was the final one, they should not have followed him in additional rak'ahs; if it was the first, they should not have separated themselves from the imam. This precaution avoids potential invalidation of their prayer.

Key Terms
خليفة (khalifah): The person appointed by the imam to lead the prayer after the imam's hadath.
حدث (hadath): Anything that invalidates wudu (ritual purity) and thus the prayer.
أحوط (ahwat): Most precautionary; a recommended measure to avoid invalidating the prayer in cases of uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario described, what should the successor (khalifah) do when the congregation is uncertain whether the imam's sitting was the first or last?
A) Continue the prayer as normal and complete the remaining rak'ahs.
B) Pray two rak'ahs alone while the congregation sits, then each prays individually.
C) Lead the congregation in the remaining rak'ahs as if it were the first sitting.
D) Immediately end the prayer and start over.

Key Takeaway
When uncertainty about the imam's progress in prayer arises, the precautionary (ahwat) Hanafi ruling is for the successor to pray a separate two-rak'ah unit alone while the congregation waits, after which everyone completes individually.

The Masbuq: Definition and Four Exceptions to His Being a Munfarid
Defines the masbuq and lists four exceptions to him being a munfarid in qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the masbuq, state the general rule that he is a munfarid in his qada, and list the four exceptions with their basic rulings.

Core Idea
A masbuq is a munfarid in his qada except in four specific situations that modify his independence.

When you join a congregation late, you become a masbuq—one who must complete the missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam. Hanafi fiqh treats the masbuq as an independent worshipper (munfarid) during his qada, but this independence is not absolute. There are four exceptions where the masbuq is not fully treated as a munfarid, and understanding these is crucial for correct prayer.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of masbuq
Understand who is a masbuq: one who missed the first rak'ah or more of the imam's prayer. The general principle is that he is munfarid in the parts he completes after the imam's salam (qada).
2
Identify the first exception: inability to lead or follow another masbuq
A masbuq cannot validly follow another masbuq, nor can he be followed as an imam. If a masbuq follows another masbuq, the follower's prayer is invalid. Sub-issues include the imam appointing a masbuq as successor, following mistaken sajdah al-sahw, and the fifth rak'ah scenario.
This exception has multiple sub-cases detailed in the passage.
3
Identify the second exception: takbir for starting anew
If a masbuq says takbir intending to start a new prayer (musta'nif), he cuts off his previous prayer and becomes a fresh prayer. A munfarid cannot do this; his takbir would not cut off his prayer.
4
Identify the third exception: following the imam's sahw prostrations
If the masbuq stands to complete his qada while the imam still has sajdah al-sahw to perform before the masbuq entered, the masbuq must return and prostrate with the imam, provided he has not yet performed a sajdah in his own rak'ah. A munfarid is not required to follow another's sahw.
5
Identify the fourth exception: takbir al-tashriq
The masbuq must recite the takbir of tashriq (during Hajj season) by agreement of the school. In contrast, a munfarid is not required to do so according to Abu Hanifah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحقيقة المسبوق هو من لم يدرك أول صلاة الإمام والمراد بالأول وله أحكام كثيرة فمنها أنه منفرد فيما يقضي إلا في أربع مسائل : إحداها أنه لا يجوز اقتداؤه ولا الاقتداء به لأنه بان تحريمة فلو اقتدى مسبوق بمسبوق فسدت صلاة المقتدي قرأ أو لم يقرأ دون الإمام واستثنى منلاخسرو وفي الدرر والغرر من قولهم لا يصح الاقتداء بالمسبوق أن إمامه لو أحدث فاستخلفه استخلافه وصار إماماً اهـ. وهو يصح به في لأنه سهو كلامهم فيما إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به وهو في هذه الحالة لا الاقتداء أصلاً فلا استثناء. ولو ظن الإمام أن عليه سهواً فسجد للسهو فتابعه المسبوق فيه ثم علم أنه ليس عليه سهو ففيه روايتان والأشهر أن صلاة المسبوق تفسد لأنه اقتدى في موضع الانفراد. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث في زماننا لا تفسد لأن الجهل في القراء غالب كذا الظهيرية. ولو لم يعلم لم تفسد في قولهم كذا في الخانية. ولو قام الإمام إلى الخامسة في صلاة الظهر فتابعه المسبوق إن قعد الإمام على رأس الرابعة تفسد صلاة المسبوق، وإن لم يقعد لم تفسد حتى يقيد الخامسة بالسجدة فإذا قيدها بالسجدة فسدت صلاة الكل لأن الإمام إذا قعد على الرابعة تمت صلاته في حق المسبوق فلا يجوز للمسبوق متابعته، ولو نسي أحد المسبوقين المتساويين كمية ما عليه فقضى ملاحظاً للآخر بلا اقتداء به صح. ثانيها لو كبر ناوياً للاستئناف يصير مستأنفاً قاطعاً للأولى بخلاف المنفرد على ما يأتي. ثالثها لو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وعلى الإمام سجدتا سهو قبل أن يدخل معه كان عليه أن يعود فيسجد معه ما لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة، فإن لم يعد حتى سجد يمضي وعليه أن يسجد في آخر صلاته بخلاف المنفرد لا يجب عليه السجود السهو غيره رابعها يأتي بتكبير التشريق اتفاقاً بخلاف المنفرد لا يجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة، وفيما سوى ذلك هو منفرد لعدم المشاركة فيما يقضيه حقيقة وحكماً.
And the reality of the masbuq is the one who did not catch the beginning of the imam's prayer, meaning the first (rak'ah). And it has many rulings, among them that he is a munfarid (individual) in what he completes (qada) except in four issues: First, it is not permissible for him to follow (another) nor to be followed (as imam), because his tahrimah (beginning) is separate. If a masbuq follows another masbuq, the prayer of the follower is invalid, whether he recited or not, unlike (following) the imam. And [؟] excepted in al-Durar wa al-Gharar from their statement: it is not valid to follow a masbuq because if his imam had hadath and appointed him as successor, he becomes imam. [He said:] it is valid [؟] because it is a slip of their speech regarding when he stands to complete what he missed, and in this case there is no following at all, so there is no exception. And if the imam thinks he has sahw and prostrates for sahw, and the masbuq follows him in that, then learns that he had no sahw, there are two narrations: the more famous is that the masbuq's prayer is invalid because he followed in a place of being munfarid. And Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said in our time it is not invalid because ignorance is common among reciters. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah. And if he did not know, it is not invalid according to them. Thus in al-Khaniyyah. And if the imam stands for a fifth (rak'ah) in Zuhr prayer and the masbuq follows him: if the imam sat at the fourth, the masbuq's prayer is invalid; if he did not sit, it is not invalid until he connects the fifth with a sajdah; when he connects it with a sajdah, everyone's prayer is invalid because when the imam sat at the fourth, his prayer was complete with respect to the masbuq, so the masbuq may not follow him. And if one of two equal masbuqs forgets the amount he owes, and he completes (qada) observing the other without following him, it is valid. Second: if he says takbir intending to start anew, he becomes a musta'nif (one starting anew), cutting off the first, unlike the munfarid as will come. Third: if he stands to complete what he missed while the imam has two sajdahs of sahw before he (the masbuq) enters with him, he must return and prostrate with him as long as he has not connected the rak'ah with a sajdah. If he does not return until after prostrating, he continues and must prostrate at the end of his prayer, unlike the munfarid who is not required to prostrate for sahw of others. Fourth: he says takbir of tashriq by agreement, unlike the munfarid who is not required to do so according to Abu Hanifah. And beyond that, he is a munfarid due to lack of participation in what he completes, in reality and in ruling.
Source pages p. 661

Commentary
This passage defines the masbuq (one who misses the beginning of the imam's prayer) and states the general rule: the masbuq is considered a munfarid (praying alone) in his qada (the parts he completes after the imam's salam). However, there are four exceptions to this rule. The first exception is that a masbuq cannot be followed as an imam nor can he follow another masbuq as a follower, because his tahrimah (opening takbir) is separate from the imam's. The text then discusses various sub-rulings, including the case of the imam experiencing hadath and appointing a masbuq as successor, the case of the imam prostrating for sahw mistakenly, the imam standing for a fifth rak'ah, and two masbuqs praying together. The second exception is that if the masbuq intentionally starts anew with takbir, he cuts off the previous prayer, unlike a munfarid. The third exception involves returning to follow the imam's sahw prostrations. The fourth exception is that the masbuq must recite takbir al-tashriq, whereas a munfarid does not according to Abu Hanifah. Beyond these four exceptions, the masbuq is treated as a munfarid in his qada.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): One who missed the first rak'ah or more of the imam's prayer and completes the missed part after the imam's salam.
انفراد (infirad): The state of praying alone; the masbuq is treated as an individual in his qada.
قضاء (qada): The part of the prayer that the masbuq performs after the imam's salam to complete what he missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases is a masbuq NOT considered a munfarid in his qada?
A) When he recites al-Fatihah alone.
B) When he performs sajdah al-sahw for his own mistake.
C) When he says takbir intending to start anew (musta'nif).
D) When he completes the missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq is generally a munfarid in his qada, but four exceptions restrict his independence in specific scenarios involving following others, starting anew, sajdah al-sahw, and takbir al-tashriq.

Rulings on Masbuq: Salam, Sahw, and Standing for Qada
Lists various rulings related to the masbuq regarding salam, sahw, and when to stand for qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three rulings for the masbuq regarding salam and standing for qada, and apply each to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
A masbuq's timings of salam and standing for qada depend on the imam's actions, with exceptions for necessity.

When a latecomer (masbuq) follows an imam in congregation, several precise rulings govern his actions at the end of the imam's prayer. These include when he may say salam, whether he needs to perform sajdah al-sahw, and the correct moment to stand for his missed rak'ahs. This lesson extracts three key rulings from the passage and explains their application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings on salam
Read the first part of the passage: it distinguishes three scenarios: salam with imam forgetfully, before imam, and after imam. Note the consequence for each.
Focus on the condition of being a follower (muqtadi) and the effect on sajdah al-sahw.
2
Determine the time to stand for qada
The passage states that the masbuq should not stand before the imam's two taslims, and explains the reason: waiting for possible sajdah al-sahw by the imam.
Note the qualification from Fath al-Qadir regarding the imam's practice of sajdah al-sahw before or after salam.
3
Recognize exceptions for early standing
List the exceptional cases where the masbuq may stand earlier: fear of expiry of wudu time (for masah), fear of missing the prayer time in Jumu'ah, 'Eid, Fajr, or for an excused person.
Understand the basis: necessity overrides the general rule.
4
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Practice applying these rules to concrete examples, such as an 'Eid prayer where the time is short, or a regular congregation.
Check your understanding against the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أحكامه أنه لو سلم مع الإمام ساهياً أو قبله لا يلزمه سجود السهو لأنه مقتد، وإن سلم بعده لزمه، وإن سلم مع الإمام على ظن أن عليه السلام مع الإمام فهو سلام عمد فتفسد. كذا في الظهيرية. ومن أحكامه أنه لا يقوم إلى القضاء قبل التسليمتين بل ينتظر فراغ الإمام بعدهما لإحتمال سهو على الإمام فيصبر حتى يفهم أنه لا سهو عليه إذ لو كان لسجد. وقيده في فتح القدير بحثاً بأن محله ما إذا اقتدى بمن يرى سجود السهو بعد السلام، أما إذا اقتدى بمن يراه قبله فلا . قلت : الخلاف بین الأئمة إنما هو في الأولوية فربما اختار الإمام الشافعي أن يسجد بعد السلام عملاً بالجائز فلهذا أطلقوا استنظاره. ومن أحكامه أنه لا يقوم المسبوق قبل السلام بعد قدر التشهد إلا في مواضع إذا خاف وهو ماسح تمام المدة لو انتظر سلام الإمام أو خاف المسبوق في الجمعة والعيدين والفجر أو المعذور خروج الوقت أو ذلك فإنه قال : حتى لا يؤتم به وتقطع تكبيرة الافتتاح تحريمته ويلزمه العود إلى سهو إمامه ويأتي بتكبير التشريق فإن ذلك كله فيما يقضي كما هو صريح صدر كلامه فإحراج قوله وإن صلح للخلافة عن تلك الحيثية إلى حيثية أخرى تأويل بعيد جداً لا يعترض بمثله على ما جرى عليه المؤلف من التحقيق. قوله: (ولو قام قبله أي قبل قدر التشهد رملي قوله : (فإن وجد منه قيام الخ) قال
And among its rulings: if he says salam with the imam forgetfully or before him, sajdah al-sahw is not necessary for him because he is a follower. If he says salam after him, it is necessary. If he says salam with the imam thinking that he should say salam with him, it is intentional salam and invalidates (the prayer). Thus in al-Zahiriyyah. And among its rulings: he should not stand for qada before the two taslims (salam), but waits for the imam to finish after them due to the possibility of sahw on the imam. He waits until he understands that there is no sahw on him, because if there were, he would prostrate. And al-Qadir restricted it in Fath al-Qadir by investigation: that it is applicable if he followed someone who performs sajdah al-sahw after salam; if he followed someone who performs it before salam, then no. I said: the difference among imams is only about preference; perhaps Imam al-Shafi'i chose to prostrate after salam acting upon what is permissible, so they allowed waiting for him. And among its rulings: the masbuq should not stand before salam after the amount of tashahhud except in places: if he fears that his time (for wiping) as one who is masah will expire if he waits for the imam's salam, or the masbuq fears (expiry of time) in Jumu'ah, the two 'Eids, and Fajr, or the excused one fears the end of time, or that: he said: so that he will not be followed, and the takbir of iftitah cuts off his tahrimah, and he must return to the sahw of his imam, and he says takbir of tashriq. All of that is in what he completes (qada), as is clear from the beginning of his speech. So forcing his statement 'and if he is fit for khilafah' from that perspective to another perspective is a far-fetched interpretation that is not objected to by what the author has done in verification. He said: (And if he stands before, i.e., before the amount of tashahhud, [؟], he said: (If there is found from him standing...)) he said.
Source pages p. 662

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings for the masbuq. First, regarding salam: if the masbuq says salam with the imam forgetfully or before him, no sajdah al-sahw is required because he is a follower. If he says salam after the imam, sajdah al-sahw becomes necessary. If he intentionally says salam with the imam, it invalidates his prayer. Second, the masbuq should not stand for qada before the imam completes the two taslims; he waits in case the imam needs to perform sajdah al-sahw. This is qualified by Fath al-Qadir: it applies if the imam performs sajdah al-sahw after salam; if before salam, the masbuq can stand earlier. Third, the masbuq should not stand before salam after the amount of tashahhud except in certain situations: when he fears expiry of his wudu time (if he is masah), or when he fears leaving the time of the prayer in Jumu'ah, 'Eid, Fajr, or for an excused person. In such cases, he may stand early. The text ends with a discussion about the interpretation of 'if he is fit for khilafah' from the perspective of qada.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness; required when certain elements are omitted or added inadvertently.
قضاء (qada): The missed rak'ahs that the masbuq prays after the imam's salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the masbuq need to perform sajdah al-sahw for salam?
A) If he says salam with the imam forgetfully.
B) If he says salam after the imam.
C) If he says salam before the imam forgetfully.
D) If he says salam with the imam intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must wait for the imam's two taslims before standing, and his salam timing determines whether sajdah al-sahw is required or the prayer is invalidated.

The Masbuq Following the Imam in Sajdah Sahw When the Imam is Mistaken
Commentary on masbuq rulings from Kanz al-Daqaiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations regarding the masbuq following the imam in sajdah sahw when the imam was mistaken and apply the mufta bihi view of Abu al-Layth.

Core Idea
The masbuq's prayer is not invalid if he follows the imam's mistaken sajdah sahw, due to common ignorance.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: the imam mistakenly performs sajdah sahw, and the masbuq follows him. What happens to the masbuq's prayer? The Hanafi school has two narrations. We will analyze the proofs and the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the masbuq following the imam in sajdah sahw when the imam was mistaken. The ruling is contested between invalid (first narration) and valid (mufta bihi).
The masbuq is a follower in what he prays with the imam but independent in his qada'.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'innama ju'ila al-imam li yu'tamma bihi' is the general proof for following the imam, but the specific scenario raises the question of whether the masbuq's prayer is invalidated.
The hadith is not explicitly cited in this segment but underlies the obligation of followership.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies an obligation to follow, but the masbuq's independence in his qada' creates a conflict. The two narrations differ on whether the masbuq's following here is a violation of that independence.
The first narration sees it as following in a place of independence; the second views it as excusable due to ignorance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Two riwayat: one says prayer is invalid, the other (preferred by Abu al-Layth) says it is not invalid. The text cites al-Zahira favoring the latter.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the view of Abu al-Layth that the prayer is not invalid, due to widespread ignorance among the public (jahil ghalib).
Tarjih authority: al-Zahira and later fatwa manuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاقتداء بالمسبوق أن إمامه لو أحدث فاستخلفه استخلافه وصار إماماً اهـ. وهو صح لأنه سهو كلامهم فيما إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به وهو في هذه الحالة لا الاقتداء أصلاً فلا استثناء. ولو ظن الإمام أن عليه سهواً فسجد للسهو فتابعه المسبوق فيه ثم علم أنه ليس عليه سهو ففيه روايتان والأشهر أن صلاة المسبوق تفسد لأنه اقتدى في موضع الانفراد. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث في زماننا لا تفسد لأن الجهل في القراء غالب كذا الظهيرية. ولو لم يعلم لم تفسد في قولهم كذا في الخانية. ولو قام الإمام إلى الخامسة في صلاة الظهر فتابعه المسبوق إن قعد الإمام على رأس الرابعة تفسد صلاة المسبوق، وإن لم يقعد لم تفسد حتى يقيد الخامسة بالسجدة فإذا قيدها بالسجدة فسدت صلاة الكل لأن الإمام إذا قعد على الرابعة تمت صلاته في حق المسبوق فلا يجوز للمسبوق متابعته، ولو نسي أحد المسبوقين المتساويين كمية ما عليه فقضى ملاحظاً للآخر بلا اقتداء به صح. ثانيها لو كبر ناوياً للاستئناف يصير مستأنفاً قاطعاً للأولى بخلاف المنفرد على ما يأتي. ثالثها لو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وعلى الإمام سجدتا سهو قبل أن يدخل معه كان عليه أن يعود فيسجد معه ما لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة، فإن لم يعد حتى سجد يمضي وعليه أن يسجد في آخر صلاته بخلاف المنفرد لا يجب عليه السجود السهو غيره رابعها يأتي بتكبير التشريق اتفاقاً بخلاف المنفرد لا يجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة، وفيما سوى ذلك هو منفرد لعدم المشاركة فيما يقضيه حقيقة وحكماً.

ومن أحكامه أنه لو سلم مع الإمام ساهياً أو قبله لا يلزمه سجود السهو لأنه مقتد، وإن سلم بعده لزمه، وإن سلم مع الإمام على ظن أن عليه السلام مع الإمام فهو سلام عمد فتفسد. كذا في الظهيرية. ومن أحكامه أنه لا يقوم إلى القضاء قبل التسليمتين بل ينتظر فراغ الإمام بعدهما لإحتمال سهو على الإمام فيصبر حتى يفهم أنه لا سهو عليه إذ لو كان لسجد. وقيده في فتح القدير بحثاً بأن محله ما إذا اقتدى بمن يرى سجود السهو بعد السلام، أما إذا اقتدى بمن يراه قبله فلا . قلت : الخلاف بین الأئمة إنما هو في الأولوية فربما اختار الإمام الشافعي أن يسجد بعد السلام عملاً بالجائز فلهذا أطلقوا استنظاره. ومن أحكامه أنه لا يقوم المسبوق قبل السلام بعد قدر التشهد إلا في مواضع إذا خاف وهو ماسح تمام المدة لو انتظر سلام الإمام أو خاف المسبوق في الجمعة والعيدين والفجر أو المعذور خروج الوقت أو خاف أن يبتدره الحدث أو أن تمر الناس بين يديه ولو قام في غيرها بعد قدر التشهد صح ويكره تحريماً لأن المتابعة واجبة بالنص . قال عليه السلام إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه (۱) وهذه المخالفة له إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المفيدة للوجوب . ولو قام قبله قال في النوازل : إن قرأ بعد فراغ الإمام من التشهد ما تجوز به الصلاة جاز وإلا فلا. هذا في المسبوق بركعة أو ركعتين فإن كان بثلاث فإن وجد منه قيام بعد التشهد الإمام جاز وإن يقرأ لأنه سيقرأ في الباقيتين والقراءة فرض في كل الركعتين ولو قام حيث يصح وفرغ قبل سلام الإمام وتابعه في السلام ؛ قيل تفسدو الفتوى على أن لا تفسدو إن كان اقتداؤه بعد المفارقة مفسداً لأن هذا مفسد بعد الفراغ فهو كتعمد الحدث في هذه الحالة. أحكامه أن ومن الإمام لو تذكر سجدة فإما تلاوية أو صلبية، فإن كانت تلاوية وسجدها إن لم يقيد المسبوق ركعته بسجدة فإنه يرفض ذلك ويتابعه ويسجد معه للسهو ثم يقوم إلى القضاء ولو لم يعد فسدت صلاته لأن عود الإمام إلى سجود التلاوة يرفع القعدة وهو بعد لم يصر منفرداً لأن ما أتى به دون ركعة فيرتفض في حقه أيضاً، وإذا ارتفضت لا يجوز له الانفراد لأن هذا أوان افتراض المتابعة والانفراد في هذه الحالة مفسد للصلاة، ولو تابعه بعد تقييدها بالسجدة فيها فسدت رواية واحدة، وإن لم يتابعه فظاهر الرواية كما في المحيط الفساد، وفي الظهيرية وهو أصح الروايتين لأن ارتفاضها في حق الإمام لا يظهر في حق المسبوق. ولو تذكر الإمام سجدة صلبية وعاد إليها يتابعه وإن لم يتابعه فسدت وإن كان قيد ركعته بالسجدة تفسد في عدم الرملي : يعني أنه لا يعتد بقيام المسبوق قبل فراغ الإمام من التشهد فكأنه قبل فراغه منه لم يقم، وبعد فراغه يعتبر قائماً حتى ، إذا وجد جزء قليل من قيام بعد فراغه منه جاوز وإن لم يقرأ لأنه سيقرأ في الباقيتين وإلا أي وإن لم يوجد ذلك لا يجوز والله أعلم .اهـ. وأوضح المسألة أيضاً في شرح المنية من سجود السهو. قوله : ( وإن كان اقتداؤه بعد المفارقة مفسداً (الخ) هذا صريح في أنه لو اقتدى به بعد المفارقة قبل الفراغ تفسد صلاته تأمل. ولعل مراد القول الأول فساد ما بقي وما مضى، ومراد الثاني لا يفسد ما مضى ويفسد ما بقي ولكن القول الأول مشكل لأن فرض المسألة أنه تابعه في السلام فقط وذلك بعد فراغه وتلك المتابعة فعل عمد فإفسادها ما مضى لا وجه له تأمل. قوله: (ولو لم يعد فسدت صلاته كذا أطلقه في الفتح، لكن في الذخيرة أنه لو لم يتابع الإمام ينظر إن وجد منه القيام والقراءة بعد فراغ الإمام من القعدة الثانية مقدار ما تجوز به الصلاة جازت صلاته وإلا فلا، لأن بعود إمامه إلى سجود التلاوة ارتفعت القعدة فصار كأنه قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به قبل فراغ الإمام من
The following of the masbuq: if his imam breaks wudu and appoints him as successor, his appointment becomes valid and he becomes imam... (continues with detailed rulings on masbuq's following, sajdah sahw, salam, standing before imam's taslim, imam remembering sajdah, etc.).
Source pages p. 662

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the rulings specific to the masbuq (latecomer) in congregational prayer. The author first discusses the scenario where the imam thinks he has made a mistake and performs sajdah sahw, and the masbuq follows him, then it turns out there was no mistake. There are two narrations: the more famous one says the masbuq's prayer is invalid because he followed in a place where he should have been independent; Abu al-Layth said it is not invalid due to common ignorance. Then the text lists four specific rules where the masbuq differs from the munfarid: 1) if he intends isti'naf (renewal) with takbir, he becomes musta'nif; 2) if he stands for qada' while the imam still owes sajdah sahw, he must return and follow unless he has tied the rak'ah with a sajdah; 3) he must perform takbir tashriq if applicable; 4) otherwise, he is like a munfarid in his qada'. Then follow rulings on salam: if he salam with or before the imam forgetfully, no sajdah sahw; if after, it is required; if deliberately with the imam, invalid. Then the ruling that the masbuq should not stand for qada' before the imam's two taslims, waiting to see if there is sahw, except he may stand early in certain cases (fear of time expiring, event, people passing, etc.). The text cites the hadith: 'The imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' It is makruh tahriman to stand before the imam finishes tashahhud. The final section deals with the imam remembering a sajdah (tilawah or salbiyyah). If it is tilawah and the masbuq has not tied his rak'ah, he must abandon his qada' and follow the imam, then perform sajdah sahw. If he does not follow, his prayer is invalid. If he has tied the rak'ah, there is a difference: one narration says invalid, another says not. The relied-upon view (as in al-Zahira) is that it is not invalid because the imam's abandonment does not affect the masbuq. For a salbiyyah sajdah, the same rule applies. The commentary ends with a discussion of whether the masbuq's prayer is considered 'after separation' (mufaraqah) and some details from al-Fath and al-Dhakhira.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer in congregational prayer who joins after the imam has already started and must complete missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, either before or after salam.
روايتان (riwayatan): Two narrations or versions of a ruling, often indicating a difference of opinion within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the masbuq's prayer if he follows the imam in sajdah sahw that later turns out to be mistaken?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but the masbuq must perform sajdah sahw again
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed
D) The prayer is invalid only if the masbuq had tied his rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's prayer is not invalid if he follows the imam's mistaken sajdah sahw according to the mufta bihi view.

Salah — Prayer

The Masbuq Standing for Qada' Before the Imam's Taslim: Rules and Proof
Commentary on masbuq rulings from Kanz al-Daqaiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general prohibition against the masbuq standing before the imam's taslim, list the exceptions, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The masbuq must wait for the imam's two taslims before standing; early standing is makruh tahriman unless excused.

This lesson covers a crucial adab of the masbuq: he should not stand to complete his missed rak'ahs until the imam has finished both salams, unless specific excuses exist. The hadith 'la takhtalifu' is the proof. We also examine the interaction with the imam's sajdah sahw timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the masbuq standing for qada' before the imam completes his two taslims. The ruling is makruh tahriman if done without excuse.
Standing after the imam's first salam but before the second is also included.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'innama ju'ila al-imam li yu'tamma bihi' and 'la takhtalifu alayhi' is explicitly cited as proof for the obligation of following.
The text states: 'لأن المتابعة واجبة بالنص' (because followership is wajib by textual proof).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'li yu'tamma bihi' indicates that following is the purpose of the imam; 'la takhtalifu' prohibits differing, implying obligation until the imam completes.
Wajh: the prohibition of differing extends to all actions until the end of the prayer, including the taslim.
4
Note the exceptions
The text lists exceptions: fear of time expiring (especially in Jumu'ah, Eid, Fajr), fear of passing people, fear of hadath, or if the masbuq is a mas-hur (someone with a continuous excuse).
These exceptions allow early standing without makruh.
5
Note the cross-madhhab aspect
The text mentions that if the imam follows the Shafi'i view of sajdah sahw after salam, the masbuq should wait accordingly; the difference is in priority, not obligation.
This affects when the masbuq considers the imam 'finished'.

Source Text

الاقتداء بالمسبوق أن إمامه لو أحدث فاستخلفه استخلافه وصار إماماً اهـ. وهو صح لأنه سهو كلامهم فيما إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به وهو في هذه الحالة لا الاقتداء أصلاً فلا استثناء. ولو ظن الإمام أن عليه سهواً فسجد للسهو فتابعه المسبوق فيه ثم علم أنه ليس عليه سهو ففيه روايتان والأشهر أن صلاة المسبوق تفسد لأنه اقتدى في موضع الانفراد. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث في زماننا لا تفسد لأن الجهل في القراء غالب كذا الظهيرية. ولو لم يعلم لم تفسد في قولهم كذا في الخانية. ولو قام الإمام إلى الخامسة في صلاة الظهر فتابعه المسبوق إن قعد الإمام على رأس الرابعة تفسد صلاة المسبوق، وإن لم يقعد لم تفسد حتى يقيد الخامسة بالسجدة فإذا قيدها بالسجدة فسدت صلاة الكل لأن الإمام إذا قعد على الرابعة تمت صلاته في حق المسبوق فلا يجوز للمسبوق متابعته، ولو نسي أحد المسبوقين المتساويين كمية ما عليه فقضى ملاحظاً للآخر بلا اقتداء به صح. ثانيها لو كبر ناوياً للاستئناف يصير مستأنفاً قاطعاً للأولى بخلاف المنفرد على ما يأتي. ثالثها لو قام لقضاء ما سبق به وعلى الإمام سجدتا سهو قبل أن يدخل معه كان عليه أن يعود فيسجد معه ما لم يقيد الركعة بسجدة، فإن لم يعد حتى سجد يمضي وعليه أن يسجد في آخر صلاته بخلاف المنفرد لا يجب عليه السجود السهو غيره رابعها يأتي بتكبير التشريق اتفاقاً بخلاف المنفرد لا يجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة، وفيما سوى ذلك هو منفرد لعدم المشاركة فيما يقضيه حقيقة وحكماً.

ومن أحكامه أنه لو سلم مع الإمام ساهياً أو قبله لا يلزمه سجود السهو لأنه مقتد، وإن سلم بعده لزمه، وإن سلم مع الإمام على ظن أن عليه السلام مع الإمام فهو سلام عمد فتفسد. كذا في الظهيرية. ومن أحكامه أنه لا يقوم إلى القضاء قبل التسليمتين بل ينتظر فراغ الإمام بعدهما لإحتمال سهو على الإمام فيصبر حتى يفهم أنه لا سهو عليه إذ لو كان لسجد. وقيده في فتح القدير بحثاً بأن محله ما إذا اقتدى بمن يرى سجود السهو بعد السلام، أما إذا اقتدى بمن يراه قبله فلا . قلت : الخلاف بین الأئمة إنما هو في الأولوية فربما اختار الإمام الشافعي أن يسجد بعد السلام عملاً بالجائز فلهذا أطلقوا استنظاره. ومن أحكامه أنه لا يقوم المسبوق قبل السلام بعد قدر التشهد إلا في مواضع إذا خاف وهو ماسح تمام المدة لو انتظر سلام الإمام أو خاف المسبوق في الجمعة والعيدين والفجر أو المعذور خروج الوقت أو خاف أن يبتدره الحدث أو أن تمر الناس بين يديه ولو قام في غيرها بعد قدر التشهد صح ويكره تحريماً لأن المتابعة واجبة بالنص . قال عليه السلام إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه (۱) وهذه المخالفة له إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المفيدة للوجوب . ولو قام قبله قال في النوازل : إن قرأ بعد فراغ الإمام من التشهد ما تجوز به الصلاة جاز وإلا فلا. هذا في المسبوق بركعة أو ركعتين فإن كان بثلاث فإن وجد منه قيام بعد التشهد الإمام جاز وإن يقرأ والانفراد في هذه الحالة مفسد للصلاة، ولو تابعه بعد تقييدها بالسجدة فيها فسدت رواية واحدة، وإن لم يتابعه فظاهر الرواية كما في المحيط الفساد، وفي الظهيرية وهو أصح الروايتين لأن ارتفاضها في حق الإمام لا Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer in congregational prayer who joins after the imam has already started and must complete missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.
قدر التشهد (qadr al-tashahhud): The minimum time needed to recite the tashahhud (at-tahiyyat) in the final sitting.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, either before or after salam.

In which of the following situations is it permissible for the masbuq to stand for qada' before the imam's taslim?

Salah — Prayer
advanced

Masbuq and Imam’s Recall of Sajdah: Obligation to Follow
Explains obligations of a masbuq regarding sajdah tilawah and salbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a masbuq when the imam recalls a sajdah (tilawah or salbiyah) and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement on the consequence of not following.

Core Idea
The masbuq must follow the imam in sajdah tilawah and salbiyah; failure invalidates in zahir al-riwaya but not in the sounder narration.

In congregational prayer, when the imam remembers a sajdah—whether the wajib sajdah tilawah or the rukn sajdah salbiyah—the masbuq (latecomer) faces a complex situation. The general principle is that following the imam (mutaba'ah) is wajib based on the hadith, but the specific rulings differ between the two types of sajdah. This lesson unpacks the obligations and the intra-Hanafi debate on whether failure to follow invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of sajdah
Distinguish between sajdah tilawah (wajib, not a pillar) and sajdah salbiyah (rukn, an integral part of the prayer). The ruling for the masbuq differs based on this distinction.
Sajdah tilawah is wajib in prayer; sajdah salbiyah is fard.
2
State the obligation to follow
For both sajdahs, the imam's recall triggers an obligation on the masbuq to follow. This is based on the hadith 'The imam is appointed only to be followed.'
The hadith is cited in the source: إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ فَلَا تَخْتَلِفُوا عَلَيْهِ
3
Analyze the consequence of not following in sajdah tilawah
According to zahir al-riwaya, if the masbuq does not follow in sajdah tilawah, his prayer is invalid. However, there is a sounder narration (al-Zahiriyyah) that it is not invalid because the imam's invalidation does not affect the masbuq.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The text states al-Zahiriyyah is 'asahh al-riwayatayn'.
4
Analyze the consequence of not following in sajdah salbiyah
For sajdah salbiyah, failure to follow invalidates the prayer in all narrations. This is because it is a rukn, and the masbuq would be separating from the imam with two pillars upon him (sajdah and sitting).
The source says: 'ولو تذكر الإمام سجدة صلبية وعاد إليها يتابعه وإن لم يتابعه فسدت'
5
Apply the mufta bihi and note the thamarah
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the masbuq must follow in both cases; not following in sajdah tilawah invalidates according to the cautious view, though the sounder narration allows validity. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the masbuq must repeat his prayer.
The source indicates that the fatwa follows the more cautious view of invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاف أن يبتدره الحدث أو أن تمر الناس بين يديه ولو قام في غيرها بعد قدر التشهد صح ويكره تحريماً لأن المتابعة واجبة بالنص . قال عليه السلام إنما جعل الإمام ليؤتم به فلا تختلفوا عليه» (۱) وهذه المخالفة له إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المفيدة للوجوب . ولو قام قبله قال في النوازل : إن قرأ بعد فراغ الإمام من التشهد ما تجوز به الصلاة جاز وإلا فلا. هذا في المسبوق بركعة أو ركعتين فإن كان بثلاث فإن وجد منه قيام بعد التشهد الإمام جاز وإن يقرأ لأنه سيقرأ في الباقيتين والقراءة فرض في كل الركعتين ولو قام حيث يصح وفرغ قبل سلام الإمام وتابعه في السلام ؛ قيل تفسدو الفتوى على أن لا تفسدو إن كان اقتداؤه بعد المفارقة مفسداً لأن هذا مفسد بعد الفراغ فهو كتعمد الحدث في هذه الحالة. الرملي : يعني أنه لا يعتد بقيام المسبوق قبل فراغ الإمام من التشهد فكأنه قبل فراغه منه لم يقم، وبعد فراغه يعتبر قائماً حتى ، إذا وجد جزء قليل من قيام بعد فراغه منه جاوز وإن لم يقرأ لأنه سيقرأ في الباقيتين وإلا أي وإن لم يوجد ذلك لا يجوز والله أعلم .اهـ. وأوضح المسألة أيضاً في شرح المنية من سجود السهو. قوله : ( وإن كان اقتداؤه بعد المفارقة مفسداً (الخ) هذا صريح في أنه لو اقتدى به بعد المفارقة قبل الفراغ تفسد صلاته تأمل. ولعل مراد القول الأول فساد ما بقي وما مضى، ومراد الثاني لا يفسد ما مضى ويفسد ما بقي ولكن القول الأول مشكل لأن فرض المسألة أنه تابعه في السلام فقط وذلك بعد فراغه وتلك المتابعة فعل عمد فإفسادها ما مضى لا وجه له تأمل. قوله: (ولو لم يعد فسدت صلاته كذا أطلقه في الفتح، لكن في الذخيرة أنه لو لم يتابع الإمام ينظر إن وجد منه القيام والقراءة بعد فراغ الإمام من القعدة الثانية مقدار ما تجوز به الصلاة جازت صلاته وإلا فلا، لأن بعود إمامه إلى سجود التلاوة ارتفعت القعدة فصار كأنه قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به قبل فراغ الإمام من (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الصلاة باب ۱۸ مسلم في كتاب الصلاة حديث ٧٧، ٨٢، ٨٦. أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب .٦٨ الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب ١٥۰ النسائي في كتاب الأئمة باب ١٦، ٣٨. الموطأ في كتاب النداء حديث ٥٧. أحمد في مسنده (٢٣٠/٢، ٣٠٤). أحكامه أن ومن الإمام لو تذكر سجدة فإما تلاوية أو صلبية، فإن كانت تلاوية وسجدها إن لم يقيد المسبوق ركعته بسجدة فإنه يرفض ذلك ويتابعه ويسجد معه للسهو ثم يقوم إلى القضاء ولو لم يعد فسدت صلاته لأن عود الإمام إلى سجود التلاوة يرفع القعدة وهو بعد لم يصر منفرداً لأن ما أتى به دون ركعة فيرتفض في حقه أيضاً، وإذا ارتفضت لا يجوز له الانفراد لأن هذا أوان افتراض المتابعة والانفراد في هذه الحالة مفسد للصلاة، ولو تابعه بعد تقييدها بالسجدة فيها فسدت رواية واحدة، وإن لم يتابعه فظاهر الرواية كما في المحيط الفساد، وفي الظهيرية وهو أصح الروايتين لأن ارتفاضها في حق الإمام لا يظهر في حق المسبوق. ولو تذكر الإمام سجدة صلبية وعاد إليها يتابعه وإن لم يتابعه فسدت وإن كان قيد ركعته بالسجدة تفسد في عدم الروايات كلها عاد أو لم يعد لأنه انفرد وعليه ركنان - السجدة والقعدة ـ وهو عاجز عن متابعته بعد إكمال الركعة، والأصل أنه إذا اقتدى في موضع الانفراد أو انفرد في موضع الاقتداء تفسد .
If he fears that a hadath (ritual impurity) might overcome him or that people might pass in front of him, and if he stands in other than that (i.e., for a valid reason) after the extent of the tashahhud, it is valid but makruh tahriman, because following (the imam) is obligatory by textual proof. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is appointed only to be followed, so do not differ with him.' And this differing with him, and other ahadith, indicate obligation. If he stood before that (the imam's tashahhud), it is said in al-Nawazil: If he recited after the imam finished the tashahhud what would make the prayer valid, it is permitted; otherwise not. This is for the masbuq who missed one or two rak'ahs. If he missed three, then if he stood after the imam's tashahhud, it is permitted even if he does not recite because he will recite in the remaining two, and recitation is fard in every two rak'ahs. And if he stood when it is valid and finished before the imam's salam and followed him in salam, it was said: it invalidates according to the fatwa, but also that it does not invalidate if his following after separation was invalidating, because this is an invalidating act after completion, so it is like intentionally causing a hadath in this state. Al-Ramli: This means that the masbuq's standing before the imam finishes the tashahhud is not considered, so it is as if he did not stand before that; after he finishes, he is considered standing, so if a small part of standing is found after his finishing, it passes even if he does not recite because he will recite in the remaining two. Otherwise, i.e., if that is not found, it is not permitted. And Allah knows best. End. He also clarified the issue in Sharh al-Munyah from Sujud al-Sahw. His statement: (And if his following after separation was invalidating, etc.) This clearly indicates that if he followed him after separation before completion, his prayer is invalid - consider. Perhaps the meaning of the first statement is invalidation of what remains and what passed, and the meaning of the second is that what passed is not invalidated but what remains is invalidated. But the first statement is problematic because the assumption is that he followed him only in salam, and that was after his completion, and that following is an intentional act, so invalidating what passed has no basis - consider. His statement: (And if he did not return, his prayer is invalidated) Thus it is absolute in al-Fath, but in al-Dhakhirah: if he did not follow the imam, look: if he stood and recited after the imam finished the second sitting to the extent that would make the prayer valid, his prayer is valid; otherwise not, because by his imam's return to the sajdah tilawah, the sitting was lifted, so it is as if he stood to make up what he was preceded by before the imam finished. (1) Narrated by Bukhari in Kitab al-Salah, Bab 18; Muslim in Kitab al-Salah, Hadith 77, 82, 86; Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Salah, Bab 68; Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Salah, Bab 150; Nasa'i in Kitab al-A'imma, Bab 16, 38; Muwatta in Kitab al-Nida', Hadith 57; Ahmad in his Musnad, 2/230, 304. Its rulings: And from them: if the imam recalls a sajdah, either tilawah or salbiyah. If it is tilawah and he performs it, if the masbuq has not tied his rak'ah with a sajdah, then he discards that (his own action) and follows him, and prostrates with him for sahw (forgetfulness), then stands to make up. And if he did not return (to following), his prayer is invalidated because the imam's return to the sajdah tilawah lifts the sitting, and he has not yet become separate (munfarid) because what he performed is less than a rak'ah, so it is also invalidated for him. And if it is invalidated, he is not permitted to separate because this is the time when following is obligatory, and separation in this state invalidates the prayer. And if he followed him after tying his rak'ah with a sajdah, it invalidates in one narration. And if he did not follow him, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) as in al-Muhit is that it is invalid. In al-Zahiriyyah, it is the sounder of the two narrations because its invalidation (irtifad) in the imam's case does not appear for the masbuq. And if the imam recalls a salbiyah sajdah and returns to it, he follows him; if he does not follow, it is invalid. And if he tied his rak'ah with a sajdah, it invalidates in all narrations whether he returned or not, because he separated and has two pillars upon him - the sajdah and the sitting - and he is unable to follow him after completing the rak'ah. The principle is: if he follows in a place of separation or separates in a place of following, it invalidates.
Source pages p. 663

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a detailed set of rulings concerning a masbuq (latecomer) in congregational prayer. It begins by addressing the situation where the masbuq stands up to complete his missed rak'ahs before the imam has finished the final tashahhud. The ruling is that this is permissible but makruh tahriman, because following the imam is wajib based on the hadith 'The imam is appointed only to be followed.' If the masbuq stands before the imam finishes tashahhud, the view from al-Nawazil is that it is only valid if he recites after the imam finishes enough to make the prayer valid; otherwise not. The passage then differentiates between missing one, two, or three rak'ahs. The core of the lesson concerns what happens when the imam remembers a sajdah (prostration) during the prayer: either a sajdah tilawah (recitation prostration, which is wajib) or a sajdah salbiyah (part of the prayer, a rukn). For sajdah tilawah, if the imam returns to perform it, the masbuq must follow him if he has not yet tied his own rak'ah with a sajdah. If he does not follow, his prayer is invalid according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), but there is a sounder narration in al-Zahiriyyah that it does not invalidate because the imam's invalidation does not affect the masbuq. For sajdah salbiyah, the masbuq must follow; failure to do so invalidates his prayer in all narrations because sajdah salbiyah is a pillar (rukn), and the masbuq becomes separated from the imam with two pillars upon him. The passage concludes with the legal principle that following in a place of separation or separating in a place of following invalidates the prayer. The commentary also includes clarifications by al-Ramli and references from al-Fath and al-Dhakhirah regarding the validity of the masbuq's prayer if he does not follow.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs with the imam.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran during prayer.
سجدة صلبية (sajdah salbiyah): A prostration that is an integral part of the prayer (rukn), such as the sajdah in each rak'ah.
متابعة (mutāba‘ah): Following the imam in actions such as standing, bowing, prostrating, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a masbuq who does not follow the imam when the imam returns to perform sajdah salbiyah?
A) His prayer is invalid in all narrations.
B) His prayer is valid if he recites enough Quran.
C) His prayer is valid according to the sounder narration.
D) His prayer is makruh tahriman but valid.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must follow the imam in both sajdah tilawah and sajdah salbiyah; failure to follow in sajdah salbiyah always invalidates, while in sajdah tilawah there is an intra-Hanafi dispute, but the cautious ruling is invalidation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Masbuq's Makeup: First or Last?
Explains dispute between Sahibayn and Muhammad on whether masbuq's first prayer is with imam or after

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on whether the masbuq's makeup prayer is his first or last, and apply the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) to a specific scenario.

Core Idea
The masbuq's makeup is his first prayer except for recitation—a nuanced Hanafi rule requiring careful sequencing.

When you join the prayer late as a masbuq, the rak'ahs you make up after the imam’s salam are not simply a continuation. The Hanafi school has a detailed dispute about their order: are they your first or last rak'ahs? This lesson unpacks the intra-madhhab disagreement between the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad, and shows how the difference affects the sequence of recitation and tashahhud. You will learn to apply the mufta bihi view to real prayer scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The fundamental question: Are the rak'ahs that the masbuq makes up after the imam considered his first or last prayer (in terms of order)? This affects where tashahhud falls and whether he recites a surah.
Remember: the masbuq's prayer with the imam counts as part of his own prayer.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn), what the masbuq makes up is his first prayer, except for recitation and qunut, which are considered as his last. This means that the first rak'ah of his makeup is like a second rak'ah in terms of tashahhud, but he still recites surah.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
State Muhammad's alternative position
In a narration from Imam Muhammad, what the masbuq prays with the imam is his first prayer, and what he makes up is his last. Therefore, he should sit for tashahhud earlier and recite surah only in the first makeup rak'ah.
This view is considered weak by later Hanafis.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Compare the two orders for a masbuq who missed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer. Under Sahibayn: surah, surah + tashahhud, then Fatihah only + final tashahhud. Under Muhammad: surah + tashahhud, then two rak'ahs with Fatihah only + final tashahhud. The difference is in when tashahhud occurs and how many surah recitations.
This example is explicitly given in the text.
5
Note the tarjih and why
Later Hanafi authorities (al-Zayla'i, Sheikh Ismail) affirm that the mufta bihi is the view of al-Sahibayn. The anecdote of Yahya is cited as support for Muhammad's personal opinion but is not relied upon for fatwa.
Know that the 'zahir al-riwayah' position is that of the Sahibayn.

Its rulings: And among them: He (the masbuq) makes up the first part of his prayer with respect to recitation and the last part with respect to tashahhud, such that if he caught one rak'ah of Maghrib with the imam, then he recites al-Fatihah and a surah in both (missed) rak'ahs, and if he abandons recitation in one of them, his prayer is invalid. And he must make up one rak'ah with tashahhud because it is his second, and if he abandons (tashahhud), it is valid by istihsan not by qiyas. And if he catches one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer, he must make up one rak'ah reciting al-Fatihah and a surah with tashahhud because he makes up the last part with respect to tashahhud, and (then) he makes up a rak'ah reciting likewise without tashahhud, and in the third he has a choice with recitation being better. And if he catches two rak'ahs, he makes up two rak'ahs reciting in them and with tashahhud, and if he abandons in one of them, it is invalid. And among its rulings: If he begins making up what he missed, in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa it is disliked because... the tashahhud. End. Summarized. And such was not mentioned for the sajdah al-salbiyah because it itself is a pillar of the prayer, so not following in it is invalidating, unlike sajdah al-tilawah because it is wajib not a pillar. Consider his statement: (He makes up the first part of his prayer etc.) What he mentioned following al-Fath and al-Durar is the statement of Muhammad (rahimahullah). He said in al-Siraj: When the masbuq stands to make up, what he makes up is the first part of his prayer in ruling according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: It is the last part except with respect to recitation and qunut, so that he recites the opening supplication (istiftah) in what he makes up. And according to Muhammad, he recites istiftah when he enters with the imam, and the difference does not appear in recitation and qunut, such that if he caught the third of witr and performed qunut with the imam, he does not perform qunut in what he makes up by consensus. Its explanation: If he missed three rak'ahs, then when the imam says salam, he stands and prays one rak'ah with Fatihah and a surah, then stands without tashahhud and prays another with Fatihah and a surah, then sits and recites tashahhud, then stands and prays another with Fatihah only, then recites tashahhud and says salam. This is according to them (Sahibayn). And Muhammad said: He makes up one rak'ah with Fatihah and a surah, sits and recites tashahhud, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with Fatihah only, then recites tashahhud and says salam. It is narrated that Yahya al-Bakka', who was a companion of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (rahimahullah), asked Muhammad about the masbuq: does he make up the first part of his prayer or the last? Muhammad said: In the ruling of recitation and qunut, it is the last; with respect to the sitting (qada), it is the first. Yayha said mockingly: This is an inverted prayer! Muhammad said: You will not succeed. And it happened that all his companions succeeded and Yahya did not. End. Sheikh Ismail said: But in Salat al-Jallab, it implies that the statement that what the author mentioned is the statement of Muhammad is weak, and that it is the statement of the two (Sahibayn), which is what al-Zayla'i affirmed. His statement: (And he must make up one rak'ah with tashahhud) means the first rak'ah of the two rak'ahs. He said in Sharh al-Munyah: Even if he caught one rak'ah of Maghrib with the imam, he recites Fatihah and a surah in the two rak'ahs and sits in the first of them because it is his second, and if he does not sit, it is valid by istihsan not by qiyas, and no sajdat al-sahw is required even if forgetfully because it is the first from one perspective. End. And what al-Ayni narrated from al-Mabsut does not contradict it that this is istihsan and the qiyas is that he prays two rak'ahs then sits. The face (argument)...
Source pages p. 664

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a key issue in Hanafi fiqh regarding the masbuq (one who joins the prayer late): whether the rak'ahs he prays after the imam's salam are considered his first or last prayer (i.e., in terms of order). The dispute is between the two primary disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, known as al-Sahibayn) and Imam Muhammad in some narrations. According to al-Sahibayn, what the masbuq makes up after the imam is his first prayer in ruling, except that for recitation and qunut, it is his last. According to one view attributed to Muhammad, what he prays with the imam is his first, and what he makes up is his last, except that for recitation he does istiftah in the qada. The practical consequence appears in the order of tashahhud: if a masbuq misses three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, under the Sahibayn's view he would pray one rak'ah with surah, then another with surah, then sit for tashahhud (because that second rak'ah is his second overall with tashahhud), then stand and pray the final rak'ah without surah and then final tashahhud. Under Muhammad's view, he would pray one rak'ah with surah and tashahhud, then two rak'ahs with only Fatihah and then tashahhud. The passage includes an anecdote where Yahya al-Bakka' asked Muhammad and was rebuked. The author also notes that some later scholars (like Sheikh Ismail) consider the view attributed to Muhammad as weak, and the correct position is that of al-Sahibayn. The passage also provides detailed rulings for specific cases by number of missed rak'ahs, including the rule that if the masbuq catches one rak'ah of Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with Surah and sits in the first of them (since it is his second rak'ah), but if he omits the sitting, it is valid by istihsan. The commentary emphasizes the distinction between sajdah tilawah (wajib) and sajdah salbiyah (rukn) regarding following the imam.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the imam late and misses some rak'ahs of the prayer.
قضاء (qada'): The rak'ahs that the masbuq prays after the imam's salam to complete his prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): A Hanafi method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more suitable ruling.
صاحبين (al-sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two foremost students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, if a masbuq misses three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, how should he make them up?
A) He prays one rak'ah with Fatihah and surah, then one with Fatihah and surah with tashahhud, then one with Fatihah only with tashahhud.
B) He prays one rak'ah with Fatihah and surah with tashahhud, then two rak'ahs with Fatihah only with tashahhud.
C) He prays one rak'ah with Fatihah and surah without tashahhud, then one with Fatihah and surah with tashahhud, then one with Fatihah only with final tashahhud.
D) He prays three rak'ahs each with Fatihah and surah with tashahhud at the end.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's makeup is considered his first prayer (except for recitation) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, determining the sequence of surah and tashahhud.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Masbuq's Qada: First or Last Prayer?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on masbuq's qada order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Sahibayn and Muhammad on the masbuq's qada and apply the mufta bihi view to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The masbuq's qada is the first part of his prayer according to Sahibayn, but the last part according to Muhammad.

Praying behind an imam can be complex when you join late. One key issue is whether the rak'ahs you make up are considered the beginning or the end of your prayer. This lesson examines the internal Hanafi disagreement between Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan on this very point. We will explore the practical consequences and see why the view of Sahibayn is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school
State the views of Sahibayn and Muhammad regarding whether the masbuq's qada is the first or last part of his prayer.
Sahibayn: qada is the first part. Muhammad: qada is the last except for recitation and qunut.
2
Understand the methodological basis
Analyze how each position uses qiyas and istihsan. Sahibayn rely on istihsan for the sitting, while Muhammad holds to strict qiyas.
Istihsan is a Hanafi principle that allows leniency.
3
Apply the positions to a concrete scenario
Take a masbuq who catches one rak'ah of Maghrib. Work out the required actions under each view.
Focus on recitation and sitting for tashahhud.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical differences in prayer structure between the two views.
The key difference is when the tashahhud occurs.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Ascertain which view is considered the sounder (zahir al-riwayah) and is relied upon for fatwa, citing authorities like al-Zayla'i.
The majority of later Hanafi scholars prefer Sahibayn's view.

والقنوت حتى لو أدرك ثالثة الوتر فقنت مع الإمام لا يقنت فيما يقضي بالإجماع. وفي الوجيز ما أدركه المسبوق مع الإمام فهو آخر صلاة المسبوق، وما يقضيه بعد فراغ الإمام فهو أول صلاته عندهما. وقال محمد ما صلاه
