Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Imam's Hadath and the Masbuq: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadath's effect on masbuq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether the masbuq's prayer is invalidated by the imam's hadath after the final sitting, and evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred view).

Core Idea
Hadath nullifies the part of prayer it touches; thus building on a null part is impossible.

One of the key intra-Hanafi disputes concerns the effect of the imam's hadath (ritual impurity) on the prayer of a masbuq. If the imam, after sitting for the final tashahhud, experiences hadath, does this invalidate the masbuq's prayer? Abu Hanifa held that it does, because hadath corrupts the corresponding part of the masbuq's prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagreed, drawing an analogy to the imam's speech or leaving the mosque, which do not invalidate. This lesson unpacks their arguments and the preferred Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of disagreement
The dispute is about the effect of the imam's hadath (after the final sitting) on the masbuq's prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, it invalidates the masbuq's prayer. According to the Sahibayn, it does not.
The imam's hadath after sitting for tashahhud does not invalidate his own prayer by consensus, but its effect on the follower is contested.
2
Trace the opposing analogy
The Sahibayn argue by analogy (qiyas) to the imam's speech or leaving the mosque after the final sitting. Since those acts do not invalidate the imam's prayer, and the follower's prayer is 'built on' the imam's, they should not invalidate the follower's either. This is a general analogy: whatever does not harm the imam's prayer should not harm the follower's.
The underlying principle: 'Salat al-muqtadi mabniyya 'ala salat al-imam' – the follower's prayer is built on the imam's in validity and invalidity.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's distinction
Abu Hanifa distinguishes hadath from speech/leaving. Hadath is an internal corruption that nullifies the part of prayer it encounters. Since the masbuq's prayer is built on the imam's, the nullified part in the imam's prayer corrupts the corresponding part in the masbuq's. The masbuq then cannot build on a null part. Speech and leaving, however, are acts of exiting the prayer (munhiyyat), not internal corruptions, so they do not have the same effect.
The key is the nature of the act: hadath is a 'mufsid' (corrupter) while speech/leaving are 'mukhrij' (exiting acts).
4
Determine the tarjih and practical consequence
The Hanafi school adopts Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that according to Abu Hanifa, the masbuq must repeat his prayer if the imam has hadath after the final sitting. According to the Sahibayn, the masbuq's prayer remains valid.
The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, supports Abu Hanifa's distinction and criticizes the analogy of the Sahibayn.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة - باب الحدث في الصلاة
المسبوق فلو أتم صلاة الإمام تفسد بالمنافي صلاته دون القوم كما تفسد بقهقهة إمامه اهـ.
الإقامة والإمام الثاني نوى الإقامة أيضاً ثم جاء الإمام الأول كيف يفعل؟ قال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل: إذا حضر الأوّل يقتدي بالثاني في الذي هو باقي صلاته، فإذا صلى الإمام الثاني الركعة الثانية يقعد قدر التشهد ويستخلف رجلاً مسافراً من الذي أدرك أوّل صلاته حتى يسلم بالقوم ثم يقوم الثاني فيصلي ثلاث ركعات والإمام الأول يصلي ركعتين بعد سلام الإمام الثاني ولا يتغير فرض القوم بنية الإمام الثاني ولا فرض الإمام الأول ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير: وأما اللاحق فإنما يتحقق في حقه تقديم غيره إذا خالف الواجب بأن بدأ بإتمام صلاة الإمام فإنه حينئذ يقدم غيره للإتمام ثم يشتغل بما فاته معه، أما إذا فعل الواجب بأن قدم ما فاته مع الإمام ليقع الأداء مرتباً فيشير إليهم إذا تقدم أن لا يتابعوه فينتظرونه حتى يفرغ مما فاته مع الإمام ثم يتابعونه ويسلم بهم وفيه نظر، بل يتحقق في حقه تقديم الغير مطلقاً لأنه يلزم من فعل الواجب انتظارهم وهو مكروه فلذا إذا تقدم له أن يتأخر ويقدم رجلاً كما في المحيط. وفي الظهيرية : المسبوق يخالف اللاحق في القضاء في ستة أشياء: في محاذاة المرأة، والقراءة، والسهو، والقعدة الأولى إذا تركها الإمام، وفي ضحك الإمام في موضع السلام، وفي نية الإمام الإقامة إذا قيد المسبوق الركعة بسجدة ا هـ. وقد تقدم في بحث المحاذاة شيء من أحكام اللاحق. قوله: (فلو أتم صلاة الإمام تفسد بالمنافي صلاته دون القوم أي لو أتم المسبوق الخليفة صلاة الإمام المحدث فأتى بما ينافي الصلاة من ضحك أو كلام أو خروج من المسجد أو انحراف عن القبلة تفسد صلاته دون صلاة القوم، لأن المفسد في حقه وجد في خلال الصلاة وفي حقهم بعد إتمام أركانها أراد بالقوم المدركين وأما من حاله مثل حاله فصلاته فاسدة لما ذكرنا . ولم يتعرض لصلاة الإمام المحدث لأن فيه اختلافاً والصحيح أنه إن كان فرغ لا تفسد صلاته، وإن لم يفرغ تفسد صلاته لأنه صار مأموماً بالخليفة بعد الخروج من بالقوم قوله : (واستخلف المسبوق) أي المسافر الآخر الذي اقتدى بعدما صلى ركعة. قوله : (ثم يقوم الثاني) أي الإمام الثاني الذي هو خليفة الإمام الأول والمقام مقام إضمار ولكن صرح بالفاعل لئلا يتوهم عود الضمير على الخليفة الثاني المدرك قوله : ( بعد سلام الإمام الثاني) قال الرملي : أي الذي خلفه الخليفة الذي سلم بالقوم. قوله : (ولا) فرض الإمام الأول قال الرملي: صوابه ولا بنية الإمام الأول اهـ. أي لأن المعنى عليه مع أن العبارة في البزازية كذلك قوله : ( وفيه نظر الخ) أقول : عبارة الفتح هكذا : وكما يقدم مدركاً للسلام ولو تقدم كذا الآخران، أما المقيم فلكذا، وأما اللاحق فإنما يتحقق في حقه تقديم غيره .الخ. أي تقديمه للسلام كما هو مبني التفصيل، وهذا أيضاً هو المفهوم من عبارة المؤلف أولاً ومعلوم أن تقديم غيره للسلام ولا يتحقق إلا إذا خالف الواجب فسقط النظر . لدى اختتامه لا بخروجه من المسجد وكلامه ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده توضأ عامداً المسجد، ولذا قالوا: ولو تذكر الخليفة قائتة فسدت صلاة الإمام الأول والثاني والقوم، ولو تذكرها الأول بعد ما خرج من المسجد فسدت صلاته خاصة، أو قبل خروجه فسدت صلاته وصلاة الخليفة والقوم. وقالوا : لو صلى الإمام المحدث ما بقي من صلاته في منزله قبل فراغ هذا المستخلف تفسد صلاته لأن انفراده قبل فراغ الإمام لا يجوز قوله : (كما فسدت بقهقهة إمامه لدى اختتامه لا بخروجه من المسجد وكلامه أي كما تفسد صلاة المسبوق بحدث إمامه بعد القعود قدر التشهد ولا تفسد صلاة المسبوق بخروج إمامه من المسجد وكلامه بعد القعود ولا خلاف في الثاني وخالفا في الأول قياساً على الثاني لأن صلاة المقتدي مبنية على صلاة الإمام صحة وفساداً، ولم تفسد صلاة الإمام اتفاقاً في الكل فكذا المقتدي. وفرق الإمام بأن الحديث مفسد للجزء الذي يلاقيه من صلاة الإمام فيفسد مثله من صلاة المقتدي غير أن الإمام لا يحتاج إلى البناء والمسبوق محتاج إليه والبناء على الفاسد فاسد، بخلاف السلام لأنه منه والكلام في معناه ولهذا لا يخرج المقتدي منها بسلام الإمام وكلامه وخروجه فيسلم ويخرج بحدثه عمداً فلا يسلم بعده قيد بالمسبوق لأن صلاة المدرك لا تفسد اتفاقاً، وفي صلاة اللاحق روايتان، وصحح في السراج الوهاج الفساد، وصحح في الظهيرية عدمه معللاً بأن النائم كأنه خلف الإمام والإمام قد تمت صلاته فكذلك صلاة النائم تقديراً ! وفي نظر، لأن الإمام لم يبق عليه شيء بخلاف اللاحق، وفي فتح القدير: لو كان في القوم لاحق إن فعل الإمام ذلك بعد أن ما فاته قام يقضي وقيد بكونه عند اختتامه لأن الحدث العمد لو حصل قبل القعود بطلت صلاة الكل اتفاقاً . وقيد وافساد المسبوق عنده بما إذا لم يتأكد انفراده، فلو قام قبل سلامه تاركاً للواجب فقضى ركعة فسجد لها ثم فعل الإمام ذلك لا تفسد صلاته لأنه استحكم انفراده حتى لا يسجد لو سجد الإمام لسهو عليه ولا تفسد صلاته لو فسدت صلاة الإمام بعد سجوده قوله: (ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده توضأ وبنى وأعادهما لأن إتمام الركن بالانتقال الحدث لا يتحقق فلا بد من الإعادة أما على قول محمد فظاهر وأما عند أبي يوسف فالسجدة وإن تمت بالوضع لكن الجلسة بين السجدتين فرض عنده ولا تتحقق هي بغير طهارة والانتقال من . مع 6 الإمام هـ. لا تفسد وإلا تفسد عنده . ومع قوله : ( لأنه منه اسم فاعل من أنهى ينهي . قال في العناية : المنهي ما اعتبره الشرع رافعاً للتحريمة عند فراغ الصلاة كالتسليم والخروج بصنع المصلي فإن الشرع اعتبرهما كذلك قال صلى الله عليه وسلم وتحليلها التسليم». وقال الله تعالى فإذا قضيتم الصلاة فانتشروا في الأرض) [الجمعة: ١٠] اهـ . قوله: (وفي فتح القدير لو كان في القوم لاحق الخ قال في النهر : قد سبق أن الإمام الأول إذا لم يفرغ من صلاته وقد أتى المسبوق الخليفة بمنافٍ تفسد صلاته على الراجح مع أنه لاحق، وهذا يعكر على ما في الفتح ويؤيد ما في السراج .
Book of Prayer - Chapter of Event in Prayer. The latecomer (masbuq): if he completes the prayer of the imam, his prayer is invalidated by a nullifier, but not the prayer of the congregation, just as it is invalidated by the laughter of his imam at its conclusion, not by his leaving the mosque or his speech. And if he (the imam) causes hadath in his ruku' or sujud, he performs wudu and builds upon it and repeats them (the rakahs). The iqamah and the second imam also intended the iqamah, then the first imam came; how should he act? Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: When the first (imam) arrives, he should follow the second in what remains of his prayer. When the second imam prays the second rakah, he sits for the amount of tashahhud and appoints a traveler from among those who caught his first prayer, so that he makes taslim with the congregation. Then the second (imam) stands and prays three rakahs, and the first imam prays two rakahs after the salutation of the second imam. The obligation of the congregation does not change by the intention of the second imam, nor the obligation of the first imam. In Fath al-Qadir: As for the lahiq, his appointing another is realized only if he violates the obligatory (wajib) by starting to complete the prayer of the imam; then at that time he appoints another to complete it, then he occupies himself with what he missed with him. But if he does the obligatory by presenting what he missed with the imam so that the performance is in order, he signals to them, if he proceeds, not to follow him; they wait until he finishes what he missed with the imam, then they follow him and he makes taslim with them. And there is consideration in this; rather, his appointing another is realized absolutely because from doing the obligatory results their waiting, which is disliked. Therefore, if he proceeds, he should step back and appoint a man, as in al-Muhit. In al-Zahiriyyah: The masbuq differs from the lahiq in making up (qada') in six things: in aligning with a woman, in recitation, in forgetfulness (sahw), in the first sitting if the imam leaves it, in the imam's laughter in the place of taslim, and in the imam's intention of iqamah if the masbuq ties the rakah with a sajdah. And something of the rulings of the lahiq has preceded in the discussion of alignment. His statement: (If he completes the prayer of the imam, his prayer is invalidated by a nullifier, but not the congregation's) meaning: if the masbuq khalifah completes the prayer of the imam who has hadath and does something contrary to prayer such as laughter, speech, leaving the mosque, or turning away from the qiblah, his prayer is invalidated but not the prayer of the congregation, because the invalidator occurred in his case during the prayer, and in their case after the completion of its pillars. By 'congregation' he means those who caught up (mudrikun). As for one whose state is like his (i.e., another masbuq), his prayer is invalidated. And he did not address the prayer of the imam who had hadath because there is a disagreement; the correct view is that if he (the imam) had finished, his prayer is not invalidated, and if he had not finished, his prayer is invalidated because he becomes a follower of the khalifah after exiting from ... with the congregation. His statement: (And the masbuq appointed) meaning the other traveler who followed after praying one rakah. His statement: (Then the second stands) meaning the second imam who is the khalifah of the first imam; the position is implicit, but he made the agent explicit to avoid misunderstanding that the pronoun refers to the second mudrik khalifah. His statement: (After the taslim of the second imam) al-Ramli said: i.e., the one whom the khalifah who made taslim with the congregation appointed. His statement: (And not) the obligation of the first imam; al-Ramli said: its correct form is 'and not by the intention of the first imam'. i.e., because the meaning is upon it, and the expression in al-Bazzaziyyah is likewise. His statement: (And there is consideration in this, etc.) I say: the expression of al-Fath is: just as he appoints a mudrik for the taslim, and if he proceeds, then the two others. As for the muqim, it is such-and-such. As for the lahiq, his appointing another is realized only ... etc., i.e., his appointing another for the taslim as is built on the detailed discussion. And this is also the understanding from the author's statement first, and it is known that his appointing another for the taslim is realized only if he violates the obligatory, so the consideration falls. At its conclusion, not by his leaving the mosque or his speech. And if he causes hadath in his ruku' or sujud, he performs wudu and builds upon it and repeats them. In the mosque, therefore they said: If the khalifah remembers a missed [something?], the prayer of the first imam, the second, and the congregation is invalidated. If the first (imam) remembers it after leaving the mosque, his prayer alone is invalidated; or before his leaving, his prayer and the prayer of the khalifah and the congregation are invalidated. And they said: If the imam who had hadath prays what remains of his prayer in his home before this appointee finishes, his prayer is invalidated because his being alone before the completion of the imam is not permissible. His statement: (Just as it is invalidated by the laughter of his imam at its conclusion, not by his leaving the mosque or his speech) meaning just as the prayer of the masbuq is invalidated by the hadath of his imam after sitting for the amount of tashahhud, and it is not invalidated by the imam's leaving the mosque or his speech after that sitting. There is no disagreement regarding the second, and they disagreed regarding the first by analogy to the second, because the prayer of the follower is built on the prayer of the imam in validity and invalidity, and the imam's prayer is not invalidated by consensus in all cases, so also the follower. The Imam (Abu Hanifa) distinguished [saying] that hadath invalidates the part it encounters from the imam's prayer, so it invalidates its like from the follower's prayer, except that the imam does not need to rebuild while the masbuq needs to rebuild, and building on something invalid is invalid. This is unlike taslim, because it (taslim) is from its completion, and speech is in its meaning. Therefore, the follower does not exit from it by the imam's taslim, speech, or leaving; rather, he makes taslim and exits by his own deliberate hadath; he does not make taslim after it. He restricted it to the masbuq because the prayer of the mudrik is not invalidated by agreement. Regarding the prayer of the lahiq, there are two narrations. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, he corrected invalidation; in al-Zahiriyyah, he corrected non-invalidation, rationalizing that the sleeper (i.e., the one who missed part) is as if behind the imam, and the imam's prayer is complete, so likewise the sleeper's prayer is estimated as if complete! And there is consideration, because the imam has nothing remaining upon him, unlike the lahiq. In Fath al-Qadir: If there is a lahiq in the congregation, and the imam does that after what he (the lahiq) missed, he (the lahiq) stands and makes up. And he restricted it to being at its conclusion because deliberate hadath if it occurs before the sitting invalidates everyone's prayer by agreement. And he restricted the invalidation of the masbuq in his view to when his being alone is not confirmed. So if he stood before his taslim leaving the wajib and made up a rakah and performed sujud for it, then the imam did that, his prayer is not invalidated because his being alone is established, to the extent that if the imam prostrated for forgetfulness (sahw), he would not prostrate; and his prayer is not invalidated if the imam's prayer becomes invalid after his sujud. His statement: (And if he causes hadath in his ruku' or sujud, he performs wudu and builds upon it and repeats them because the completion of the pillar is not realized by the transition [due to] hadath, so repetition is necessary. As for according to the saying of Muhammad, it is apparent. As for according to Abu Yusuf, although the sajdah is completed by placing, the sitting between the two sajdahs is obligatory according to him, and it is not realized without purity, and the transition from ... With 6 the imam ... not invalidated, otherwise it is invalidated according to him. And with his statement: (Because it is from it) the agent noun from 'anha' yunhi. al-Inayah said: 'al-munhi' is what the Law considers to be a remover of the tahrimah at the end of the prayer, like taslim and exiting by the act of the worshiper, for the Law considers them so. The Prophet said: 'And its tahlil is the taslim.' And Allah said: 'Then when you have completed the prayer, disperse in the land' (62:10). His statement: (And in Fath al-Qadir: If there is a lahiq in the congregation, etc.) al-Nahr said: It has preceded that if the first imam has not finished his prayer and the masbuq khalifah did something contradictory, his prayer is invalidated according to the more correct view, even though he is a lahiq. This contradicts what is in al-Fath and supports what is in al-Siraj.
Source pages p. 666

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqaiq, covering several interconnected rulings about the masbuq (one who joins the congregation after the imam has started) and the lahiq (one who missed part of the prayer but catches up later). The passage opens with the base ruling: if a masbuq acts as khalifah (substitute imam) because the original imam had hadath (event nullifying wudu), and then the khalifah himself does something that nullifies prayer (like laughter, speech, leaving the mosque, or turning from qiblah), only the khalifah's prayer is invalidated, not the congregation's. This is because the nullifier occurred during his prayer, whereas the congregation had already completed the pillars. The text then clarifies that 'congregation' here means those who were present from the start (mudrikun); another masbuq in a similar state would also have his prayer invalidated. The ruling on the original imam's prayer is left ambiguous; the correct view is that if he had already finished (i.e., after taslim), his prayer is not invalidated, but if he hadn't finished, his prayer is invalidated because he becomes a follower of the khalifah. The passage then discusses a scenario with a second imam who gives iqamah and leads, then the first imam returns. According to Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, the first imam follows the second in what remains, and the second imam after two rakahs sits, appoints a traveler to lead the congregation to taslim, then the second imam completes three rakahs and the first completes two. The obligations of the followers do not change. Next, a quote from Fath al-Qadir explains the ruling on a lahiq: he can appoint someone else only if he violates the wajib (i.e., he starts by completing the imam's prayer). If he does the wajib (i.e., first makes up what he missed), he signals the congregation to wait, then leads them in taslim. This is disliked, so it's better for him to step back and appoint another. Then a quote from al-Zahiriyyah lists six differences between a masbuq and a lahiq in the make-up (qada) of prayer: regarding alignment with a woman, recitation, forgetfulness, the first tashahhud, the imam's laughter at taslim, and the imam's intention of iqamah. The commentary then returns to explain the base text's statement that laughter of the imam at the conclusion invalidates, but leaving the mosque or speech after the conclusion does not. There is an ikhtilaf: the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogized hadath to leaving/speech, arguing since the imam's prayer is not invalidated by either, the follower's should not be either. Abu Hanifa distinguished: hadath nullifies the part of prayer it touches, so it corrupts the corresponding part in the follower's prayer. Since the follower needs to build on the imam's prayer, building on a null part is invalid. Taslim and speech are acts of exiting the prayer, not internal corruptions. The passage concludes with rulings on hadath during ruku' or sujud: one must perform wudu and rebuild, repeating the affected rakahs. This is agreed upon by Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, though their reasoning differs. A later quote from al-Nahr critiques Fath al-Qadir's view on the lahiq, noting that the masbuq khalifah's prayer is invalidated even if he is a lahiq, supporting al-Siraj.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer after the imam has already started, missing one or more rak'ahs.
حدث (hadath): A ritual impurity (minor) that nullifies wudu. In prayer, it invalidates the prayer if it occurs deliberately or inadvertently before completion.
منهي (munhi): An act that is considered by the Law as a remover of the tahrimah (prohibition of worldly acts) at the conclusion of prayer, such as taslim or exiting by the worshiper's own action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, why does the imam's hadath after the final sitting invalidate the masbuq's prayer, while the imam's speech or leaving does not?
A) Because hadath is a mufsid that corrupts the part of prayer it touches, and the masbuq must build on a valid part.
B) Because hadath is a major sin, unlike speech or leaving.
C) Because the masbuq is not considered a follower after the final sitting.
D) Because the imam's prayer becomes invalid, so the follower's must also be invalid.

Key Takeaway
The imam's hadath after the final sitting invalidates the masbuq's prayer (Abu Hanifa's relied-upon view) because hadath corrupts the part of prayer it touches, and building on a null part is invalid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Effect of Imam's Hadath on Masbuq and Lahiq
Commentary on ruling that masbuq's prayer is invalidated by imam's hadath after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the invalidation of the masbuq's prayer by the imam's hadath after tashahhud, distinguish the Sahibayn's opposing view, and explain the rationale behind each.

Core Idea
The masbuq's prayer is built on the imam's—so a hadath corrupts the foundation, invalidating the masbuq's prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq dives into a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: does the imam's hadath after the final tashahhud invalidate the masbuq's prayer? Abu Hanifa says yes because the masbuq builds on that part; the Sahibayn say no, analogizing to the imam's exit or speech. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals the school's method of qiyas and the unique role of 'building on a part' in Hanafi prayer theory.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
Identify the exact scenario: imam has hadath after the final tashahhud, and a masbuq is following. Abu Hanifa rules that the masbuq's prayer is invalidated.
The masbuq is one who missed one or more rak'ahs and must complete after the imam's salam.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view and their proof
The Sahibayn hold that the masbuq's prayer is not invalidated. Their evidence is qiyas to the imam's exit or speech, which do not invalidate the imam's prayer nor the follower's.
They argue consistency: if the imam's prayer remains valid, the follower's should too.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's distinguishing response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: hadath invalidates the specific part it encounters, whereas exit and speech do not corrupt a part. The masbuq needs to build on that part, and building on a corrupt part invalidates.
This is the key difference: the follower's need to 'build' (ibnā') on the imam's part.
4
Examine the lahiq's case and the two narrations
The text also discusses the lahiq (someone who slept and wakes up). There are two narrations: one invalidates his prayer (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj), another does not (al-Zahiriyya). The stronger view is invalidation.
The lahiq is considered like one behind the imam in estimation, but he still needs to build on the imam's completed prayer.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa, the masbuq must repeat his prayer if the imam has hadath after tashahhud; under the Sahibayn, he does not. The relied-upon position in the school is Abu Hanifa's view.
The exception: if the masbuq's separation (infirād) is established before the hadath, his prayer is not invalidated.

لدى اختتامه لا بخروجه من المسجد وكلامه ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده توضأ عامداً المسجد، ولذا قالوا: ولو تذكر الخليفة قائتة فسدت صلاة الإمام الأول والثاني والقوم، ولو تذكرها الأول بعد ما خرج من المسجد فسدت صلاته خاصة، أو قبل خروجه فسدت صلاته وصلاة الخليفة والقوم. وقالوا : لو صلى الإمام المحدث ما بقي من صلاته في منزله قبل فراغ هذا المستخلف تفسد صلاته لأن انفراده قبل فراغ الإمام لا يجوز قوله : (كما فسدت بقهقهة إمامه لدى اختتامه لا بخروجه من المسجد وكلامه أي كما تفسد صلاة المسبوق بحدث إمامه بعد القعود قدر التشهد ولا تفسد صلاة المسبوق بخروج إمامه من المسجد وكلامه بعد القعود ولا خلاف في الثاني وخالفا في الأول قياساً على الثاني لأن صلاة المقتدي مبنية على صلاة الإمام صحة وفساداً، ولم تفسد صلاة الإمام اتفاقاً في الكل فكذا المقتدي. وفرق الإمام بأن الحديث مفسد للجزء الذي يلاقيه من صلاة الإمام فيفسد مثله من صلاة المقتدي غير أن الإمام لا يحتاج إلى البناء والمسبوق محتاج إليه والبناء على الفاسد فاسد، بخلاف السلام لأنه منه والكلام في معناه ولهذا لا يخرج المقتدي منها بسلام الإمام وكلامه وخروجه فيسلم ويخرج بحدثه عمداً فلا يسلم بعده قيد بالمسبوق لأن صلاة المدرك لا تفسد اتفاقاً، وفي صلاة اللاحق روايتان، وصحح في السراج الوهاج الفساد، وصحح في الظهيرية عدمه معللاً بأن النائم كأنه خلف الإمام والإمام قد تمت صلاته فكذلك صلاة النائم تقديراً ! وفي نظر، لأن الإمام لم يبق عليه شيء بخلاف اللاحق، وفي فتح القدير: لو كان في القوم لاحق إن فعل الإمام ذلك بعد أن ما فاته قام يقضي وقيد بكونه عند اختتامه لأن الحدث العمد لو حصل قبل القعود بطلت صلاة الكل اتفاقاً . وقيد وافساد المسبوق عنده بما إذا لم يتأكد انفراده، فلو قام قبل سلامه تاركاً للواجب فقضى ركعة فسجد لها ثم فعل الإمام ذلك لا تفسد صلاته لأنه استحكم انفراده حتى لا يسجد لو سجد الإمام لسهو عليه ولا تفسد صلاته لو فسدت صلاة الإمام بعد سجوده
Upon its conclusion, not by his exiting the mosque nor his speech. And if he had an event in his bowing or prostrating, he performs ablution intentionally for the mosque. Hence they said: If the deputy imam remembers a missed prayer, the prayer of the first imam, the second, and the congregation is invalidated. If the first remembers after leaving the mosque, only his prayer is invalidated; if before exiting, his prayer, the deputy's, and the congregation's are invalidated. They said: If the imam who had an event prays the remainder of his prayer in his home before the completion of this substitute, his prayer is invalidated because his separation before the completion of the imam is not permissible. His statement: (Just as it is invalidated by the loud laughter of his imam upon its conclusion, not by his exiting the mosque nor his speech) meaning: just as the prayer of the masbuq is invalidated by the hadath of his imam after the sitting of tashahhud, and the prayer of the masbuq is not invalidated by the imam's exiting the mosque or his speech after the sitting. No disagreement in the second, but they differed in the first by analogy to the second because the prayer of the follower is built on the prayer of the imam in validity and invalidity. The imam's prayer is not invalidated by universal agreement, so too the follower. The Imam [Abu Hanifa] distinguished by saying that hadath invalidates the part it encounters from the imam's prayer, so it invalidates the equivalent from the follower's prayer, except that the imam does not need to build, whereas the masbuq needs to build, and building on invalid is invalid, unlike the salutation because it comes from him and speech is in its meaning; therefore the follower does not exit from it by the imam's salutation, speech, or exit. He [the masbuq] gives salutation and exits by his own intentional hadath, so he does not give salutation after it. He restricted [the ruling] to the masbuq because the prayer of the mudrik is not invalidated by agreement. And concerning the prayer of the lahiq, there are two narrations: in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj it is confirmed as invalidated, and in al-Zahiriyya its non-invalidation is confirmed, reasoned that the sleeper is as if behind the imam and the imam has completed his prayer, so too the sleeper's prayer is considered valid by estimation. However, there is a consideration because nothing remains upon the imam, unlike the lahiq. In Fath al-Qadir: If there is a lahiq among the congregation, if the imam does that after what he missed, he stands to make up. And he restricted it to being upon its conclusion because if the intentional hadath occurs before the sitting, the prayer of all is invalidated by agreement. And he restricted the invalidation of the masbuq according to him to when his separation is not confirmed. So if he stood before his salutation, leaving an obligatory act, and prayed a rak'ah and performed sajdah for it, then the imam does that, his prayer is not invalidated because his separation has become firmly established, to the extent that he does not perform sajdah if the imam performed sajdah for forgetfulness, and his prayer is not invalidated if the imam's prayer is invalidated after his sajdah.
Source pages p. 667

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of the imam's hadath (ritual impurity) on the followers after the final tashahhud. The matn states that the masbuq's prayer is invalidated by the imam's hadath (after the sitting of tashahhud) but not by the imam exiting the mosque or speaking. The commentator explains that there is no disagreement on the second part (exit and speech), but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) opposed Abu Hanifa on the first part. The Sahibayn's evidence is qiyas (analogy) to the cases of exit and speech: since the imam's prayer is not invalidated by those, and the follower's prayer is built on the imam's, it should not be invalidated. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: hadath invalidates the part of the imam's prayer that it encounters, and since the masbuq needs to build on that part, building on a corrupted part corrupts his own prayer. In contrast, salam and speech are from the imam and do not corrupt the part being built upon. The passage also discusses the lahiq (one who sleeps during prayer) where two narrations exist. The preferred position in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is invalidation; in al-Zahiriyya, non-invalidation is preferred. Fath al-Qadir is cited for additional details. The bottom line: The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the masbuq's prayer is invalidated by the imam's hadath after the final tashahhud, and the lahiq's prayer is also invalidated according to the stronger view.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): The person who joins the prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs, thus has to complete his prayer after the imam salutes.
اللاحق (al-lahiq): The person who sleeps during prayer and then wakes up and follows the imam; his position is considered similar to being behind the imam in estimation.
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud laughter that disrupts the prayer and invalidates it, used here as an analogy for something that invalidates the imam's prayer at its conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what invalidates the masbuq's prayer if it occurs after the final tashahhud?
A) The imam's exiting the mosque
B) The imam's speaking after tashahhud
C) The imam's hadath after tashahhud
D) The imam's loud laughter before tashahhud

Key Takeaway
The masbuq's prayer is like a building on the imam's foundation—when the foundation (imam's part) is corrupted by hadath, the building falls.

Hadath in Ruku or Sujud: Repetition and Completion Types
Commentary on ruling with intra-Hanafi reasoning and completion types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for hadath in ruku/sujud and explain the two types of completion (tamam al-mahiyya vs. tamam mukhrij an al-uhdah) that underlie the ruling.

Core Idea
Hadath in ruku or sujud requires repeating those positions because completion requires purity throughout the pillar.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a crucial point: if a person experiences hadath (ritual impurity) while in ruku or sujud, they do not have to repeat the entire prayer. Instead, they make wudu, build upon what was valid, and repeat only those affected positions. The commentator unpacks the reasoning behind this, including different explanations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and introduces a key distinction between completion of essence and completion that fully discharges liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
State the scenario (hadath in ruku/sujud) and the required actions: perform wudu, build (continue from where you left off), and repeat the ruku and sujud.
2
Understand the Reasoning of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf
Muhammad's view: the pillar is not completed at all without purity. Abu Yusuf's view: the prostration is completed by placing, but the sitting between prostrations and the transition require purity; those are not valid without purity.
Both agree on the outcome: repetition is required.
3
Grasp the Distinction Between Two Types of Completion
Completion of essence (tamam al-mahiyya) means the physical action is performed. Completion that exits from liability (tamam mukhrij an al-uhdah) means the act fulfills the obligation. The sajdah under hadath is complete in essence but not in a way that discharges the duty.
This distinction explains why repetition is necessary.
4
Apply the Ruling for an Imam
If the imam has hadath, he appoints a substitute. The substitute does not repeat the ruku/sujud because he can complete by persistence (istidamah) on the original imam's action.
5
Note the Condition About Raising the Head
If the imam raised his head intending performance of a pillar (e.g., saying 'Sami'a Allah' intending to complete ruku), then the prayer is invalid. If he did not intend performance, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
This condition prevents misuse of the 'building' rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده توضأ وبنى وأعادهما) لأن إتمام الركن بالانتقال الحدث لا يتحقق فلا بد من الإعادة أما على قول محمد فظاهر وأما عند أبي يوسف فالسجدة وإن تمت بالوضع لكن الجلسة بين السجدتين فرض عنده ولا تتحقق هي بغير طهارة والانتقال من ركن إلى ركن فرض بالإجماع. وذكر المصنف في الكافي أن التمام على نوعين : تمام ماهية و تمام مخرج عن العهدة، فالسجدة وإن تمت بالوضع ماهية لم تتم تماماً مخرجاً عن العهدة ا هـ . والإعادة هنا على سبيل الفرض وهي مجاز عن الأداء لأنهما لم يصحا، فلذا لو لم يعد فسدت صلاته. ولو كان إماماً فقدم غيره ودام المقدم على ركوعه وسجوده لأنه يمكنه الاتمام بالاستدامة عليه، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية : ولو أحدث الإمام في الركوع فقدم غيره فالخليفة لا يعيد الركوع ويتم كذلك ذكره شمس الأئمة السرخسي . وقيد المصنف في الكافي بناءه بما إذا لم يرفع مريداً الأداء فلو سبقه الحدث في الركوع فرفع رأسه قائلاً سمع الله لمن حمده فسدت صلاته وصلاة القوم ولو رفع رأسه من السجود وقال الله أكبر مريداً به أداء ركن فسدت صلاة الكل، وإن لم يرد به أداء الركن ففيه روايتان عن أبي حنيفة ا هـ. وقد قدمناه .
His statement: (And if he has an event in his bowing or his prostration, he performs ablution and builds and repeats them) because the completion of the pillar through transition when there is hadath is not realized, so repetition is necessary. As for according to Muhammad, it is apparent; but according to Abu Yusuf, although the prostration is completed by placing, yet the sitting between the two prostrations is an obligatory act according to him, and it is not realized without purity, and the transition from one pillar to another is obligatory by consensus. The author mentioned in al-Kafi that completion is of two types: completion of essence and completion that exits from liability. So although the prostration is completed by placing in terms of essence, it is not completed in a way that exits from liability. So repetition is on the basis of obligatory, and it is a metaphor for performance because they did not become valid. Hence if he does not repeat, his prayer is invalidated. And if he is an imam, he appoints another, and the one appointed continues upon his bowing and prostration because he can complete by persistence upon it. For this reason it is said in al-Zahiriyya: If the imam has an event in bowing and appoints another, the deputy does not repeat the bowing and completes like that, as stated by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. And the author in al-Kafi restricted his building upon condition that he did not raise intending performance; if hadath preceded him in bowing and he raised his head saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', his prayer and the congregation's prayer are invalidated. And if he raised his head from prostration and said 'Allahu Akbar' intending by it performance of a pillar, the prayer of all is invalidated. And if he did not intend performance of a pillar, then there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. We have already presented this.
Source pages p. 667

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and reasoning for one who experiences hadath (ritual impurity) while in ruku or sujud. The matn (from Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that such a person should make wudu, build upon what he has already done, and repeat those positions (ruku and sujud). The commentator (of al-Bahr al-Raiq) explains that the reason is that the completion of a pillar (rukn) requires passing through it with purity. Hadath prevents a valid transition to the next pillar, so the bowing or prostration was not properly completed. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: according to Muhammad, this is clear because the pillar is not completed without purity. According to Abu Yusuf, although the sajdah is completed by placing, the sitting between the two prostrations is obligatory and requires purity, and the transition from one pillar to another is also obligatory. The author of al-Kafi distinguishes two types of completion: completion of essence and completion that exonerates from liability. The sajdah may be complete in essence but not in a way that fulfills the obligation. Therefore repetition is obligatory. If the person who had hadath was the imam, he may appoint a substitute. The substitute does not need to repeat the ruku/sujud because he can complete the prayer by continuing upon them. There is also a condition: if the imam raised his head intending performance, then the prayer is invalidated; if not, there are two narrations.

Key Terms
تمام الماهية (tamam al-mahiyyah): Completion of the essence of an act, e.g., placing the forehead for sajdah, but not necessarily fulfilling the obligation properly.
تمام مخرج عن العهدة (tamam mukhrij 'an al-'uhdah): Completion that fully discharges one's obligation, requiring all conditions and integrals to be validly performed.
الاستدامة (al-istidamah): Persistence upon an action; here, the substitute imam can continue the prayer by persisting on the bowing and prostration of the original imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has hadath in ruku, after making wudu he must:
A) Repeat the entire prayer from the beginning
B) Build upon his prayer and repeat only the ruku and sujud
C) Continue without repeating anything
D) Repeat only the ruku

Key Takeaway
Hadath in ruku or sujud necessitates repeating those positions after wudu because completion of the pillar requires purity; the prayer is not entirely invalidated but the affected parts must be redone.

Remembering a Missed Sajdah During Ruku or Sujud: The Hanafi Ruling
Commentary on ruling that if one remembers a missed sajdah during ruku/sujud and performs it, he need not repeat the ruku/sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether to repeat ruku/sujud when a missed sajdah is remembered during them, and explain the basis that sequence is not a condition for repetitive actions.

Core Idea
Sequence is not a condition in prayer's repetitive acts; a missed sajdah remembered in ruku/sujud need not be compensated by repeating those acts.

In the flow of prayer, lapses happen. If you forget a sajdah and remember it while already in ruku or sujud, what should you do? The Hanafi school provides a clear, merciful ruling: you perform the missed sajdah immediately and continue, without needing to redo the ruku or sujud you were in. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this lenient ruling and addresses related nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Situation
Understand the exact scenario: a person is in ruku or sujud of a rak'ah and realizes that they missed a sajdah from a previous part of the prayer. What should they do according to Hanafi fiqh?
Note that this applies to both obligatory and tilawa sajdahs.
2
State the Ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq
The matn says: 'لم يعدهما' – he does not repeat the ruku and sujud. This is the relied-upon position. The prayer is valid without repetition.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The rationale is that sequence (tartib) is not a condition for validity in actions that are legislated repetitively, such as sajdah and ruku within a rak'ah. Therefore, missing the sequence due to forgetfulness does not require undoing the later act.
This principle is derived from the nature of prayer.
4
Reconcile with Al-Wafi's View
Al-Wafi suggests that repetition is preferable (afdal) to achieve sequence as much as possible. The commentator reconciles by stating that the matn indicates non-necessity, while al-Wafi indicates preference. There is no contradiction.
The mufta bihi is the non-necessity position.
5
Identify the Exception
If the missed sajdah is a structural sajdah remembered in the final sitting, or if one remembers a missed surah recitation while in ruku, sequence is required and the current act is disrupted. This shows the principle is specific to repetitive acts.
This exception is noted in Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو ذكر راكعاً أو ساجداً سجدة فسجدها لم يعدهما) لأن الانتقال مع شرط وقد وجد لأن الترتيب ليس بشرط فيما شرع مكرراً من أفعال الصلاة. وذكر المصنف في الوافي في هذه المسألة أنه يعيدهما ولا تناقض لأن ما في الكنز لبيان عدم اللزوم، وما في أصله لبيان الأفضل لتقع الأفعال مرتبة بالقدر الممكن وكان ينبغي أن تكون إعادتهما واجبة لأن الترتيب المذكور واجب. قال المصنف في الكافي ولئن كان الترتيب واجباً فقد سقط بعذر النسيان. وتبعه المحقق في فتح القدير وفيه نظر لأن الترتيب الساقط بعذر النسيان إنما هو ترتيب الفوائت وأما لواجب في الصلاة إذا تركه ناسياً فإن حكمه السهو. وجوابه أنهم لم يمنعوا وجوب سجود السهو وإنما الكلام في إعادته لأجل تركه الترتيب، فالمعلل له عدم لزوم الإعادة لا عدم وجوب السجود أطلق في السجدة فشملت الصلاتية والتلاوية، وقيد بالتذكر في الركوع والسجود لأنه لو تذكر سجدة صلبية في القعود الأخير فسجدها أو تذكر في الركوع أنه لم يقرأ السورة فعاد لقراءتها ارتفض ما كان فيه لأن الترتيب فيه فرض كما أسلفناه في صفة الصلاة، وفي فتح القدير: له أن يقضي المتروكة عقب التذكر وله أن يؤخرها إلى آخر الصلاة فيقضيها هناك اهـ . وبما ذكر هنا ظهر ضعف ما في فتاوى قاضيخان من أن الإمام لو صلى ركعة وترك منها سجدة وصلى أخرى وسجد لها فتذكر المتروكة في السجود أنه يرفع رأسه من السجود ويسجد المتروكه ثم يعيد ما، السجدة
His statement: (And if he remembers a sajdah while bowing or prostrating and performs it, he does not repeat them) because the transition is with a condition and it has been found, because sequence is not a condition in what is legislated repetitively from the actions of prayer. And the author mentioned in al-Wafi in this issue that he repeats them, and there is no contradiction because what is in al-Kanz is to explain non-necessity, and what is in its source is to explain the preferable, so that actions occur in sequence as much as possible. And it would be appropriate that their repetition be obligatory because the mentioned sequence is obligatory. The author said in al-Kafi: Even if the sequence is obligatory, it is waived due to the excuse of forgetfulness. And the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir followed him, but there is consideration because the sequence waived due to forgetfulness is only the sequence of missed prayers. As for an obligatory act during prayer that is left forgetfully, its ruling is forgetfulness prostration. The answer is that they did not deny the obligation of prostration of forgetfulness; the discussion is about repeating it due to leaving the sequence. So what is given as a reason is the non-necessity of repetition, not the non-obligation of prostration. He uses the general word 'sajdah' which includes both prayer sajdah and recitation sajdah. And he restricted it to remembering during bowing and prostration because if he remembers a structural sajdah in the final sitting and performs it, or remembers while bowing that he did not recite the surah and returns to recite it, what he was in is disrupted because the sequence is obligatory there, as we have explained in the description of prayer. In Fath al-Qadir: He may make up the missed sajdah immediately after remembering or delay it until the end of the prayer and make it up there. And by what is mentioned here, the weakness of what is in Fatawa Qadikhan becomes apparent, namely that if the imam prays a rak'ah and leaves out a sajdah and prays another rak'ah and prostrates for it, then remembers the missed sajdah in prostration, that he should raise his head from the prostration and prostrate the missed one, then repeat what, the sajdah.
Source pages p. 668

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on remembering a missed obligatory sajdah while in the middle of a rak'ah (in ruku or sujud). The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that if a person remembers a missed sajdah while he is already in ruku or sujud, and he performs that sajdah, he does not need to repeat the ruku or sujud he was in. The commentator explains that this is because the actions of prayer are repetitive, and sequence (tarteeb) is not a condition for such repetitive actions. There is a differing view from al-Wafi that suggests he should repeat them, but the commentator reconciles by saying that the matn indicates non-necessity, while the other view indicates the preferable option (to have actions in sequence). The author of al-Kafi argues that even if sequence is obligatory, it is waived due to the excuse of forgetfulness. The text from Fath al-Qadir adds nuance: the sequence that is waived is only for missed prayers, not for obligatory acts within the prayer; if an obligatory act is left forgetfully, the compensation is prostration of forgetfulness. So the discussion is about the necessity of repetition, not about the obligation of sujud al-sahw. The last part criticizes a fatwa from Qadikhan that would require the imam to raise his head from prostration to prostrate the missed sajdah, which contradicts the principle that sequence is not a condition in this context.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Sequence of prayer actions; here, it is considered not a condition for validity in repetitive acts like sajdah and ruku.
السجدة الصلاتية (al-sajdah al-salawiyyah): A sajdah that is part of the prayer structure, as opposed to a tilawa sajdah (recitation prostration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person remembers a missed sajdah while in ruku, what is the ruling according to Kanz al-Daqa'iq?
A) He must repeat the ruku and sujud.
B) He does not need to repeat the ruku and sujud.
C) His prayer is invalidated.
D) He must perform sujud al-sahw instead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sequence is not a condition for repetitive prayer actions, so a missed sajdah remembered in ruku or sujud does not require repeating those acts; the prayer remains valid.

Condition for Transferring to Another Imam
Commentary on condition for transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a follower to transfer to another imam and apply it to scenarios involving the original imam's exit from the mosque.

Core Idea
A follower cannot transfer from the original imam unless that imam has physically exited the mosque.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key condition for the validity of transferring from one imam to another. It explains that the original imam's authority remains intact as long as he is within the mosque, even if he performs wudu. The ruling hinges on the imam's presence or absence from the place of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'She does not turn away from him' – meaning the follower does not transfer from the original imam.
This is the default rule.
2
Identify the exception
The ruling is restricted to when the imam has exited the mosque. If he has not exited, the follower remains with him.
The exception is when the imam physically leaves the mosque building.
3
Understand the rationale
The imam's imamate continues as long as he is in the mosque. Even if he performs wudu in the mosque and returns, his imamate is valid.
Exit from the mosque terminates the imam's leadership for that prayer.
4
Apply to a scenario
If the imam leaves to perform wudu but stays inside the mosque, he can return and continue; the follower cannot transfer.
Only exit from the mosque allows transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لم تتحول عنه أي لعدم صلاحية المؤتم لها . قال في النهر ولا بد أن يقيد هذا بما إذا خرج الإمام من المسجد لما مر من أنه إذا لم يخرج فهو على إمامته حتى لو توضأ في المسجد وعاد إلى مكانه صح والله أعلم.
His statement: (She does not turn away from him) meaning because the follower is not eligible for her. He said in al-Nahr: It must be restricted to when the imam has exited the mosque, because it has been mentioned that if he does not exit, he remains in his imamate, so that even if he performs wudu in the mosque and returns to his place, it is valid. Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 668

Commentary
This is a brief commentary on the phrase 'lam tahawwal 'anhu' from the matn. The commentator explains that the follower does not transfer from the original imam to another unless the original imam has physically exited the mosque. The reason is that as long as the imam remains in the mosque, he retains his imamate. Even if he had to perform wudu (due to hadath) and returns to his spot, his imamate is valid and the follower cannot transfer to someone else. This ruling underscores the principle that the imam's authority persists until he leaves the place of prayer.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The follower in prayer; the one who is led by the imam.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): Appointment of a substitute imam when the original imam becomes unable to continue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the imam performs wudu in the mosque
B) When the imam exits the mosque
C) When the imam speaks after prayer
D) When the imam sits for tashahhud

Key Takeaway
A follower cannot transfer from his imam unless that imam has physically exited the mosque; mere wudu or leaving the prayer line does not suffice.

Remembering a Missed Sajdah in Ruku' or Sujud: Hanafi Ruling
Hanafi ruling on missed sajdah with proof and intra-madhhab analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a missed sajdah is remembered during ruku' or sujud and explain the underlying reasoning regarding tartib (order).

Core Idea
A missed sajdah remembered in ruku' or sujud does not require repeating those actions; order is not a condition in repeated acts.

In the prayer, actions like ruku' and sujud are repeated across rak'ahs. Hanafi scholars have debated whether strict sequential order is required when a missed sajdah is discovered in the middle of another action. This commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the mufta bihi position: the prayer remains valid, and no obligatory repetition is necessary, though repeating is recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage addresses a worshipper who remembers a missed sajdah while in ruku' or sujud. He performs it immediately. The ruling states he does not have to repeat the ruku' or sujud he was in.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof given is: 'because the transition occurred with its condition fulfilled, as order is not a condition in actions that are legislated as repeated in the prayer.' The key phrase: الترتيب ليس بشرط فيما شرع مكرراً من أفعال الصلاة.
This is a talil (rationale) based on the nature of repeated actions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Understand why order is not a condition: Actions like sujud are repeated multiple times; requiring strict order would cause undue burden. The transition from the missed sajdah to the next action (e.g., ruku') is considered fulfilled because the sajdah itself is a valid act.
This distinguishes from non-repeated actions where order is obligatory.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The author of al-Wafi held that the subsequent actions must be repeated to maintain order. However, al-Kafi and Kanz al-Daqaiq adopt the view that no repetition is required. The author reconciles: Kanz indicates no obligation, while al-Wafi indicates recommendation (mustahabb).
The ikhtilaf is about whether repetition is wajib or mustahabb.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) sides with al-Kafi and Kanz, deeming the prayer valid and repetition recommended. He also refutes Qadikhan's fatwa that invalidates the subsequent actions.
Mufta bihi: No repetition required; if repeated, it is mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو ذكر راكعاً أو ساجداً سجدة فسجدها لم يعدهما) لأن الانتقال مع شرط وقد وجد لأن الترتيب ليس بشرط فيما شرع مكرراً من أفعال الصلاة. وذكر المصنف في الوافي في هذه المسألة أنه يعيدهما ولا تناقض لأن ما في الكنز لبيان عدم اللزوم، وما في أصله لبيان الأفضل لتقع الأفعال مرتبة بالقدر الممكن وكان ينبغي أن تكون إعادتهما واجبة لأن الترتيب المذكور واجب. قال المصنف في الكافي ولئن كان الترتيب واجباً فقد سقط بعذر النسيان. وتبعه المحقق في فتح القدير وفيه نظر لأن الترتيب الساقط بعذر النسيان إنما هو ترتيب الفوائت وأما لواجب في الصلاة إذا تركه ناسياً فإن حكمه السهو. وجوابه أنهم لم يمنعوا وجوب سجود السهو وإنما الكلام في إعادته لأجل تركه الترتيب، فالمعلل له عدم لزوم الإعادة لا عدم وجوب السجود أطلق في السجدة فشملت الصلاتية والتلاوية، وقيد بالتذكر في الركوع والسجود لأنه لو تذكر سجدة صلبية في القعود الأخير فسجدها أو تذكر في الركوع أنه لم يقرأ السورة فعاد لقراءتها ارتفض ما كان فيه لأن الترتيب فيه فرض كما أسلفناه في صفة الصلاة، وفي فتح القدير: له أن يقضي المتروكة عقب التذكر وله أن يؤخرها إلى آخر الصلاة فيقضيها هناك اهـ . وبما ذكر هنا ظهر ضعف ما في فتاوى قاضيخان من أن الإمام لو صلى ركعة وترك منها سجدة وصلى أخرى وسجد لها فتذكر المتروكة في السجود أنه يرفع رأسه من السجود ويسجد المتروكه ثم يعيد ما كان فيها لأنها ارتفضت فيعيدها استحساناً ا.هـ. فإنك قد علمت أنها لا ترتفض وأن الإعادة مستحبة، ومقتضى الارتفاض افتراض الإعادة وهو مقتض لافتراض الترتيب وقد اتفقوا على وجوبه
His saying: (And if he remembers, while bowing or prostrating, a prostration and performs it, he does not repeat them) because the transition (to the next action) occurred with its condition fulfilled, due to the fact that order is not a condition in actions of the prayer that are legislated as repeated. The author mentioned in al-Wafi regarding this issue that he does repeat them, and there is no contradiction because what is in al-Kanz indicates the absence of necessity, and what is in its source indicates the preferred (action) so that the actions occur in order as much as possible, and it would have been appropriate that their repetition be obligatory because the mentioned order is obligatory. The author said in al-Kafi: Even if the order is obligatory, it has fallen due to the excuse of forgetfulness. And the verifier in Fath al-Qadir followed him, but there is a consideration: the order that falls due to forgetfulness is only the order of missed actions, but for an obligatory element in the prayer that one forgets, its ruling is the forgetfulness prostration. The answer is that they did not deny the obligation of the forgetfulness prostration; rather, the discussion is about repeating it due to leaving the order, so what is inferred is the lack of necessity of repetition, not the lack of obligation of the prostration. He spoke absolutely about the prostration, so it includes both the prayer prostration and the recital prostration, and he restricted it to remembering in bowing and prostrating because if he remembers a core prostration in the final sitting and performs it, or remembers in bowing that he did not recite the surah and returns to recite it, what he was in becomes invalidated because order is obligatory in it, as we have mentioned earlier in the description of the prayer. In Fath al-Qadir: He may perform the missed one immediately after remembering, or he may delay it to the end of the prayer and perform it there. By what is mentioned here, the weakness of what is in the Fatawa of Qadikhan becomes apparent: that if the imam prays a rak'ah and misses a prostration from it, and prays another and prostrates for it, and then remembers the missed one while in prostration, he should raise his head from the prostration and perform the missed one, then repeat what he was in because it was invalidated. He repeats it by istihsan. End. You have known that it is not invalidated and that repetition is recommended, and the implication of invalidation is requiring repetition, and it implies requiring the order, and they have agreed upon its obligation.
Source pages p. 668

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling with proof) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It discusses the situation where a person remembers a missed sajdah (prostration) while they are in the state of ruku' (bowing) or sujud (prostration) during prayer. The author explains that if the person remembers and performs that missed sajdah, they do not need to repeat the ruku' or sujud they were in, because the transition to that action (i.e., moving from the sajdah they performed to the next ruku' or sujud) occurred with its condition fulfilled. The reasoning is that tartib (order) is not a condition in actions that are inherently repeated in the prayer, such as multiple prostrations. There is a difference of opinion: the author of al-Wafi stated that the person should repeat the ruku' or sujud, but the author of al-Kanz (the matn) indicates no repetition is necessary. The author of al-Kafi reconciles by saying that although order is obligatory, it is waived due to the excuse of forgetfulness. The commentator refutes a fatwa from Qadikhan which suggested that the later actions are invalidated and must be repeated. The correct view is that the actions are not invalidated, and if one chooses to repeat them, it is merely recommended (mustahabb) and not obligatory. The passage also clarifies that if the missed sajdah is a core prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) of the prayer and is remembered in the final sitting, it should be performed then, and if remembered during ruku' that one did not recite the surah, one must return and recite, which invalidates the ruku' because order in recitation is obligatory. The key lesson is that the prayer remains valid, and no obligatory repetition is required.

Key Terms
سجدة (sajdah): Prostration; here refers to a missed sajdah from the prayer or tilawah.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The required sequence of actions in prayer.
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repetition; here, repeating the ruku' or sujud that followed the missed sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person remembers a missed sajdah while in ruku' and performs it, what is the ruling regarding the ruku' he was in?
A) He must repeat the ruku'
B) He does not need to repeat the ruku'
C) He must also perform an additional sajdah
D) His prayer becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
A missed sajdah remembered during ruku' or sujud does not require repeating those actions; the prayer remains valid, and repetition is only recommended.

Automatic Appointment of Single Follower as Substitute Imam
Commentary on automatic istikhlaf with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on automatic istikhlaf for a single follower and explain why the follower's prayer is invalid when unfit, while the imam's remains valid.

Core Idea
A single follower is automatically designated as substitute imam without intention; if unfit for imamate, only the follower's prayer is invalid.

In congregational prayer, continuity is vital. If the imam becomes invalid (e.g., hadath), a single follower is automatically designated as substitute. But what if that follower is unsuitable? The Hanafi school has nuanced views. This lesson clarifies the conditions and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the automatic designation of a single follower as substitute imam (istikhlaf) without requiring intention. The ruling is that this designation occurs automatically for a single follower, but its effect depends on the follower's suitability.
2
Note the condition: imam must leave the mosque
The imam's imamate only ceases if he leaves the mosque (e.g., due to hadath). If he remains inside, he continues as imam, and the follower's automatic designation does not take effect.
This condition is critical—if the imam does not leave, the follower remains a follower and the original imam leads.
3
Identify categories of followers (fit vs. unfit)
The text mentions followers fit for imamate (e.g., free male) and those unfit (woman, child, hermaphrodite, illiterate, mute, etc.). The automatic designation applies absolutely, but the ruling differs for unfit followers.
4
Trace the three intra-Hanafi opinions
When an unfit follower is automatically designated: (1) some say only the imam's prayer is invalid, (2) some say both are invalid, (3) the relied-upon view (asahh) is that only the follower's prayer is invalid because the imam remains imam and the follower has no valid imam.
The ikhtilaf is only when no intentional substitution occurs; if the imam appoints someone, all agree the imam's prayer is invalid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The most correct view, endorsed by al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan, is that the follower's prayer is fasid (invalid) while the imam's prayer is sahih (valid). This is the operative position for fatwa.
The imam can continue his prayer, but the follower must repeat his prayer later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لم تتحول عنه) أي لعدم صلاحية المؤتم لها . قال في النهر ولا بد أن يقيد هذا بما إذا خرج الإمام من المسجد لما مر من أنه إذا لم يخرج فهو على إمامته حتى لو توضأ في المسجد وعاد إلى مكانه صح والله أعلم. قوله: (ويتعين المأموم الواحد للاستخلاف بلا نية) لما فيه من صيانة الصلاة، وتعيين الأول لقطع المزاحمة ولا مزاحم وصار الإمام مؤتماً إذا خرج من المسجد، وإن لم يخرج من المسجد فهو على إمامته حتى يجوز الاقتداء به، وكذا لو توضأ في المسجد يستمر على إمامته، أطلق في المأموم فشمل من يصلح للإمامة ومن لا يصلح مثل المرأة والصبي والخنثى والأمي والأخرس والمتنقل خلف المفترض والمقيم خلف المسافر في القضاء ففيه ثلاثة أقوال : قيل بفساد صلاة الإمام خاصة ، وقيل بفساد صلاتهما والأصح فساد صلاة المقتدي دون الإمام كما في المحيط وغاية البيان لأن الإمامة لم تتحول عنه فبقي إماماً وبقي المقتدي بلا إمام له فحينئذ لم يتعين للإمامة، فإطلاق المختصر منصرف لمن يصلح للإمامة، ومحل الاختلاف عند عدم الاستخلاف وإما إذا استخلفه فأجمعوا على بطلان صلاة الإمام المستخلف. وقيد بكون المأموم واحد لأنه لو كان متعدداً فلا يتعين إلا بتعيين الإمام أو القوم أو يتعين هو بالتقدم ويقتدي به لعدم الأولوية كما قدمناه. وفي التنجيس : رجل أم رجلاً واحداً فأحدثا جميعاً وخرجا جميعاً من المسجد، فصلاة الإمام تامة لأنه منفرد يبني على صلاته وصلاة المقتدي فاسدة لأنه مقتد ليس له إمام في المسجد ا هـ . والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
His saying: (He does not turn away from him) meaning due to the follower's lack of suitability for leadership. He said in al-Nahr: This must be qualified by when the imam leaves the mosque, based on what has passed that if he does not leave, he remains in his imamate such that even if he performs wudu in the mosque and returns to his place, it is valid, and Allah knows best. His saying: (And the single follower is designated for substitution without intention) because of preserving the prayer, and designating the first one to remove competition, and there is no competitor. The imam becomes a follower if he leaves the mosque, but if he does not leave the mosque, he remains in his imamate such that it is permissible to follow him, and likewise if he performs wudu in the mosque, his imamate continues. He spoke absolutely about the follower, so it includes those fit for imamate and those not, such as a woman, child, hermaphrodite, illiterate, mute, and one performing supererogatory prayer behind one performing obligatory prayer, and a resident behind a traveler in making up prayers. Regarding this, there are three opinions: Some say the prayer of the imam alone is invalid; some say both are invalid; the most correct is that the prayer of the follower is invalid, not the imam, as in al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan, because the imamate did not transfer from him, so he remains imam, and the follower remains without an imam; therefore he is not designated for imamate. Thus, the absolute statement of the abridger is directed to one fit for imamate, and the place of difference is when there is no substitution; but if he appoints him, they unanimously agree on the invalidity of the prayer of the imam who appointed. He restricted it to the follower being one because if there are multiple, he is not designated except by the imam's designation or the people's, or he designates himself by stepping forward and they follow him due to lack of priority, as we have mentioned. In al-Tanjis: A man led one man, both broke their wudu, and both left the mosque. The prayer of the imam is complete because he is alone and builds on his prayer, but the prayer of the follower is invalid because he is a follower with no imam in the mosque. End. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best.
Source pages p. 668

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling with proof) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It addresses the rule that a single follower (ma'mum wahid) is automatically designated as the substitute imam (khalifah) when the imam becomes invalid, and this does not require intention (niyyah). The reason is to preserve the prayer's continuity and avoid competition. The key condition is that the imam must have left the mosque (e.g., due to hadath) for his imamate to cease; if he remains inside, he continues as imam. The passage then discusses the suitability of the follower. The absolute statement 'single follower' includes those fit and unfit for imamate, such as women, children, hermaphrodites, illiterate, mutes, and those in certain mixed prayer situations (supererogatory behind obligatory, resident behind traveler in qada). For these unfit followers, there are three opinions: some say only the imam's prayer is invalid, some say both are invalid, but the correct (sahih) view is that only the follower's prayer is invalid because the imam remains imam and the follower has no imam. This applies when no substitution occurs; if the imam appoints someone, all agree the imam's prayer is invalid. The restriction to a single follower is because if there are multiple followers, automatic designation does not occur without specific appointment. The passage ends with a case from al-Tanjis: if both the imam and the follower break wudu and leave the mosque, the imam's prayer is valid as he is now alone, but the follower's prayer is invalid.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaaf): Appointing a substitute imam when the original imam becomes unable to continue the prayer.
المأموم الواحد (al-ma'mum al-wahid): The single follower who is automatically designated as substitute imam without intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The imam must make intention to appoint the follower.
B) The follower must be fit for imamate.
C) The imam must leave the mosque.
D) The follower must step forward.

Key Takeaway
A single follower is automatically the substitute imam without intention, but only the follower's prayer is invalid if he is unfit; the imam's prayer remains valid.

Ruling for a single muqtadi appointed as substitute imam and the effect of hadath and exiting the masjid
Commentary expanding on the ruling of istikhlaf for a single muqtadi and three opinions on prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of prayers when a single muqtadi is unfit for imamate and the imam has hadath without substitution, and explain the tarjih among the three opinions.

Core Idea
A single muqtadi automatically becomes substitute imam, but if both have hadath and exit, only the muqtadi's prayer is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the matn rule that a single follower is automatically designated for istikhlaf (substitution). The commentator clarifies that this applies only when the follower is fit to lead, otherwise a dispute arises. Three Hanafi opinions on prayer validity are presented, and the relied-upon view is that only the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid while the imam's remains valid because he becomes munfarid and builds on his prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the base rule
The matn states that a single muqtadi is designated for istikhlaf automatically without intention, to preserve the prayer. This is the default when there is only one follower.
This applies regardless of the muqtadi's fitness for imamate in the absolute sense, but is later interpreted restrictively.
2
Identify the condition of fitness
The commentator notes that the absolute term 'muqtadi' includes those unfit for imamate (woman, boy, etc.). This triggers the dispute when no substitution occurs.
The dispute arises precisely because an unfit muqtadi cannot validly assume imamate.
3
Outline the three opinions
Three sayings: (1) Only imam's prayer invalid; (2) Both prayers invalid; (3) Only muqtadi's invalid (the soundest, al-sahih).
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; no cross-madhhab mention.
4
Understand the evidence for the relied-upon view
The imamate did not transfer from the imam, so he remains imam and his prayer is valid. The muqtadi is left without an imam, so his prayer is invalid.
This is supported by al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan.
5
Apply to the case in al-Tanjis
A man leads one man, both have hadath and exit the masjid. The imam's prayer is complete (he builds as munfarid), the follower's prayer is invalid.
This is the practical application of the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويتعين المأموم الواحد للاستخلاف بلا نية لما فيه من صيانة الصلاة، وتعيين الأول لقطع المزاحمة ولا مزاحم وصار الإمام مؤتماً إذا خرج من المسجد، وإن لم يخرج من المسجد فهو على إمامته حتى يجوز الاقتداء به، وكذا لو توضأ في المسجد يستمر على إمامته، أطلق في المأموم فشمل من يصلح للإمامة ومن لا يصلح مثل المرأة والصبي والخنثى والأمي والأخرس والمتنقل خلف المفترض والمقيم خلف المسافر في القضاء ففيه ثلاثة أقوال : قيل بفساد صلاة الإمام خاصة ، وقيل بفساد صلاتهما والأصح فساد صلاة المقتدي دون الإمام كما في المحيط وغاية البيان لأن الإمامة لم تتحول عنه فبقي إماماً وبقي المقتدي بلا إمام له فحينئذ لم يتعين للإمامة، فإطلاق المختصر منصرف لمن يصلح للإمامة، ومحل الاختلاف عند عدم الاستخلاف وإما إذا استخلفه فأجمعوا على بطلان صلاة الإمام المستخلف. وقيد بكون المأموم واحد لأنه لو كان متعدداً فلا يتعين إلا بتعيين الإمام أو القوم أو يتعين هو بالتقدم ويقتدي به لعدم الأولوية كما قدمناه. وفي التنجيس : رجل أم رجلاً واحداً فأحدثا جميعاً وخرجا جميعاً من المسجد، فصلاة الإمام تامة لأنه منفرد يبني على صلاته وصلاة المقتدي فاسدة لأنه مقتد ليس له إمام في المسجد ا هـ . والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
His statement: (A single follower is designated for substitution without intention because of the preservation of the prayer, and the first is designated to cut off competition and there is no competitor. And the imam becomes a follower if he exits the masjid, but if he does not exit the masjid he remains in his imamate such that it is permissible to follow him. Likewise, if he performs wudu in the masjid he continues in his imamate. He gave an absolute statement regarding the follower, so it includes one fit for imamate and one not fit, such as a woman, a boy, a hermaphrodite, an illiterate person, a mute, one performing a supererogatory prayer behind one performing an obligatory prayer, and a resident performing a make-up prayer behind a traveler. Concerning this there are three sayings: some say the prayer of the imam alone is invalid; some say both prayers are invalid; and the soundest is that the prayer of the follower is invalid without the imam, as in al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan, because the imamate did not transfer from him, so he remains an imam, and the follower remains without an imam, so then he is not designated for imamate. Thus the absolute statement of the author is interpreted as referring to one fit for imamate. The place of disagreement is when no substitution occurs; but if he appoints him, there is consensus on the invalidity of the prayer of the imam who appointed a substitute. And he restricted it to a single follower because if there were many, then no one is designated except by the appointment of the imam or the congregation, or he designates himself by stepping forward and they follow him due to lack of priority, as we have presented. And in al-Tanjis: A man led a single man, then both had hadath and both exited the masjid; the prayer of the imam is complete because he is alone and builds on his prayer, while the prayer of the follower is invalid because he is a follower who has no imam in the masjid. End. And Allah the Exalted knows best.
Source pages p. 669

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Raiq, commenting on the matn phrase 'A single follower is designated for substitution' (ويتعين المأموم الواحد للاستخلاف). The commentator clarifies that when there is only one muqtadi, he automatically becomes the substitute imam without needing intention, to preserve the prayer. The first person (the original imam) is designated to avoid competition since no one else contests. If the imam exits the masjid (e.g., due to hadath), he ceases to be imam and becomes a follower of the substitute. If he remains in the masjid, his imamate continues and it's permissible to follow him. Similarly, if he performs wudu in the masjid, he stays imam. However, the author's absolute phrase 'follower' includes those unfit for imamate (woman, boy, hermaphrodite, illiterate, mute, etc.). This triggers a dispute among Hanafi scholars: some say only the imam's prayer is invalid, some say both are invalid, but the correct view (al-sahih) is that only the follower's prayer is invalid, not the imam's, because the imamate hasn't transferred. The imam remains imam, but the follower has no imam. Therefore, the text's absolute statement is understood as referring to followers fit for imamate. This disagreement applies only when no substitution occurs. If the imam appoints a substitute, there is consensus that the imam's prayer becomes invalid. The rule is restricted to a single follower because if there are multiple, no one is automatically designated unless the imam or congregation appoints, or one steps forward. Finally, al-Tanjis reports a case: if an imam leads one man, both have hadath and exit the masjid, the imam's prayer is valid (he prays alone and can build), but the follower's prayer is invalid because he has no imam in the masjid. This is a detailed intra-Hanafi legal discussion on the fine points of istikhlaf and hadath.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlāf): Appointing a substitute imam during prayer due to hadath or other reason.
المأموم الواحد (al-ma'mūm al-wāḥid): A single follower; if there is only one, he becomes automatically designated for istikhlaf.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, necessitating re-purification and potentially affecting imamate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, if an imam and his single muqtadi both have hadath and exit the masjid, what is the status of their prayers?
A) Both prayers are invalid.
B) Only the imam's prayer is invalid.
C) Only the muqtadi's prayer is invalid.
D) Both prayers are valid if they build.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a single muqtadi (especially one unfit for imamate) is with an imam and both experience hadath and exit the masjid without substitution, the soundest opinion is that only the muqtadi's prayer is invalid; the imam's prayer remains valid as he builds as munfarid.
